Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Returning from Extra Rak'ah Before Sajdah
Ruling on returning to qa'dah after forgetting and standing for extra rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person forgets the final sitting and stands for an extra rak'ah before performing its sajdah, and explain why sujud al-sahw becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Before prostrating an extra rak'ah, return to the final sitting; delay of a fard makes sujud al-sahw wajib.

Forgetfulness in prayer is common, and the Hanafi school provides clear guidance on how to correct it. This lesson examines a specific scenario: forgetting the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and standing up for an additional rak'ah. The ruling depends on whether the prostration (sajdah) of that extra rak'ah has been performed. We will focus on the case before sajdah, where the prayer can still be corrected by returning to the sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forgetfulness scenario
The person forgets the final sitting and stands for an extra rak'ah in a 4-rak'ah prayer (e.g., stands for a fifth), in Maghrib (fourth), or in Fajr (third). The key condition is that he has NOT yet performed the sajdah of that extra rak'ah.
If sajdah has been performed, the ruling differs (not covered in this lesson).
2
Understand the ruling: return to the sitting
The ruling is to return to the final sitting. This is because it is possible to abandon less than a full rak'ah, and returning to the correct sequence salvages the prayer.
Imam Quduri's statement about voiding the extra rak'ah is explained by this return.
3
Grasp the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: less than a rak'ah (i.e., without sajdah) is not considered a valid unit of prayer in reality or by legal ruling. This is evidenced by the example of an oath: if someone swears not to pray and then prays less than a rak'ah, he does not break his oath.
This shows that actions less than a rak'ah can be voided (laghw) without harm.
4
Apply the principle of laghw
When one returns from an action to something that precedes it in sequence, the action from which he returns becomes void (laghw). Here, the extra rak'ah becomes void because its place (the fifth rak'ah) is after the final sitting.
Analogous example: sitting for tashahhud then remembering missed sajdah – the sitting becomes void.
5
Conclude with wajib of sujud al-sahw
Having returned to the sitting, sujud al-sahw becomes wajib because there was a delay of an obligation – either the final sitting (fard) or the salam (wajib). This delay necessitates compensation via sujud al-sahw.
The text notes a subtlety: 'wajib' in al-Hidayah could refer to salam or to fard (final sitting).

Source Text

باب سجود السهو اور اگر قعد کا خیرہ سے سہو ہو گیا حتی کہ پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب ( پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا تو قعدہ کی انی لوٹ آئے کیونکہ اس میں اس کی نماز کی اصلاح کرتا ہے اور یہ اس کے لئے ممکن بھی ہے اس لئے کہ ایک رکعت سے کم کو چھوڑا جا سکتا امام قدوری نے کہا کہ پانچویں رکعت کو لغو کر دے کیونکہ وہ ایسی چیز کی طرف پھرا ہے جس کا محل پانچویں رکعت سے مقدم ہے پس یا چھوڑ دے اور سہو کا سجدہ کرے کیونکہ اس نے فرض کو مؤخر کر دیا ہے۔
ریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص قعدہ اخیرہ بھول گیا اور ربائی نماز میں پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا یا علاثی دلم از (مغرب دوتر) میں چوتھی رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا یا شائی میں تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب تک اس رکعت کو یعنی رباعی کی پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا تو قعدہ کی طرف لوٹ آئے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قعدہ کی طرف لوٹ آنے میں اس کی نماز کی صطلاح ہے اور اس کے لئے نماز کی اصلاح ممکن بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک رکعت سے کم کو چھوڑنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بہ رکعت سے کم نہ تو حقیقتہ نماز ہے اور نہ نماز کے حکم میں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں نماز نہیں پڑھوں گا پھر ایک ات سے کم پڑھی تو حانث نہیں ہوگا۔
مدة بائل پانچویں رکعت سے پہلے ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو شخص افعال صلوۃ میں سے کسی فعل سے ایسی چیز کی طرف لوٹا جس کا محل اس. پہلے ہے تو وہ فعل مرجوع عنہ (جس سے رجوع کیا گیا) لغو ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً کوئی شخص تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھا پھر یاد آیا کہ نماز کا سجدہ نہیں یا سجدہ تلاوت نہیں کیا پھر اس نے یہ فوت شدہ سجدہ کیا تو سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے کا قعدہ لغو ہو گیا ہے۔ کیو نہک سجدہ کامل قعدہ اخیرہ سے نرم ہے۔ بہر حال جب پانچویں رکعت چھوڑ کر قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹ آیا تو سجدہ سہو کرنا واجب ہو گیا کیونکہ اس صورت میں تا خیر فرض گیا ہے اور تا خیر واجب بھی ، تا خیر فرض تو اس لئے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں تاخیر ہوگئی ہے اور قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اور تاخیر واجب اس لئے کہ لفظ رام واجب ہے وہ مؤخر ہو گیا ہے۔ ہدایہ کی عبارت لانه اخر واجبا میں لفظ واجب سے واجب کے معروف معنی بھی مراد ہو سکتے ہیں اور واجب قطعی یعنی فرض بھی دہو سکتا ہے۔ پہلے معنی مراد لینے کی صورت میں لفظ سلام کی تاخیر مراد ہوگی اور دوسرے معنی مراد لینے میں قعدہ اخیرہ کی تاخیر مراد ہوگی ۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw: And if the final sitting was forgotten due to forgetfulness to the extent that he stood for the fifth rak'ah, then when he has not performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, he returns to the sitting because in that is the correction of his prayer, and it is possible for him because less than a rak'ah can be abandoned. Imam Quduri said: He should void the fifth rak'ah because he has turned to something whose place is before the fifth rak'ah; then he should abandon it and perform sujud al-sahw because he has delayed the obligation. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person forgets the final sitting and in a four-rak'ah prayer stands for a fifth rak'ah, or in Maghrib (two rak'ahs?) stands for a fourth, or in Fajr stands for a third, then as long as he has not tied that rak'ah (i.e., the fifth in the four-rak'ah prayer) with prostration, he returns to the sitting. The proof is that in returning to the sitting is the correction of his prayer, and it is possible for him because there is no harm in abandoning less than a rak'ah. Because less than a rak'ah is neither prayer in reality nor in the ruling of prayer. This is why if someone swore that he would not pray, then prayed less than a rak'ah, he does not become sinful. ... In any case, when he abandons the fifth rak'ah and returns to the final sitting, performing sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory because in this case there is a delay of an obligation. The delay of an obligation is because the final sitting was delayed, and the final sitting is obligatory. And the delay of a wajib is because the word (salam?) is wajib and it was delayed. In the statement of al-Hidayah 'because he delayed a wajib', the word 'wajib' can mean the well-known wajib or it can mean the absolute wajib (i.e., fard). If the first meaning is intended, then the delay of salam is meant; if the second, then the delay of the final sitting is meant.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw. It addresses the scenario where a person forgets the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and stands up for an additional rak'ah — e.g., a fifth in a four-rak'ah prayer, a fourth in Maghrib, or a third in Fajr. The ruling is that as long as he has not yet performed the prostration (sajdah) of that extra rak'ah, he should return to the sitting position. The reason is that this return corrects the prayer, and it is possible because abandoning less than a full rak'ah is permissible. The text explains that less than a full rak'ah is not considered a valid unit of prayer in reality or by legal ruling. This is proven by an example: if someone swears not to pray and then prays less than one rak'ah, he does not break his oath. The passage also mentions a principle: if a person returns from an action to something that precedes it in sequence, the action from which he returned becomes void. For instance, if someone sits for tashahhud and then remembers that he missed a sajdah (of prayer or tilawat), and performs that sajdah, the preceding sitting becomes void. Therefore, in this case, having returned from the extra rak'ah to the final sitting, sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory due to the delay of either the final sitting (which is fard) or the salam (which is wajib). The text notes a subtlety in al-Hidayah's wording: 'because he delayed a wajib' could refer to delaying the salam (a wajib) or delaying the final sitting (a fard, which is also called wajib qati').

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): The prostration(s) performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer, which may involve omission, addition, or doubt.
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting in prayer after the last rak'ah, where tashahhud is recited; it is a fard (obligatory) act according to the Hanafis.
لفو (laghw): Void or disregarded; an action that does not count and is treated as if it did not occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets the final sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer, and has NOT yet performed the prostration of that fifth rak'ah, what should he do?
A) Continue and complete five rak'ahs, then perform sujud al-sahw.
B) Return to the sitting position, then perform sujud al-sahw.
C) Abandon the prayer and restart.
D) Perform sujud al-sahw without returning to the sitting.

Key Takeaway
When you forget the final sitting and stand for an extra rak'ah, return to the sitting before prostrating the extra rak'ah, and then perform sujud al-sahw.

Extra Rak'ah with Sajdah: Hanafi Invalidation and Scholarly Disputes
Ruling when extra rak'ah's sajdah is performed; inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing the sajdah of an extra rak'ah after forgetting the final sitting, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Performing the sajdah of an extra rak'ah after forgetting the final sitting invalidates the fard – it initiates nafl before completion.

This lesson examines a specific scenario of forgetfulness in prayer: when a person forgets the final sitting and accidentally performs the prostration of an extra rak'ah. The Hanafi school holds that this invalidates the obligatory prayer, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. Understanding the reasoning behind each view will sharpen your ability to apply the principles of fard, nafl, and contradiction in salah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: if a person forgets the final sitting and performs the sajdah of the extra (fifth) rak'ah, the fard is invalidated according to the Hanafi school.
The invalidation is not immediate upon standing; it occurs only when the sajdah is performed.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the fard is not invalidated; the person should return, sit, recite tashahhud, perform sujud al-sahw, and salam.
Shafi'i position is based on a hadith and analogy.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ prayed Dhuhr five rak'ahs without repeating, and the analogy that adding something outside the prayer (like an extra rak'ah) does not invalidate.
The Hanafis interpret the hadith differently.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the Prophet ﷺ did sit for the fourth rak'ah; the analogy fails because a full rak'ah with sajdah is a complete prayer unit and initiates nafl before completing the fard, which is contradictory.
The concept of a rak'ah with sajdah being 'real prayer' is proven by an oath example.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and note intra-Hanafi difference
The practical consequence: a Hanafi must repeat the fard or consider it nafl; a Shafi'i returns and completes it. Also note: within the Hanafi school, the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say the prayer becomes nafl, while Imam Muhammad says it is completely void.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Shaykhayn.

Source Text

ان قيد الخامسة بسجدة بطل فرضه عندنا خلافا للشافعي لانه استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل اكمال كان المكتوبة ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض وهذا لان الركعة بسجدة واحدة صلوة حقيقة حتى حنت بها في يمينه لا يصلى وتحولت صلاته نفلا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف خلافا لمحمد على مامر جمہ اور اگر اس نے پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فرض باطل ہو گیا۔ امام شافعی کا اس میں اختلاف اس لئے کہ فرض کے ارکان پورے کرنے سے پہلے اس کا نفل کو شروع کر نا مستحکم ہو گیا اور اس کے لئے فرض سے نکلنا لا زم ہے اور یہ اس ا کہ رکعت تو ایک سجدہ کے ساتھ در حقیقت نماز ہے حتی کہ اگر لا یصلی کی قسم کھائی ہو تو ایک رکعت ایک سجدہ کے ساتھ پڑھنے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی نماز بدل کر نفل ہوگئی ہے تیخین کے نزدیک امام محمدکا اختلاف ہے اسی بنا پر جو گذر چکا ہے۔
پانچویں رکھ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قعدہ اخیرہ بھول گیا اور پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فرض امام شافعی کا ہو گیا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس کا فرض باطل نہیں ہوا بلکہ وہ قعدہ کی طرف عود کر کے تشہد پڑھے اور سجدہ سہو کر کے سلام پھیر دے۔ اس وقت ہے جب پانچویں رکعت کے لئے بھول کر کھڑا ہو گیا ہو لیکن اگر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے عمداً کھڑا ہوا اور قعدہ اخیرہ ترک کرنا فيضم الي ہمارے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی اگر پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے تو اس کی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی جس طرح کہ بھول کر کھڑے : یوسف لا" صورت میں نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ شخص جونہی پانچویں رکعت کے لئے عمداً کھڑا ہوا تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلے میں ہمارے اور شوافع کے درمیان دو جگہ اختلاف ہے۔ ایک تو یہ کہ بھول کر اگر ایک رکعت زیادہ کر دی ہے ترجمہ پر چار کے بجائے پانچ ہو گئیں ، تو ہمارے نزدیک پانچویں رکعت کو نہ چھوڑے بلکہ چھٹی رکعت اس کے ساتھ اور ملالے اور امام شافعی کے مزد یک پانچویں رکعت کو اسی طرح چھوڑ دیا جائے گا جس طرح ایک رکعت سے کم کو چھوڑ کر قعدہ کی طرف عود کرنے کا حکم ہے۔ 1م . اگر ایک رکعت سے کم کی زیادتی عمدا کی گئی ہے تو و ہمارے نزدیک نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ پورا ہونا اس ۔ اگر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے بھول کر کھڑا ہوا اور اس کو سجدہ کے ساتھ بھی مقید کر دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فرض باطل ہو گیا۔ شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس کا فرض باطل نہیں ہوا۔ اس پر امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ روایت ہے ان النبي صلى الظهر خمام آنحضرت نے ظہر کی پانچ رکعتیں پڑھیں اور یہ منقول نہیں ہے کہ آپ ا نے چوتھی رکعت پر قعدہ کیا اور نہ یہ منقول ہے کہ ہا اور فرض واقع ہو نے اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کیا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ کہ اس شخص نے اپنی نماز میں بھول کر اس چیز کا اضافہ کیا ہے جو داخل نماز نہیں ہے لبنان اس لئے ان پانچ نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ ایک رکعت سے کم یا زیادہ کرنے کی صورت میں نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص مع السجدہ پانچویں رکعت پڑھنے کی وجہ سے نفل کو شروع کرنے والا ہو گیا حالانکہ ابھی تک فرض نماز اس پر سجدہ سہو دا تمام ارکان مکمل نہیں ہو سکے کیونکہ عدہ اخیرہ جو کن ہے وہ نہیں پایا گیا اور فرض نماز کے تمام ارکان مکمل ہونے سے پہلے چھنگی ک بات کہو سے پورا نہیں نماز شروع کرنا فرض نماز کو فاسد کرنے والا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ فرض اور نقل کے درمیان منافات نے اور حب احد المتنافيين ہی رکعت نہ ملائی تو اس ہے من متحقق ہو گیا۔ تو آخر یعنی فرض منتفی ہو گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ رکعت بلا سجدہ حقیقہ نماز نہیں ہے اور سجدہ کے ساتھ حقیقۂ صلوۃ ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر سی نے قسم کھائی اور و حاصل یہ کہ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
گا جب کہ سجدہ تشریح کچھ رکعتوں کے ساتھ شروع نہیں کیا ہے کے اصلی کیا تو ایک رکعت مجدہ کے ساتھ پڑھنے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابوالحسن قدوری نے فرمایا کہ پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرنے کی وجہ سے فرض کے باطل ہونے میں اختلاف ہے تم انما یبط کے نزدیک وصف فرنیت باطل ہوا ہے نہ کہ اصل صلوۃ یعنی فرض ہونا باطل ہوگیا البتہ نفل ہونا باقی ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل سوا پر پیشانی ٹیکنا، اوراً باطل ہوگئی یعنی یہ نماز جو بغیر قعدہ اخیرہ کے پڑھی گئی ہے نہ فرض شمار ہوگی اور نہ نفل شمار ہوگی ۔ فریقین کے دلائل باب قضاء الفوائت میں جائے گا یا زمین پر چکے ہیں کہ شیخین کے نزدیک بطلان وصف، بطلان اصل نوستلزم نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک بطلان وصف بطلان اصل مستلزم بہانے فرمایا کہ پیشانی نمیکنه رہا امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب تو صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم چوتھی رکعت پر قعدہ اخیرہ میں بیٹھے ہیں اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس بات کی یہ ہے کہ راوی نے کہا ہے صلی الظهر خمسا اور ظہر نام ہے تمام ارکان صلوۃ کا اور تمام ارکان میں قعدہ بھی آخر سر کا اٹھانا ہے لیتے
If he forgot the final sitting and also performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, then the fard becomes invalid? Statements of the jurists: When he ties the fifth with prostration, his fard is invalidated according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because his entrance into the supererogatory prayer becomes established before completing the obligatory prayer, and the necessary consequence is his exit from the obligatory prayer. This is because a rak'ah with one prostration is real prayer to the extent that if he swears 'I will not pray' and then prays one rak'ah with one prostration, he becomes sinful. And his prayer changes to supererogatory according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad based on what has passed. ... Then the detailed scenario: if he forgot the final sitting and tied the fifth rak'ah with prostration, according to us his fard becomes invalid. Imam al-Shafi'i said that his fard does not become invalid; rather, he should return to the sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sujud al-sahw, and say salam. This is when he stood forgetfully for the fifth rak'ah. But if he stood intentionally and omitted the final sitting, according to us, if he has not performed the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah, his prayer is not invalidated, similar to the forgetful case. Al-Shafi'i said that as soon as he intentionally stands for the fifth rak'ah, his prayer is invalidated. The summary: in this issue there are two points of difference between us and the Shafi'is. First, if he added a full rak'ah forgetfully, we say he does not leave it but adds a sixth rak'ah to make it even; Shafi'i says he abandons the fifth and returns to the sitting. Second, if the addition of less than a rak'ah is intentional, according to us it does not invalidate; according to Shafi'i it does. ... Shafi'i's proof is the hadith that the Prophet prayed Dhuhr five rak'ahs, and it is not reported that he sat for the fourth or repeated his prayer. Second proof: this person added something to his prayer forgetfully that is not part of the prayer, so the prayer is not invalidated, like adding less than a rak'ah. Our proof: this person, due to performing the fifth rak'ah with prostration, has started a supererogatory prayer, while the obligatory prayer's pillars have not been completed because the final sitting was not performed. Starting a supererogatory prayer before completing the obligatory prayer invalidates the obligatory prayer because of the contradiction between fard and nafl. ... The author of al-Hidayah said: a rak'ah without prostration is not real prayer, but with prostration it is real prayer. ... Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: there is a difference of opinion regarding the invalidity of the fard due to tying the fifth with prostration. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the attribute of obligatory nature (wasf al-fardiyyah) is invalidated, not the essence of the prayer; so it becomes nafl. According to Imam Muhammad, the essence of the prayer is invalidated; it is neither fard nor nafl. The proofs of both sides go to the chapter on making up missed prayers. ... The response to the hadith presented by al-Shafi'i: the commentator al-Inayah said that the Prophet sat for the fourth rak'ah (i.e., the final sitting), and Imam Muhammad said that the narration 'prayed Dhuhr five' refers to the complete prayer including all its parts, and among those parts is the final sitting.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the effect of performing the sajdah of an extra rak'ah when one has forgotten the final sitting. According to the Hanafi school (our madhhab), if a person forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer and then performs the prostration of that rak'ah, his obligatory prayer (fard) becomes invalid. The reason is that by performing the complete rak'ah with sajdah, he has effectively begun a supererogatory prayer before completing the fard. Since a rak'ah with prostration is legally considered a valid unit of prayer (proven by the oath example), and since the final sitting (a fard pillar) was missed, the fard is invalidated. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the prayer is transformed into a nafl, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it becomes invalid altogether (neither fard nor nafl). The Shafi'i position opposes this: they say the fard is not invalidated; rather, the person should return to the sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sujud al-sahw, and salam. Their evidence includes the hadith of the Prophet praying Dhuhr five rak'ahs (implying that he did not invalidate the prayer), and the analogy that adding something outside the prayer (like an extra rak'ah) does not invalidate just as adding less than a rak'ah does not. The Hanafi response counters that the hadith is interpreted differently (the Prophet did sit for the fourth), and the analogy is rejected because adding a complete extra rak'ah with sajdah constitutes initiating a nafl before completing the fard, which is contradictory. The passage also clarifies that the difference is only when the addition is forgetful; if it is intentional, the Hanafis still do not invalidate the prayer before sajdah, but the Shafi'is do. Additionally, the text summarizes two specific sub-differences: (1) regarding adding a full rak'ah forgetfully — Hanafis advocate adding another to make it even; Shafi'is advocate abandoning the extra rak'ah; (2) regarding intentional addition of less than a rak'ah — Hanafis still preserve the prayer; Shafi'is invalidate it. Finally, the internal Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad is noted: the former see invalidation of the 'attribute' (wasf) of fardiyyah, leaving the prayer as nafl; the latter sees invalidation of the essence (asl), making it void entirely.

Key Terms
بطلان وصف (butlan al-wasf): Invalidation of the attribute (i.e., the status of being fard) while the essence of the prayer remains valid as nafl.
بطلان اصل (butlan al-asl): Invalidation of the essence; the prayer itself becomes void and counts neither as fard nor nafl.
نافلة (nafilah): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary prayer performed in addition to the obligatory ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person forgets the final sitting and performs the sajdah of the extra (fifth) rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer?
A) The prayer remains valid as fard, and sujud al-sahw is performed.
B) The fard is invalidated; according to the Shaykhayn it becomes nafl, and according to Muhammad it becomes completely void.
C) The prayer becomes invalid and must be completely repeated.
D) The person should continue and complete the fifth rak'ah, then do sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, performing the sajdah of a forgetfully added rak'ah after missing the final sitting invalidates the fard (it becomes nafl or void), and one must repeat the obligatory prayer.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
Forgetting the Final Sitting: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on forgetting final sitting and adding a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on forgetting the final sitting and adding a fifth rak'ah, and explain the Hanafi proof based on contradiction between fard and nafil.

Core Idea
If you forget the final sitting and perform a fifth rak'ah with sajdah, your fard becomes nafil — add a sixth, don't sit back.

Imagine you are praying Zuhr, and after the fourth sajdah, you forget to sit and stand for a fifth rak'ah. What should you do? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ. This lesson explores the legal reasoning behind each position, focusing on the nature of the final sitting and the effect of adding an extra rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the exact situation: a four-rak'ah fard prayer, forgetting the final sitting, standing for a fifth rak'ah, and performing the sajdah of that fifth rak'ah.
The ruling differs if one has not yet performed the sajdah.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, the prayer's fard attribute becomes invalid and it becomes a nafil. The person should not sit back, but rather complete the fifth rak'ah and add a sixth to make the nafil even. No sajdah sahw is required.
This is the mufta bihi view from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the fard remains valid. The person should return to the final sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sajdah sahw, and say salam.
The Shafi'i view considers the extra rak'ah a mistake that can be corrected by sajdah sahw.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith where the Prophet prayed Zuhr as five rak'ahs and did not repeat it. They also use qiyas: forgetfully adding something to prayer does not invalidate, similar to adding less than a rak'ah.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari.
5
Analyze the Hanafi proof and response
The Hanafi proof is that the final sitting is a pillar (rukn). Starting another prayer (nafil) before completing the fard pillars contradicts the fard, thus the fard is invalidated. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i hadith is that the Prophet actually sat for the fourth then stood thinking it was the third, and the word 'zuhr' refers to the entire prayer including the final sitting.
This interpretation resolves the apparent conflict.

شم اليها ركعة سادسة ولولم يضم لاشنى عليه لانه مظنون ثم انما يبطل فرضه بوضع الجبهة عند ابي وسف لانه سجود كامل وعند محمد برفعه لان تمام الشئ بآخره وهو الرفع ولم يصح مع الحدث وثمرة اختلاف تظهر فيما اذا سبقه الحدث في السجود بني عند محمد خلافا لابی یوسف جمعہ پس ان پانچوں کے ساتھ چھٹی رکعت ملا دے اور اگر اس نے نہ ملائی تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ مظنون ہے پھر اس کا نا بو یوسف کے نزدیک پیشانی ٹیکتے ہی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ کامل سجدہ ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک سر اٹھانے سے کیونکہ کسی چیز کا ہونا اس کے آخر کے ساتھ ہے اور وہ سراٹھانا ہے اور یہ سراٹھانا حدث کے ساتھ صحیح نہیں ہے اور اختلاف کا ثمرہ اس صورت میں ظاہر ہو ب کہ سجدہ کی حالت میں اس کو حدث لاحق ہو گیا ( اس صورت میں ) امام محمد کے نزدیک بنا کرے۔ امام ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے۔ ریح پچھلی سطروں میں گذر چکا ہے کہ جب پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس کی یہ نماز ظل ہوگئی راض واقع ہونا باطل ہو گیا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل صلوۃ ہی باطل ہوگئی ہے پس چونکہ شیخین کے نزدیک اصل صلوۃ باطل نہیں ہوئی لئے ان پانچوں رکعتوں کے ساتھ چھٹی رکعت ملا دے تا کہ نفل جفت ہو جائیں طاق نہ ر ہیں۔ کیونکہ نفضل جفت مشروع کیا گیا ہے طاق انوں کے ساتھ مشروع نہیں کیا گیا۔ رہا یہ کہ اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا یا نہیں تو بعض کا خیال ہے کہ سجدہ سہو کرے لیکن صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ ر سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ قعدہ اخیرہ نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی ہے اور جو نقصان فساد کی صورت میں ہو وہ سجدہ اسے پورا نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اس لئے سجدہ سہو واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ سجدہ سہو نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے چھٹی ات نہ ملائی تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ نماز جس کو مشروع کیا گیا ہے یعنی پانچویں رکعت وہ مظنون ہے یعنی اس نے قصد انفل نا نہیں کیا ہے اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اس کو چوتھی رکعت سمجھ کر کھڑا ہوا ہے نہ کہ پانچویں رکعت سمجھ کر۔ حاصل یہ کہ یہ نماز جو پانچویں رکعت سے شروع کی ہے وہ مظنون ہے اور مظنون غیر مضمون ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس نماز کی قضاء وغیرہ ب نہ ہوگی۔

Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. 240. Disagreement. Farḍ Abu Yusuf. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya from Ashraf al-Bidaya he will become an oath-breaker. And his prayer turned into nafil. According to the two elders, there is disagreement of Imam Muhammad, due to what has passed. The fifth rak'ah explanation: The case is that if he forgot the final sitting and bound the fifth rak'ah with prostration, then according to us his fard becomes [according to?] Imam Shafi'i. Imam Shafi'i said: His fard did not become invalid, rather he should return to the sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sajdah sahw, and say salam. This is when he stood for the fifth rak'ah forgetfully. But if he intentionally stood for the fifth rak'ah and omitted the final sitting, then according to us, even in this case, if he has not performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, his prayer will not be invalid, just as in the case of forgetfully standing, his prayer is not invalid. And Imam Shafi'i said: As soon as a person intentionally stands for the fifth rak'ah, his prayer becomes invalid. The summary is that in this issue there is disagreement between us and the Shafi'is in two places. One is that if forgetfully he added one rak'ah, making five instead of four, then according to us he should not leave the fifth rak'ah but rather add a sixth rak'ah to it. And according to Imam Shafi'i, he should leave the fifth rak'ah just as one is commanded to return to sitting when having added less than a rak'ah. If less than a rak'ah is added intentionally, then according to us the prayer does not become invalid, and according to Imam Shafi'i it becomes invalid. If he stood for the fifth rak'ah forgetfully and bound it with prostration, then according to us his fard became invalid. Shafi'i said that his fard did not become invalid. For this, Imam Shafi'i's proof is the narration: 'The Prophet prayed zuhr five [rak'ahs]' and it is not transmitted that he sat for the fourth rak'ah, nor is it transmitted that he repeated his prayer. The second proof: This person forgetfully added something that is not part of the prayer, therefore the prayer does not become invalid, just as it does not become invalid when adding less than a rak'ah or more. Our proof is that this person, by praying the fifth rak'ah with prostration, becomes one who is starting nafil, while the fard prayer's pillars have not yet been completed because the final sitting, which is a pillar, is not present. And starting another prayer before completing all pillars of the fard prayer invalidates the fard prayer, because there is contradiction between fard and nafil, and when one of the two contradictory things occurs, the other is negated. So the fard is negated. The author of Hidayah said: A rak'ah without prostration is not reality prayer, and with prostration it is reality prayer. So if he swore an oath, and... the summary is that it will not be wajib. When he has started with the prostration explanation. Some essentials: he did not start with the rak'ahs. If he performed the original once, then by praying one rak'ah with prostration he becomes an oath-breaker. Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: Regarding the invalidation of the fard by binding the fifth rak'ah with prostration, there is disagreement. According to the two elders, the attribute of fardiyyah became invalid, not the essence of prayer, meaning the fardiyyah became invalid, but its being nafil remains. And according to Imam Muhammad, the essence of prayer became invalid, meaning this prayer prayed without the final sitting will not be counted as fard nor as nafil. The proofs of both parties will come in the chapter on making up missed prayers, or they have passed: according to the two elders, invalidation of attribute does not necessitate invalidation of essence, and according to Imam Muhammad, invalidation of attribute necessitates invalidation of essence. He said: the forehead placed... The response to Imam Shafi'i's hadith: The author of 'Inayah said that the Prophet (peace and upon him) sat for the final sitting in the fourth rak'ah. And Imam Muhammad said that this matter is that the narrator said 'prayed zuhr five', and zuhr refers to all the pillars of prayer, and among the pillars is the sitting, and the lifting of the head is also part. [Page 240] Al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Two. 241. Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. For the second rak'ah, he stood thinking it was the third rak'ah. After this interpretation of the hadith, this narration will not be a proof for Shafi'i. Ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah: He adds a sixth rak'ah to it, and if he does not add, nothing is required of him because it is presumptive (maznun). Then his fard becomes invalid by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf because it is a complete prostration. And according to Muhammad, by lifting the head because the completion of a thing is by its end, and that is the lifting of the head, and this lifting is not valid with a hadath. The fruit of the difference appears when a hadath occurs during prostration: according to Muhammad he builds upon it, contrary to Abu Yusuf. So he should add a sixth rak'ah to those five, and if he does not add, nothing is wajib upon him because it is presumptive. Then his fard becomes invalid by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf because it is a complete prostration. And according to Imam Muhammad, by lifting the head because the existence of a thing is by its end, and that is lifting the head, and this lifting is not valid with a hadath. And the fruit of the difference appears when a hadath occurs during prostration (in this case) according to Imam Muhammad he builds, and there is disagreement of Imam Abu Yusuf. It has passed in the previous lines that when he bound the fifth rak'ah with prostration, according to the two elders this prayer became nafil, its being fard became invalid, and according to Imam Muhammad the essence of prayer became invalid. Since according to the two elders the essence of prayer is not invalid, he should add a sixth rak'ah to these five so that the nafil become even and not odd because even number of nafil is prescribed, odd number is not prescribed. As for whether sajdah sahw is obligatory, some think he should perform sajdah sahw, but the correct view is that sajdah sahw is not obligatory because his prayer became invalid due to omitting the final sitting, and a deficiency that occurs in a state of invalidity cannot be compensated by sajdah. Therefore sajdah sahw is not wajib, because sajdah sahw is prescribed to compensate deficiency. And if he does not add the sixth, nothing is wajib upon him because that prayer which is being done, i.e., the fifth rak'ah, is presumptive (maznun), meaning he did not intend nafil, and the reason is that this person stood thinking it was the fourth rak'ah, not the fifth. Summary: This prayer which he started with the fifth rak'ah is presumptive, and presumptive is not confirmed, so its qada etc. will not be necessary. He said 'then his fard becomes invalid', meaning when he performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, the fard becomes invalid. But prostration has a beginning, i.e., placing the forehead on the ground, and an end, i.e., lifting the forehead from the ground. So the question is: Does the fard become invalid by placing the forehead on the ground or by lifting the head from the ground? The author of Hidayah said there is disagreement in this regard. Thus Imam Abu Yusuf said that the fard becomes invalid as soon as he places the forehead because this is a complete prostration, for prostration in reality is called placing the forehead on the ground. And he (referring to Muhammad) said that when he lifts the head from the ground, then his fard becomes invalid, because a thing is completed by its end, and that end is lifting the head. Therefore prostration becomes complete when the head is lifted from the ground. And when prostration is completed by lifting the head, then

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings related to forgetting the final sitting (qadah akhirah) in a four-rak'ah prayer and standing for a fifth rak'ah. It is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is, as well as an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage type is a ruling with proof and dispute. The author begins by stating the case: if one forgets the final sitting and performs the fifth rak'ah with prostration, according to Hanafis the fard becomes nafil, while Shafi'i holds that the fard remains valid and one should return to the sitting. The text then details two points of disagreement: (1) if one adds a rak'ah forgetfully, Hanafis say to add a sixth, Shafi'i says to return; (2) if done intentionally, Hanafis say if no prostration yet, prayer remains valid, while Shafi'i says it becomes invalid immediately upon standing. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of the Prophet praying zuhr as five rak'ahs without repeating, and a qiyas analogy that adding something forgetfully does not invalidate. The Hanafi proof is that by doing the fifth rak'ah with sajdah, one has started a nafil prayer before completing the fard pillars (the final sitting is a pillar), which invalidates the fard due to contradiction. The author then addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute about when exactly the fard becomes invalid: Abu Yusuf says at placing the forehead (sajdah), Muhammad says at lifting the head. The consequence is if a hadath occurs during sajdah, Muhammad allows building, Abu Yusuf does not. The text also explains that adding a sixth rak'ah is recommended to make the nafil even, but if not added, nothing is wajib. Sajdah sahw is not wajib because the deficiency occurred after the prayer became invalid. The concept of 'maznun' (presumptive) is introduced to indicate the extra rak'ah is unintentional and thus not subject to qada.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): The prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
قعدہ اخیرہ (qada al-akhir): The final sitting in a prayer after the last sajdah, during which tashahhud and salawat are recited.
مظنون (maznun): That which is presumptive, i.e., the extra rak'ah that is not intended as nafil but a mistake.
بطلان وصف (butlan wasf): Invalidation of the attribute (fardiyyah) but not the essence of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if they forget the final sitting in Zuhr prayer, stand for a fifth rak'ah, and perform sajdah?
A) Return to the final sitting and perform sajdah sahw.
B) Complete the fifth rak'ah and add a sixth rak'ah, then say salam.
C) Discard the fifth rak'ah and repeat the entire prayer.
D) Complete the fifth rak'ah and say salam without adding a sixth.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the final sitting and performing a fifth rak'ah with sajdah turns your fard into a nafil; add a sixth rak'ah, do not return to sitting.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
7 min
Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: When Does the Fard Become Invalid?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of invalidation after adding a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on when the fard becomes invalid after adding a fifth rak'ah, and state the practical consequence if hadath occurs during sajdah.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf says fard invalid at forehead placement; Muhammad says at head lifting — affects building if hadath occurs.

Even within the Hanafi school, there is a subtle disagreement on the exact moment the fard becomes invalid when a fifth rak'ah is added. This lesson examines the views of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and the practical implications for continuing the prayer if a hadath (ritual impurity) occurs during the sajdah.

Guided Path
1
Recall the scenario
A person forgets the final sitting, stands for a fifth rak'ah, and performs sajdah. According to the two elders (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the fard attribute becomes invalid, but the prayer becomes nafil. However, they disagree on when exactly the fard becomes invalid.
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is one of the two elders; the other is Abu Yusuf.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that the fard becomes invalid at the moment of placing the forehead on the ground for sajdah, because that is a complete sajdah and the act of nafil is finalized.
He considers the sajdah complete upon forehead placement.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's view
Muhammad holds that the fard becomes invalid only upon lifting the head from sajdah, because the completion of an act is at its end.
He considers the sajdah complete upon lifting the head.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a hadath (e.g., breaking wudu) occurs during sajdah, according to Muhammad, since the sajdah is not yet complete, the fard is still intact, and the prayer can be built upon after purification. According to Abu Yusuf, the fard is already invalid, so the prayer cannot be built upon.
Building means continuing from where you left off after making wudu.
5
Apply the ruling to adding a sixth rak'ah and sajdah sahw
The text also rules that after the fifth rak'ah with sajdah, one should add a sixth rak'ah to make the nafil even. Sajdah sahw is not required because the deficiency occurred after the prayer became nafil. This rule is consistent regardless of the intra-Hanafi difference on timing.
The sixth rak'ah is recommended, not obligatory.

تم انما يبطل الخ سے فرمایا ہے کہ جب پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کیا تو فرض باطل ہو جائے گا لیکن سجدہ کا ایک تو آغاز ہے یعنی زمین یشانی ٹیکنا، اور ایک اس کا منتہی ہے یعنی زمین سے پیشانی اٹھانا۔ تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ زمین پر پیشانی ٹھیک دینے سے فرض باطل ہو ے گا یاز مین پر سے سر اٹھانے سے فرض باطل ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اس بارے میں ختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام ابو یوسف نے یا کہ پیشانی ٹیکتے ہی فرض باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ کامل سجدہ ہے اس لئے کہ سجدہ در حقیقت پیشانی زمین پر رکھ دینے کا نام ہے۔ اور نے فرمایا کہ سر جب زمین پر سے اٹھا لے گا تب اس کا فرض باطل ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شے پوری ہوتی ہے اس کے آخر کے ساتھ ، اور اس کا ر کا اٹھانا ہے لہذا سجدہ اس وقت کامل ہو گا جب سرزمین سے اٹھا لیا جائے۔ اور جب سر اٹھانے سے سجدہ کامل ہوتا ہے تو سر اٹھانے
Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. 240. Disagreement. Farḍ Abu Yusuf. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya from Ashraf al-Bidaya he will become an oath-breaker. And his prayer turned into nafil. According to the two elders, there is disagreement of Imam Muhammad, due to what has passed. The fifth rak'ah explanation: The case is that if he forgot the final sitting and bound the fifth rak'ah with prostration, then according to us his fard becomes [according to?] Imam Shafi'i. Imam Shafi'i said: His fard did not become invalid, rather he should return to the sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sajdah sahw, and say salam. This is when he stood for the fifth rak'ah forgetfully. But if he intentionally stood for the fifth rak'ah and omitted the final sitting, then according to us, even in this case, if he has not performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, his prayer will not be invalid, just as in the case of forgetfully standing, his prayer is not invalid. And Imam Shafi'i said: As soon as a person intentionally stands for the fifth rak'ah, his prayer becomes invalid. The summary is that in this issue there is disagreement between us and the Shafi'is in two places. One is that if forgetfully he added one rak'ah, making five instead of four, then according to us he should not leave the fifth rak'ah but rather add a sixth rak'ah to it. And according to Imam Shafi'i, he should leave the fifth rak'ah just as one is commanded to return to sitting when having added less than a rak'ah. If less than a rak'ah is added intentionally, then according to us the prayer does not become invalid, and according to Imam Shafi'i it becomes invalid. If he stood for the fifth rak'ah forgetfully and bound it with prostration, then according to us his fard became invalid. Shafi'i said that his fard did not become invalid. For this, Imam Shafi'i's proof is the narration: 'The Prophet prayed zuhr five [rak'ahs]' and it is not transmitted that he sat for the fourth rak'ah, nor is it transmitted that he repeated his prayer. The second proof: This person forgetfully added something that is not part of the prayer, therefore the prayer does not become invalid, just as it does not become invalid when adding less than a rak'ah or more. Our proof is that this person, by praying the fifth rak'ah with prostration, becomes one who is starting nafil, while the fard prayer's pillars have not yet been completed because the final sitting, which is a pillar, is not present. And starting another prayer before completing all pillars of the fard prayer invalidates the fard prayer, because there is contradiction between fard and nafil, and when one of the two contradictory things occurs, the other is negated. So the fard is negated. The author of Hidayah said: A rak'ah without prostration is not reality prayer, and with prostration it is reality prayer. So if he swore an oath, and... the summary is that it will not be wajib. When he has started with the prostration explanation. Some essentials: he did not start with the rak'ahs. If he performed the original once, then by praying one rak'ah with prostration he becomes an oath-breaker. Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: Regarding the invalidation of the fard by binding the fifth rak'ah with prostration, there is disagreement. According to the two elders, the attribute of fardiyyah became invalid, not the essence of prayer, meaning the fardiyyah became invalid, but its being nafil remains. And according to Imam Muhammad, the essence of prayer became invalid, meaning this prayer prayed without the final sitting will not be counted as fard nor as nafil. The proofs of both parties will come in the chapter on making up missed prayers, or they have passed: according to the two elders, invalidation of attribute does not necessitate invalidation of essence, and according to Imam Muhammad, invalidation of attribute necessitates invalidation of essence. He said: the forehead placed... The response to Imam Shafi'i's hadith: The author of 'Inayah said that the Prophet (peace and upon him) sat for the final sitting in the fourth rak'ah. And Imam Muhammad said that this matter is that the narrator said 'prayed zuhr five', and zuhr refers to all the pillars of prayer, and among the pillars is the sitting, and the lifting of the head is also part. [Page 240] Al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Two. 241. Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. For the second rak'ah, he stood thinking it was the third rak'ah. After this interpretation of the hadith, this narration will not be a proof for Shafi'i. Ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah: He adds a sixth rak'ah to it, and if he does not add, nothing is required of him because it is presumptive (maznun). Then his fard becomes invalid by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf because it is a complete prostration. And according to Muhammad, by lifting the head because the completion of a thing is by its end, and that is the lifting of the head, and this lifting is not valid with a hadath. The fruit of the difference appears when a hadath occurs during prostration: according to Muhammad he builds upon it, contrary to Abu Yusuf. So he should add a sixth rak'ah to those five, and if he does not add, nothing is wajib upon him because it is presumptive. Then his fard becomes invalid by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf because it is a complete prostration. And according to Imam Muhammad, by lifting the head because the existence of a thing is by its end, and that is lifting the head, and this lifting is not valid with a hadath. And the fruit of the difference appears when a hadath occurs during prostration (in this case) according to Imam Muhammad he builds, and there is disagreement of Imam Abu Yusuf. It has passed in the previous lines that when he bound the fifth rak'ah with prostration, according to the two elders this prayer became nafil, its being fard became invalid, and according to Imam Muhammad the essence of prayer became invalid. Since according to the two elders the essence of prayer is not invalid, he should add a sixth rak'ah to these five so that the nafil become even and not odd because even number of nafil is prescribed, odd number is not prescribed. As for whether sajdah sahw is obligatory, some think he should perform sajdah sahw, but the correct view is that sajdah sahw is not obligatory because his prayer became invalid due to omitting the final sitting, and a deficiency that occurs in a state of invalidity cannot be compensated by sajdah. Therefore sajdah sahw is not wajib, because sajdah sahw is prescribed to compensate deficiency. And if he does not add the sixth, nothing is wajib upon him because that prayer which is being done, i.e., the fifth rak'ah, is presumptive (maznun), meaning he did not intend nafil, and the reason is that this person stood thinking it was the fourth rak'ah, not the fifth. Summary: This prayer which he started with the fifth rak'ah is presumptive, and presumptive is not confirmed, so its qada etc. will not be necessary. He said 'then his fard becomes invalid', meaning when he performed the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, the fard becomes invalid. But prostration has a beginning, i.e., placing the forehead on the ground, and an end, i.e., lifting the forehead from the ground. So the question is: Does the fard become invalid by placing the forehead on the ground or by lifting the head from the ground? The author of Hidayah said there is disagreement in this regard. Thus Imam Abu Yusuf said that the fard becomes invalid as soon as he places the forehead because this is a complete prostration, for prostration in reality is called placing the forehead on the ground. And he (referring to Muhammad) said that when he lifts the head from the ground, then his fard becomes invalid, because a thing is completed by its end, and that end is lifting the head. Therefore prostration becomes complete when the head is lifted from the ground. And when prostration is completed by lifting the head, then
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings related to forgetting the final sitting (qadah akhirah) in a four-rak'ah prayer and standing for a fifth rak'ah. It is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is, as well as an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage type is a ruling with proof and dispute. The author begins by stating the case: if one forgets the final sitting and performs the fifth rak'ah with prostration, according to Hanafis the fard becomes nafil, while Shafi'i holds that the fard remains valid and one should return to the sitting. The text then details two points of disagreement: (1) if one adds a rak'ah forgetfully, Hanafis say to add a sixth, Shafi'i says to return; (2) if done intentionally, Hanafis say if no prostration yet, prayer remains valid, while Shafi'i says it becomes invalid immediately upon standing. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of the Prophet praying zuhr as five rak'ahs without repeating, and a qiyas analogy that adding something forgetfully does not invalidate. The Hanafi proof is that by doing the fifth rak'ah with sajdah, one has started a nafil prayer before completing the fard pillars (the final sitting is a pillar), which invalidates the fard due to contradiction. The author then addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute about when exactly the fard becomes invalid: Abu Yusuf says at placing the forehead (sajdah), Muhammad says at lifting the head. The consequence is if a hadath occurs during sajdah, Muhammad allows building, Abu Yusuf does not. The text also explains that adding a sixth rak'ah is recommended to make the nafil even, but if not added, nothing is wajib. Sajdah sahw is not wajib because the deficiency occurred after the prayer became invalid. The concept of 'maznun' (presumptive) is introduced to indicate the extra rak'ah is unintentional and thus not subject to qada.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): The prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
قعدہ اخیرہ (qada al-akhir): The final sitting in a prayer after the last sajdah, during which tashahhud and salawat are recited.
مظنون (maznun): That which is presumptive, i.e., the extra rak'ah that is not intended as nafil but a mistake.
بطلان وصف (butlan wasf): Invalidation of the attribute (fardiyyah) but not the essence of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the intra-Hanafi dispute, if a hadath occurs while the forehead is on the ground during the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah, which imam allows building upon the prayer after purification?
A) Imam Abu Yusuf
B) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Both imams allow building
D) Neither imam allows building

Key Takeaway
The exact moment of invalidation differs among Hanafi imams; if hadath occurs during sajdah, Abu Yusuf says no building, Muhammad says building is allowed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
When Does a Mistaken Fifth Rak'ah Invalidate Fard?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on moment of invalidation by fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the moment a mistakenly added fifth rak'ah invalidates the fard prayer and apply the practical consequence when hadath occurs during the sajdah of that rak'ah.

Core Idea
Completion of sajdah: placing the forehead (Abu Yusuf) vs raising the head (Muhammad) — determines if fard can be rescued after hadath.

This lesson explores a subtle but practically important intra-Hanafi dispute about the exact moment a mistakenly added fifth rak'ah invalidates the fard prayer. The key question is: when exactly is a sajdah considered complete? The answer has direct consequences for whether a person can salvage their prayer if their wudu breaks during that sajdah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah
The passage begins by stating that if a person mistakenly adds a fifth rak'ah, he should add a sixth to make the supererogatory prayer even-numbered. This is recommended, not obligatory.
No sajdah sahw is required if he does not add a sixth, because the prayer is invalidated.
2
State the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Both agree the fard becomes invalid upon completing the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah. Abu Yusuf says placing the forehead completes sajdah; Muhammad says raising the head completes it.
This is the core of the dispute.
3
Analyse the rational proof (dalil aqli) of each imam
Abu Yusuf argues sajdah is essentially placing. Muhammad argues an action's completion is by its end. Muhammad also uses consensus: if hadath occurs in a pillar, repetition is obligatory; if placing completed sajdah, repetition would not be needed.
Muhammad's proof uses consensus and logical implication.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If hadath occurs during the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah, according to Abu Yusuf the fard is already invalid (sajdah complete on placing), so he cannot continue. According to Muhammad, sajdah is not yet complete, so the fard is still valid; he can return to the fourth rak'ah after wudu.
This shows the real-world impact of the dispute.
5
Note the absence of tarjih in Al-Hidayah
The text presents both positions without declaring a preponderant (mufta bihi) view. Both are considered valid within the Hanafi school.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

He adds a sixth rak'ah to it, and if he does not add, nothing is incumbent upon him because it is presumptive. Then his fard is invalidated by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf because it is a complete sajdah, and according to Muhammad by raising it because the completion of a thing is by its end, which is raising, and it is not valid with hadath. The fruit of the difference appears when hadath precedes him in sajdah: according to Muhammad he builds, contrary to Abu Yusuf. ... Then when he prostrates for the fifth rak'ah, the fard becomes invalid. But sajdah has a beginning, which is placing the forehead on the ground, and an end, which is raising the forehead from the ground. So the question is: does the fard become invalid upon placing the forehead on the ground or upon raising the head from the ground? The author of Hidayah said there is a difference. Imam Abu Yusuf said: upon placing the forehead, the fard becomes invalid because it is a complete sajdah, for sajdah is essentially placing the forehead on the ground. And he (Muhammad) said: when he raises his head from the ground, then his fard becomes invalid because a thing is completed by its end, and its end is raising; therefore sajdah is complete when the head is raised from the ground. And when sajdah is complete by raising the head, the fard becomes invalid only after raising the head, not before. Imam Muhammad supported his statement: 'And it is not valid with hadath', i.e., raising the head while in a state of hadath is not valid. The conclusion: all agree that if hadath occurs in a pillar, its repetition is obligatory. So Imam Muhammad said: if during the fifth rak'ah hadath occurs, its repetition is obligatory by consensus. And when its repetition is obligatory, it shows that sajdah is not completed merely by placing the forehead. Because if sajdah were completed merely by placing the forehead, its repetition would not be obligatory if hadath occurred, since the sajdah would already have been completed. So it is established that the completion of sajdah is by raising the forehead from the ground, not merely by placing it on the ground. The fruit of the difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad appears in the case where this person is in the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah and hadath overtakes him. He goes to perform wudu, then remembers that he did not perform the final sitting after the fourth rak'ah. According to Imam Muhammad, he performs wudu, returns to the final sitting, completes his fard by reciting tashahhud, performs sajdah sahw, and says salam. Because according to Muhammad, sajdah is not complete before raising the head from the ground, and raising the head while in hadath is not valid. So in his view, this sajdah is not considered valid. And when the sajdah is not considered valid, the fifth rak'ah has not been connected with sajdah, so his fard has not become invalid. Since his fard is not invalid, he returns to the final sitting and completes his fard. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, this person does not build on his prayer because according to Abu Yusuf, upon placing the forehead on the ground the sajdah is complete, and when the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah is complete, his fard becomes invalid, and building upon an invalid prayer is not permissible.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the moment when a supererogatory rak'ah (fifth) invalidates the fard prayer. The ruling: if a person mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah, he should add a sixth to make the supererogatory prayer even-numbered. He is not required to add it. The point of contention: at what moment does the fard become invalid? Abu Yusuf holds that placing the forehead in sajdah completes the sajdah and thus invalidates the fard. Muhammad holds that the sajdah is only complete upon raising the head, so the fard becomes invalid only after that. The practical consequence is evident when a person experiences hadath during the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah. According to Muhammad, since raising the head with hadath is invalid, the sajdah is not considered, so the fard remains valid and he can return to the final sitting. According to Abu Yusuf, the sajdah is already complete upon placing the forehead, so the fard is invalid and he cannot build on it. The passage clarifies that sajdah sahw is not required because the prayer has become invalidated by omitting the final sitting properly.

Key Terms
مظنون (maznun): Presumptive; here referring to the fifth rak'ah being unintentional, not deliberately added as a supererogatory prayer.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when does the mistakenly added fifth rak'ah invalidate the fard prayer?
A) When one stands for the fifth rak'ah
B) When one places the forehead in sajdah
C) When one raises the head from sajdah
D) Only after completing the sixth rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the moment sajdah is completed has a direct practical consequence for whether a person can salvage their fard prayer after hadath occurs during a mistakenly added rak'ah.

Returning to Final Sitting After Standing for Fifth Rak'ah
Ruling on returning to final sitting after standing for fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on returning to the final sitting after standing for a fifth rak'ah without salam and identify the condition that permits return.

Core Idea
Salams must be performed while sitting; a standing salam is invalid, so return to sitting is wajib.

This passage addresses a common forgetfulness scenario: after completing tashahhud in the fourth rak'ah, the worshipper forgetfully stands up without saying salam. The text rules that he must return to the sitting position as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth rak'ah, and then say salam. We will examine the reasoning behind this ruling and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The worshipper sits for tashahhud in the fourth rak'ah then stands without salam. The ruling is that he must return to the sitting.
The return is wajib (obligatory) because salam must be performed while sitting.
2
Determine the condition for return
The return is valid only as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth rak'ah. If he has prostrated, the fifth rak'ah is counted and the prayer changes.
The text says 'malam yasjud lil-khamisah' (as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth).
3
Analyze the rationale
Saying salam while standing is not legislated (ghayr mashru'). Since he has only stood and not completed a full rak'ah, the standing action is less than a rak'ah and can be abandoned.
The principle: 'less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment' (ma duna al-rak'ah bi-mahall al-rafd).
4
Apply the ruling
He returns to the sitting, does not repeat tashahhud (since it was already done correctly), and then says salam to complete the fard prayer.
No repetition of tashahhud is needed; the prayer continues from where it was interrupted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قعد في الرابعة ثم قام ولم يسلم عاد الى القعدة مالم يسجد للخامسة وسلم لان التسليم في حالة الم دوگانہ پر آتے غير مشروع وامكنه الاقامة على وجهه بالقعود لان ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض تشریح ترجمہ اور اگر چوتھی رکعت پر قعدہ کیا پھر کھڑا ہو گیا اور سلام نہیں پھیرا تو قعدہ کی طرف عود کرے جب تک کہ پانچویں رکعت کے رکعت نہیں سجد ہ نہیں کیا اور سلام پھیرے کیونکہ قیام کی حالت میں سلام پھیر نا مشروع نہیں ہے اور وجہ مشروع پر قعدہ کی طرف عود کرنے کے ساتھ چھٹی دونوں کو قائم کرناممکن بھی ہے کیونکہ ایک رکعت سے کم چھوڑے جانے کا مل ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مصلی نے مقدار تشہد چوتھی رکعت پر قاعدہ کیا ،اور سلام نہیں پھیرا بلکہ بھول کر کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب واجب کی و پانچویں رکعت کے لئے سجدہ نہیں کیا قعدہ کی طرف لوٹ جائے لیکن قعدہ کی طرف لوٹ آنے کے بعد تشہد کا اعادہ نہ کرے بلکہ بعد ہی تو اس کی فرض کے سلام پھیر دے۔
And if he sits in the fourth (rak'ah) then stands and does not say salam, he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth, and says salam, because saying salam while standing is not legislated, and it is possible for him to establish (the prayer) properly by sitting, because less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment. Explanation: Translation: If he sits for the fourth rak'ah then stands up and does not say salam, he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth rak'ah, and says salam, because saying salam while standing is not legislated, and it is possible for him to establish (the prayer) properly by returning to the sitting, because less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment. Explanation: The scenario is that if the worshipper sits for the measure of tashahhud in the fourth rak'ah, and does not say salam but forgetfully stands up, then as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth rak'ah, he returns to the sitting. But after returning to the sitting, he does not repeat the tashahhud; rather he then says the salam of his fard prayer.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding someone who, after sitting for tashahhud in the fourth rak'ah, forgetfully stands up without saying salam. The ruling: he should return to the sitting (qa'dah) as long as he has not performed the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah. The reason given is that saying salam while standing is not legislated (ghayr mashru'). Also, since he has not yet completed a full rak'ah (he only stood up), the action of standing is less than a rak'ah and can be abandoned (rafd). Therefore, returning to the sitting is possible and correct. After returning, he should not repeat the tashahhud; he simply says salam to complete the fard prayer. This ruling is based on the principle that once the final sitting is performed with tashahhud, the prayer is nearly complete; the salam is the final act, and it must be performed in the sitting position. If he stands, he is in a state incompatible with the salam, so he must rectify by sitting.

Key Terms
قعدہ (qa'dah): The sitting posture after the fourth rak'ah (final sitting) containing tashahhud.
سلام (salam): The concluding salutation of the prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition allows a person to return to the final sitting after standing up for a fifth rak'ah without salam?
A) He has not yet performed the ruku of the fifth rak'ah
B) He has not yet prostrated for the fifth rak'ah
C) He has not yet recited anything in the fifth rak'ah
D) He can always return regardless

Key Takeaway
Returning to the sitting is wajib if no sajdah of the fifth rak'ah has been performed, to enable the proper sitting position for salam.

When is Sajdah Complete: Placing vs Lifting the Forehead
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the moment sajdah is completed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the completion of sajdah and apply the practical consequence (thamarah) when hadath occurs during the sajdah of a fifth rak'ah.

Core Idea
Sajdah is not complete until the forehead is lifted; if hadath occurs before lifting, the sajdah must be repeated.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement between two of the school's greatest imams—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question is deceptively simple: when exactly is a prostration considered legally complete? The answer determines whether a mistaken fifth rak'ah invalidates the entire prayer or can be corrected. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a difference in definition leads to a difference in ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Act and Context
The act is sajdah during a mistakenly added fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer. The key event is hadath (ritual impurity) occurring while the forehead is on the ground but before lifting it.
2
State the Two Rival Positions
Imam Muhammad holds sajdah is complete only after lifting the forehead. Imam Abu Yusuf holds sajdah is complete upon placing the forehead.
Both are within the Hanafi school; neither is outside the madhhab.
3
Analyse Imam Muhammad's Proof
He argues: if sajdah were complete by placing, hadath would not necessitate repetition of the sajdah. But there is consensus (ittifaq) that when hadath occurs during a pillar, that pillar must be repeated. Therefore, sajdah cannot be complete until lifting.
The proof is by necessity (talil) from the obligation to repeat.
4
Analyse Imam Abu Yusuf's Position
He considers the placement itself as completion, similar to how other actions (e.g., ruku) are considered performed once the posture is assumed. The text does not give his full proof but implies a more literal view.
His position may analogize sajdah to other actions where the completion is by initiation.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
According to Muhammad: the fifth rak'ah is not fully tied to a sajdah, so the fard (obligatory prayer) is not yet invalidated; the person can perform wudu, return to the final sitting, recite tashahhud, perform sajdah al-sahw, and conclude with salam. According to Abu Yusuf: the fifth rak'ah is complete, invalidating the fard, so the person must restart the prayer.
This is the practical consequence that matters for fatwa.

Source Text

Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. The fard becomes invalid only after the sitting. Before that it does not become invalid. Imam Muhammad said in support of his statement: 'And it is not valid with hadath', meaning raising the head with hadath is not correct. The conclusion is that [؟and] there is consensus on the well-known that whichever pillar in which hadath occurs, repeating that pillar is obligatory. So Imam Muhammad said: If hadath occurs in the obligatory connection of the fifth rak'ah, then its repetition is obligatory by consensus. And when its repetition is obligatory, it became known that the sajdah is only completed by placing the forehead. If the sajdah were completed merely by placing the forehead, then in case of hadath its repetition would not be obligatory, because with hadath the sajdah would have been completed. Nevertheless, it is proven that the completion of sajdah is by lifting the forehead from the ground, not merely by placing it on the ground. [؟Sharik] is the fruit of the difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad in this case: that person [؟-Mushakhkhas-] went for [؟wudu] and then remembered that he did not perform the last sitting after the fourth rak'ah. According to Imam Muhammad, he should perform [؟wudu] and return to the last sitting and complete his fard prayer in such a way that he recites tashahhud, performs sajdah al-sahw, and says salam, because [؟there is no disagreement] with Muhammad that before lifting the head from the ground the sajdah is not complete. And raising the head with hadath is not correct. So according to him, this sajdah is not considered valid. And when the sajdah is not valid, then the fifth rak'ah has not been tied with sajdah. And when the fifth rak'ah is not tied with sajdah, then its fard has not become invalid. And when the fard is not invalid, he should return to the last sitting and complete the fard. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, this person [؟builds] upon his prayer, because according to Imam Abu Yusuf, by placing the forehead on the ground the sajdah is completed. And when the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah is completed, then his fard becomes invalid. And when the fard is invalid, he cannot build upon it because building upon the invalid is not allowed.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the completion of sajdah (prostration) and its effect on the validity of an additional rak'ah added due to forgetfulness. The issue arises when a person performing a four-rak'ah prayer mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah, prostrates, and then experiences hadath (ritual impurity) before lifting the forehead from the sajdah. The key point of difference: Imam Muhammad holds that sajdah is only complete after lifting the forehead from the ground. Therefore, if hadath occurs before lifting, the sajdah is invalid, meaning the fifth rak'ah has not been properly tied to a sajdah, and the fard (obligatory prayer) is not yet invalidated. Consequently, the person can perform wudu, return to the last sitting (qa'dah akhira), recite tashahhud, perform sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness), and conclude with salam. Imam Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, holds that sajdah is complete merely by placing the forehead on the ground. Thus, if hadath occurs after placing but before lifting, the sajdah is still valid, and the fifth rak'ah is complete. This makes the fard invalid due to an extra rak'ah, and the person cannot build upon it; the prayer must be restarted. The passage uses reasoning ('talil) based on the principle that if sajdah were complete by just placing, then hadath would not require repetition of the sajdah, but since repetition is required (by consensus when hadath occurs during a pillar), sajdah must only be complete after lifting. This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf without mention of tarjih.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, such as passing wind or urine.
سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration, a pillar of prayer involving placing the forehead on the ground. The dispute is whether it is completed by placing or lifting.
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting after the last rak'ah of prayer, where tashahhud is recited.
ثمرہ (thamarah): The practical consequence or fruit of a scholarly difference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why does the occurrence of hadath before lifting the forehead require repetition of the sajdah?
A) Because hadath invalidates any incomplete action.
B) Because sajdah is not complete until the forehead is lifted, so it is still part of the pillar.
C) Because hadath always requires repetition of the entire prayer.
D) Because lifting the forehead is the actual pillar, not placing it.

Key Takeaway
The completion of sajdah is not merely by placing the forehead; it requires lifting, and this difference determines whether a mistaken fifth rak'ah can be corrected.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Returning to Sitting Before Fifth Sajdah
Ruling for one who stands for fifth rak'ah without salam and returns before prostrating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for forgetfully standing for a fifth rak'ah and explain the conditions for returning to sitting and the requirement of sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
A forgetful extra standing before sajdah in the fifth rak'ah is corrected by returning to sitting and performing sajdah al-sahw, as long as the fifth sajdah has not been performed.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in prayer: forgetfully standing up for an extra rak'ah after the fourth without saying salam. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy based on the Prophet's ﷺ action. The key insight is that a rak'ah is only considered complete once sajdah has been performed, which allows the worshiper to abandon the incomplete portion and correct the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The worshiper has completed the fourth rak'ah tashahhud and forgetfully stands for a fifth without saying salam.
2
Determine the Critical Condition
Check whether the worshiper has performed sajdah for the fifth rak'ah. The ruling applies only if sajdah has not been performed.
If sajdah has been performed, a different correction is required.
3
Apply the Ruling
If no sajdah, the worshiper must return to sitting (qa'dah), say salam, and perform sajdah al-sahw. He should not repeat tashahhud.
Sajdah al-sahw compensates for the forgetful standing.
4
Understand the Proof
The hadith of the Prophet ﷺ standing for a fifth and returning to sitting before prostrating provides the naqli proof. The rational proof: salam while standing is not prescribed; returning to sitting is the proper way.
The hadith is ahad but indicates the practice.
5
Internalize the Principle
A rak'ah is only complete when sajdah is performed. Before that, it is 'less than a rak'ah' and can be abandoned without invalidating the prayer.
Analogous to leaving a first rak'ah to join the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
