Building Upon Two Rak'ahs After Sujood al-Sahw
Ruling on building after sujood al-sahw in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building additional rak'ahs after sujood al-sahw in nafl prayer and identify the exception for a traveler.

Core Idea
Sujood al-sahw marks the end of the prayer; adding more rak'ahs invalidates the sujood but the prayer remains valid.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir addresses a specific scenario: a person prays two rak'ahs of nafl, makes an error, performs sujood al-sahw, and then wants to add two more rak'ahs by building (bina). The ruling clarifies when building is permissible and when it is not, along with the consequences if one does build. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the integrity of the prayer structure in voluntary prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is building additional rak'ahs after performing sujood al-sahw in a nafl prayer. The ruling is that one should not build (lam yabni).
The prohibition is explicit from Imam Muhammad's statement.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir, which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The authority is Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This is a transmitted ruling from the early Hanafi masters.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reason given is that sujood al-sahw, when performed in the middle of the prayer due to building, invalidates the building. Sujood al-sahw is prescribed at the end of prayer, and placing it in the middle disrupts the continuity.
The phrase 'lianna al-sujood yubtilu li-wuqu'ihi fi wast al-salah' provides the legal cause.
4
Note the exception
A traveler who performs sujood al-sahw and then intends to stay (becomes resident) may build, because if he does not build, the entire prayer becomes invalid due to the change in obligation from two to four rak'ahs.
This exception demonstrates that necessity (darurah) allows building to preserve the prayer's validity.
5
Evaluate the consequence if built
If one erroneously builds despite the prohibition, the prayer remains valid because the original tahrimah remains, and the sujood al-sahw becomes invalid. This is the correct position (huwa al-sahih).
The ruling balances prohibition with preservation of the prayer's validity when done in ignorance or forgetfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفل کی دورکعتیں پڑھیں ان میں بھولا اور سجدہ سہو بھی کر لیا دو اور رکعتوں کی بنا پہلی پر کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں
قال ومن صلى ركعتين تطوعا فسهى فيهما وسجد للسهو ثم اراد ان يصلى اخريين لم يبن لان السجود يبطل لوقوعه في وسط الصلوة بخلاف المسافر اذا سجد للسهو ثم نوى الاقامة حيث يبنى لانه لولم بين يبطل جميع الصلوة ومع هذا الوادى صح لبقاء التحريمة ويبطل سجود السهو هو الصحيح ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ جس شخص نے دو رکعت نفل نماز پڑھیں اور ان میں سہو ہو گیا اور سہو کا سجدہ کیا پھر چاہا کہ دوسری دو رکعت پڑھے تو بناء نہ کرے کیونکہ سجدہ سہو اس کو باطل کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ سجدہ وسط صلوۃ میں پڑ گیا ہے بخلاف مسافر کے جب اس نے سجدہ سہو کیا پھر اقامت کی نیت کر لی تو وہ بناء کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مسافر اگر بناء نہ کرے تو پوری ہی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اس کے باوجود اگر اس نے ادا کیا تو صحیح ہے کیونکہ تحریمہ باقی ہے اور سجدہ سہو باطل ہو جائے گا یہی قول صحیح ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے نقل کی دو رکعتیں پڑھی لیکن ان میں کوئی سہو ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے جدا ہو کیا۔ پر اس نے چاہا کہ ان دور کعتوں پر اور دو رکعت نفل کی بناء کرے تو اس شخص کو بناء کی اجازت نہیں ہے بلکہ سلام پھیر کر علیحدہ تحریمہ کرے ساتھ دو رکعت نفل پڑھنے دلیل سے پہلے یہ بات ذہن نشین رکھئے کہ سجدہ سہو نماز کے آخر میں مشروع کیا گیا ہے نماز کے دو شعوں
He prayed two rak'ahs of nafl, forgot in them, and performed sujood al-sahw, then he wanted to pray two more rak'ahs. Can he build upon the first? He said: 'Whoever prays two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer (tatawwu'), forgets in them, performs sujood al-sahw, then wants to pray two more rak'ahs, he should not build (lam yabni) because the sujood al-sahw invalidates [the building] due to its occurrence in the middle of the prayer. Unlike a traveler who, when he performs sujood al-sahw and then intends to stay (iqamah), he may build because if he does not build, the entire prayer becomes invalid. Despite this, if he does perform it, it is valid because the tahrimah remains and the sujood al-sahw becomes invalid. That is the correct statement.' Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that a person who prayed two rak'ahs of nafl, forgetfulness occurred, he performed sujood al-sahw, then wanted to pray another two rak'ahs, should not build. Because sujood al-sahw invalidates building since it fell in the middle of the prayer. Unlike a traveler who, after sujood al-sahw, intends to stay (iqamah); he may build because if he does not build, the entire prayer becomes invalid. Despite this, if he performed it (i.e., built), it is valid because the tahrimah remains and the sujood al-sahw becomes invalid. This is the correct statement. Explanation: The case is that a person prayed two rak'ahs of nafl, but forgetfulness occurred which caused him to... (text cuts off) but he wanted to build upon these two rak'ahs with another two rak'ahs of nafl. This person is not permitted to build; rather, he should say salam and begin a new tahrimah with two rak'ahs of nafl. Keep in mind that sujood al-sahw is prescribed at the end of the prayer...
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir. The ruling: If a person prays two rak'ahs of nafl, forgets, and performs sujood al-sahw at the end of those two rak'ahs, and then wants to add two more rak'ahs by building (i.e., without saying salam and starting a new prayer), they should not do so. The reason is that sujood al-sahw falls at the end of the prayer, and adding more rak'ahs would place it in the middle, which invalidates the building. However, if they do build, the prayer is valid because the original tahrimah remains, and the sujood al-sahw becomes invalid. An exception is a traveler who, after performing sujood al-sahw, intends to stay (becoming a resident). He may build because if he does not, the entire prayer becomes invalid since he now must pray full (four rak'ahs) and the prayer would be incomplete. The commentary clarifies that building is not permitted; one should say salam and begin a new prayer with a new tahrimah.

Key Terms
بناء (bina): Building upon previous rak'ahs, i.e., continuing the prayer without a new tahrimah.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer (nafl).
وسط الصلوة (wast al-salah): The middle of the prayer, i.e., before the end. Sujood al-sahw performed in the middle invalidates the building of additional rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, what is the ruling if a person prays two rak'ahs of nafl, performs sujood al-sahw, then tries to add two more rak'ahs by building?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) He should not build, but if he does, the prayer is valid and the sujood becomes invalid.
C) He must build because the prayer is continuous.
D) He can build only if he is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
Building additional rak'ahs after sujood al-sahw in nafl prayer is prohibited, but if done, the prayer remains valid while the sujood becomes void, unless one is a traveler needing to complete the obligation.

Building After Sajdah al-Sahw and the Traveler's Exception
Ruling on building after sajdah sahw with traveler's comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on building after sajdah al-sahw and identify when building becomes obligatory for a traveler.

Core Idea
Building after sajdah al-sahw is valid but renders the sajdah invalid; a traveler must build to avoid invalidating the fard.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on building (bina') after performing sajdah al-sahw in the middle of prayer. The commentary from Al-Hidayah clarifies that while building is permissible, it invalidates the sajdah already done, requiring its repetition. However, a special exception applies to a traveler who intends to settle, for whom building becomes obligatory to preserve the fard prayer. This distinction illustrates the Hanafi legal maxim of choosing the lesser harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Consider a person who prays two rak'ahs, then performs sajdah al-sahw due to forgetfulness, and then builds (adds two more rak'ahs without a new takbir).
The key is that sajdah al-sahw occurred mid-prayer.
2
State the ruling for the normal case
Building is not recommended, but if done, the prayer remains valid because the tahrimah (opening sanctity) persists. However, the sajdah al-sahw becomes invalid because it was performed in the middle of prayer, where it is not legislated. It must be repeated after the complete prayer.
The sajdah is invalid, not the prayer.
3
Provide the proof
The proof is that sajdah al-sahw is prescribed only at the end of prayer (before or after salam). Performing it mid-prayer contravenes this prescription, so it is invalid.
This is based on the hadith evidence for sajdah al-sahw.
4
Examine the traveler's exception
If a traveler who intended to perform qasr (two rak'ahs) performs sajdah al-sahw after two rak'ahs and then intends to stay (iqamah), he must build and complete four rak'ahs. Even though this violates the proper timing of sajdah al-sahw, the greater harm of invalidating the entire fard prayer is avoided by tolerating the lesser harm of violating a wajib (the correct placement of sajdah).
The maxim: 'A greater evil is removed by tolerating a lesser evil' applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ بلا شبہ اس شخص کو بناء نہ کرنی چاہئے لیکن اس کے باوجود اگر بناء کر لی اور دوسرا دوگانہ بھی ادا کر لیا تو صحیح ہے کیونکہ ابھی تک تحریمہ باقی ہے البتہ سجدہ سہو باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ جب بناء کی تو سجدہ سہو نماز کے درمیان میں واقع ہو گیا ہے حالانکہ نماز کے درمیان میں سجدہ سہو مشروع نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے یہ سجدہ غیر معتبر ہوگا اور اس پر سجدہ سہو کا اعادہ واجب ہوگا۔ بخلاف المسافرالح ، اس عبارت کا حکم مسئلہ متن کے خلاف ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے فرض رباعی کا قصر کرتے ہوئے دو رکعت پڑھیں اور سہو پیش آنے کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کیا پھر سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے اقامت کی نیت کی تو یہ مسافر ای تحریمہ پر بناء کرے اور چار رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیرے کیونکہ اقامت کی نیت سے اس پر چار رکعت پوری کرنا لازم ہو گیا ہے اب اگر یہ شخص بناء نہ کرے تو اس کی پوری نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور بناء کرنے میں نقض واجب ہے کیونکہ سجدہ سہو کا باطل کرنا ہے اور نقض واجب ادنی ہے یہ نسبت ابطال فرض کے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ بڑی برائی کو دور کرنے کے لئے چھوٹی برائی کو برداشت کیا جاسکتا ہے اس لئے اعلی یعنی فرض نماز کو باطل ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے ادنی یعنی سجدہ سہو کے نقض کو برداشت کر لیا جائے گا۔
The author of Hidayah says: Undoubtedly, this person should not perform building (bina'), but if he does build and also performs the second two rak'ahs, it is valid because the opening takbir (tahrimah) still remains. However, his sajdah al-sahw becomes invalid because when he built, the sajdah al-sahw occurred in the middle of the prayer, while sajdah al-sahw in the middle of the prayer is not legislated. Therefore, this sajdah is invalid and he must repeat the sajdah al-sahw. Contrary to the traveler... The ruling of this phrase contradicts the text. The summary is: A traveler, while performing the qasr of a four-rak'ah fard, prayed two rak'ahs and performed sajdah al-sahw due to forgetfulness, then before making salam he intended to stay (iqamah). This traveler should build upon his tahrimah and complete four rak'ahs and then make salam, because by intending iqamah, completing four rak'ahs became obligatory upon him. Now if this person does not build, his entire prayer becomes invalid. In building, there is violation of a wajib (invalidating the sajdah al-sahw), and violating a wajib is a lesser evil compared to invalidating a fard. The principle is: A greater evil can be removed by tolerating a lesser evil. Therefore, to save the higher (fard prayer) from invalidation, the lower (violation of sajdah al-sahw) is tolerated.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from the commentary on Hidayah, addressing the situation where a person performs sajdah al-sahw after two rak'ahs and then considers building (bina') upon that prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one should not build, because the sajdah al-sahw should be performed at the end of the prayer after salam. However, if one does build, the prayer remains valid because the tahrimah (opening sanctity) persists, but the sajdah al-sahw becomes invalid because it occurred mid-prayer where sajdah al-sahw is not allowed; therefore, it must be repeated after the complete prayer. The text contrasts this with the traveler who intended to settle (iqamah) after two rak'ahs while having performed sajdah al-sahw. In that case, building is required to complete the now-full four-rak'ah fard. Even though building violates the wajib of performing sajdah al-sahw at the end, this lesser harm is tolerated to avoid the greater harm of invalidating the entire fard prayer. This follows the Hanafi legal maxim that a greater evil is removed by tolerating a lesser evil.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): continuing the prayer upon the existing opening takbir, joining another set of rak'ahs without a new tahrimah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person builds upon his prayer after performing sajdah al-sahw in the middle, what is the status of his sajdah al-sahw?
A) It is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) It is invalid and must be repeated after the complete prayer.
C) The entire prayer becomes invalid.
D) The sajdah is valid only if performed before salam.

Key Takeaway
Building after sajdah al-sahw is permissible but invalidates the sajdah; the traveler must build to preserve the fard, applying the maxim of lesser harm.

The Effect of Salam When Sajdah al-Sahw is Obligatory: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam's effect with three applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the effect of salam when sajdah al-sahw is obligatory, and apply this to the three issues of joining prayer, qahqaha, and niyyat al-iqamah.

Core Idea
Salam's effect is contingent when sajdah is owed: Shaykhayn say mu'allaq; Muhammad says no exit at all.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute on a subtle point of prayer invalidators. The question is whether the salam of a person who owes sajdah al-sahw actually removes him from the state of prayer (hurmat al-salah). The answer determines the validity of a latecomer joining the imam after salam, and extends to other issues like laughter breaking wudu. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how wajibat and conditions interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The question is: does the salam of a person on whom sajdah al-sahw is obligatory exit him from the prayer? The answer affects the validity of subsequent actions.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that salam exits on a contingent basis (mu'allaq): if sajdah is performed, the prayer continues; if not, it ends. Imam Muhammad (and Zufar) hold that salam does not exit at all; the prayer remains until sajdah is performed.
Note the terminology: 'ala sabil al-tawaqquf (contingent) vs. no exit.
3
Examine the proofs for each side
Shaykhayn rely on the hadith 'Tahlil al-salat al-taslim' – salam is inherently an exit, but the need to perform sajdah can block its effect if sajdah is actually done. Muhammad argues that sajdah compensates a deficiency; compensation requires the original to exist, so prayer must continue, hence salam cannot exit.
Both proofs are dalil naqli (hadith and qiyas).
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequences)
Three issues manifest this dispute: (1) a latecomer joining after the imam's salam; (2) loud laughter (qahqaha) breaking wudu after salam; (3) change of fard by intending iqamah in that state. According to Shaykhayn, each ruling depends on whether sajdah is actually performed; according to Muhammad, the ruling is independent of sajdah.
Focus on the first case as it is explicitly detailed in the passage.
5
Note the lack of explicit tarjih
Al-Hidayah presents both positions without definitively favoring one. Later Hanafi works may prefer one view; the mufta bihi depends on the context of fatwa.

شخص نے قہقہہ لگایا جس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہے تو اس قہقہہ سے امام محمد اور امام زفر کے نزدیک وضوٹوٹ جائے گا کیونکہ
If a person makes salam while sajdah al-sahw is obligatory upon him, then a man enters his prayer after the salam: if the imam performs sajdah, the follower has entered; otherwise, he has not. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He has entered whether the imam performs sajdah or not, because according to him the salam of one upon whom sajdah al-sahw is obligatory does not take him out of the prayer at all, since it (the sajdah) is obligatory to compensate the deficiency, so he must be within the state of the prayer's sanctity. According to them (the two), it takes him out on a contingent basis, because the salam is inherently a cause of exiting; it does not operate due to the need to perform the sajdah, so it does not become apparent without it, and there is no need to consider non-return. The difference appears in this and in the nullification of purity by loud laughter (qahqaha) and the change of the obligation (fard) by the intention of iqamah in this situation. Translation: A person made salam at the end of prayer while sajdah al-sahw was due, then after salam a person entered into his prayer. So if the imam performed sajdah, the follower entered; otherwise not. This ruling is according to the Shaykhayn, and Imam Muhammad said: He is inside whether the imam performs sajdah or not. Because according to Imam Muhammad, the salam of one on whom sajdah al-sahw is due does not take him out of the prayer at all. Because sajdah al-sahw is obligatory to complete the deficiency, so it is necessary that the person be within the sanctity of the prayer. According to the Shaykhayn, it takes him out on a contingent basis (mu'allaq), because salam is inherently an analyzer (i.e., something that causes exit), and (here) it will not operate because there is the need to perform the sajdah. So without the sajdah, it does not become apparent, and considering non-return, there is no need. The difference appears in this issue and in the breaking of purity by qahqaha and in the change of the fard by the intention of iqamah in this state. Explanation of the case: A person upon whom sajdah al-sahw was obligatory made salam. A man, after his salam, intended to follow him and joined his prayer. According to the Shaykhayn, the ruling is: If the imam performed sajdah al-sahw, then this follower has entered his prayer; if the imam did not perform sajdah al-sahw, then the one joining is not considered to have entered...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the commentary on Hidayah. The issue is whether the salam of a person who owes sajdah al-sahw removes him from the state of prayer (hurmat al-salah) or not. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold that the salam does not remove him at all; thus, the prayer continues and a latecomer can join even after salam, regardless of whether sajdah is performed. Their proof: sajdah al-sahw is obligatory to compensate a deficiency in the prayer; compensation requires the original act to still be present, so the prayer's sanctity must remain. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the salam removes him from the prayer on a contingent (mu'allaq) basis. If he then performs sajdah al-sahw, it shows the prayer was still continuing, and the salam did not fully exit; if he does not perform sajdah, then the salam did exit him. Their proof: the hadith 'Its tahlil (exiting) is the salam' shows salam inherently causes exit, but a preventing factor (mukhalif) is the need to perform sajdah; if sajdah is performed, the need is fulfilled and the salam's effect is blocked; if not, the need is absent and salam operates. Three issues manifest this dispute: (1) joining the prayer after salam, (2) loud laughter (qahqaha) breaking wudu after salam, and (3) the fard changing due to intention of iqamah.

Key Terms
على سبيل التوقف ('ala sabil al-tawaqquf): on a contingent basis; the salam removes the person from prayer only when the sajdah is not performed; if sajdah is performed, the removal is suspended
موقوفا (mu'allaqan): suspended; the ruling of salam is dependent on the subsequent performance of sajdah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), when can a follower join the prayer of an imam who has already made salam but owes sajdah al-sahw?
A) The follower can join regardless of whether the imam performs sajdah.
B) The follower can join only if the imam performs sajdah al-sahw.
C) The follower cannot join at all after salam.
D) The follower can join only if he also owes sajdah.

Key Takeaway
Salam's effect is contingent when sajdah al-sahw is obligatory: Shaykhayn tie the exit to actual performance of sajdah; Muhammad holds the prayer remains regardless.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Salutation of One Who Owes Sajdah al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of taslim when sajdah al-sahw is due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding whether the taslim of one who owes sajdah al-sahw exits the prayer, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to three practical scenarios.

Core Idea
The salutation of one who owes sajdah al-sahw: does it exit prayer or not? The Hanafi school has two positions with real practical consequences.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad (along with Imam Zufar) concerning the effect of the final salutation (taslim) when the prostration for forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is obligatory. The core question is whether the taslim immediately ends the sacred state of prayer (tahrimah) or whether its effect is suspended pending the performance of the sajdah. Understanding this dispute is essential because it affects the validity of actions performed after the taslim, such as joining the prayer as a follower, laughing, or changing one's intention of residency. The passage provides proofs for each position and extends the disagreement to three practical cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: does the taslim of a person who owes sajdah al-sahw remove him from the state of prayer (tahrimah) or not?
The dispute is about the effect of the taslim itself, not the obligation of the sajdah.
2
State the Two Positions
Clearly articulate the position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and that of Imam Muhammad (and Imam Zufar). The Shaykhayn hold that the taslim removes the person conditionally (mawqufan); Imam Muhammad holds that it does not remove him at all.
Remember 'mawquf' means the effect is suspended pending performance of the sajdah.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the dalil for each position. Imam Muhammad uses a rational argument: compensation for a deficiency requires the continued existence of the act. The Shaykhayn rely on the hadith 'tahliluha al-taslim' but introduce the concept of an obstacle (mani') that suspends the effect.
The hadith is zanni al-dalala; the dispute is about how to apply it in the presence of an obligation.
4
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequences (thamarah) of this dispute: the validity of a follower joining after the imam's taslim, whether laughter after taslim breaks wudu, and whether a traveler's intention of iqamah changes the prayer length.
These three cases are explicitly mentioned in the text.
5
Recognize the Absence of Tarjih
Observe that the passage does not give preference to either position; both are recorded as valid within the Hanafi school. This means both views are transmitted and may be relied upon depending on context.
In later Hanafi works, there may be a preferred view, but the text here presents the ikhtilaf neutrally.

نماز میں پیدا ہو گیا ہے اور تلافی کرنا اسی وقت متحقق ہو گا جب کہ وہ چیز موجود ہو جس کی تلافی کرنا مقصود ہے۔ یعنی سجدہ کے ذریعہ نماز کے نقصان کی تلافی اسی وقت ہوسکتی ہے جبکہ نماز موجود ہو اور نماز کا قیام بقا تحریمہ پر موقوف ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ جس پر سجدہ واجب ہے اس کا سلام اس کو احرام صلوۃ سے خارج نہیں کرتا بلکہ سلام کے باوجود تحریمہ باقی رہتا ہے پس جب سلام کے بعد تحریمہ باقی ہے تو سلام کے بعد اس کی اقتداء کرنا بھی درست ہوگا امام خواہ سہو ک سجدہ کرے یا نہ کرے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سلام بذات خود محلل یعنی نماز سے خارج کرنے والا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد نبوی ہے تحلیلها التسلیم نہاں اگر مانع پیش آ جائے تو لفظ سلام اپنا عمل نہیں کرے گا۔ اور مانع عمل سجدۂ سہو ادا کرنے کی ضرورت ہے پس اگر سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کیا تو چونکہ مانع پایا گیا اس لئے لفظ سلام اپنا عمل نہیں کرے گا یعنی اس مصلی کو نماز سے خارج نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اگر سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو چونکہ مانع تحلیل نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے لفظ سلام اپنا عمل کرے گا یعنی اس مصلی کو نماز سے خارج کر دے گا۔ اس دلیل سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ جس شخص پر سجدا سہو واجب ہو اس کا سلام اس کو علی سبیل التوقف نماز سے خارج کرتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام محمد اور شیخین کا اختلاف اس مسئلہ میں ظاہر ہوگا اور اس کے علاوہ دوسرے دو مسئلوں میں ظاہر ہوگا۔ ایک یہ کہ سلام کے بعد اس شخص نے قہقہہ لگایا جس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہے تو اس قہقہہ سے امام محمد اور امام زفر کے نزدیک وضوٹوٹ جائے گا کیونکہ نماز کے اندر قبہ پایا گیا اور شیخین کے نزدیک اگر سجدہ سہو کر لیا تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سجدہ کرنے کی وجہ سے قہقہ ہی پایا گیا ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سلام کے بعد اور سجدہ سہو سے پہلے مسافر نے اقامت کی نیت کی تو امام محمد کے نزدیک بجائے دور کعت کے چار رکعت ہو جائے گی خواہ سجدہ سہو کرے یا نہ کرے اور شیخین کے نزدیک اگر سجدہ سہو کر لیا تو اس کی قامت سے چار رکعت ہو جائے گی اور اگر سجدہ سہو نہ کیا تو چار رکعت نہیں ہوگی ۔ ( شرح نقایه )
Chapter of Prostration for Forgetfulness. Translation: A person gave the salutation at the end of his prayer while the prostration for forgetfulness was obligatory upon him. Then after giving the salutation, another person entered into this worshipper's prayer. So if the imam performed the prostration, then this follower has entered his prayer; otherwise not. This is the ruling according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and Imam Muhammad said that he is entered whether the imam performs the prostration or not. This is because according to Imam Muhammad, the salutation of a person on whom the prostration for forgetfulness is obligatory does not exit him from prayer at all. Because the prostration for forgetfulness became obligatory to complete the deficiency, so it is necessary that the person remain in the reverence of prayer. And according to the Shaykhayn, it will remove him on a conditional basis (bi sabil al-tawaqquf), because the salutation itself is an analyzer (muhallil) but it will not act here due to the need to perform the prostration. So without prostration it will not become apparent, and considering the absence of return, there is no need. And the difference appears in this issue and in the issue of ritual purity being broken by laughter, and in this state intending iqamah changing the obligation. Explanation of the scenario: A person on whom the prostration for forgetfulness was obligatory gave the salutation. A man after his salutation intended to follow him and entered into his prayer. According to the Shaykhayn, the ruling is that if the imam performed the prostration for forgetfulness, then this follower has entered his prayer, and if the imam did not perform the prostration for forgetfulness, then the one who joined is not considered to have entered his prayer. The issue whether the salutation of the one with forgetfulness removes the sanctity of prayer or not, and many other issues depend on this principle: does the salutation of one on whom the prostration for forgetfulness is obligatory remove the sanctity of prayer or not? Regarding this, the school of Imam Muhammad is that his salutation does not remove him from prayer, neither conditionally (mawqufan) nor absolutely (ghayr mawquf). This is also the saying of Imam Zufar. And the school of the Shaykhayn is that his salutation removes him from prayer conditionally. The meaning of conditionally is that if after the salutation he performed the prostration for forgetfulness, it will be said that the tahrimah (prohibition of prayer) remains, and when the tahrimah remains, the following of another worshipper is also correct. And if after the salutation he did not perform the prostration, it will be said that the tahrimah did not remain, and when the tahrimah did not remain, following is not correct. The proof of Imam Muhammad is that the prostration for forgetfulness is obligatory to compensate for the deficiency that occurred in the performed prayer, and compensation is only realized when the thing being compensated is present. That is, the compensation for the deficiency of prayer through prostration can only occur when the prayer exists, and the survival of prayer depends on the continuation of tahrimah. So it becomes clear that the salutation of one on whom prostration is obligatory does not remove him from the ihtiram (sanctity) of prayer; rather, despite the salutation, the tahrimah remains. So when after the salutation the tahrimah remains, then following him after the salutation is also correct, whether the imam performs the prostration for forgetfulness or not. The proof of the Shaykhayn is that the salutation itself is an analyzer (muhallil) that removes from prayer, as the prophetic instruction is: 'Its analysis is the salutation.' So if an obstacle occurs, the word salutation will not act. And the obstacle to its action is the need to perform the prostration for forgetfulness. So if after the salutation he performed the prostration for forgetfulness, then since the obstacle was found, the word salutation will not act, meaning it will not remove this worshipper from prayer. And if he did not perform the prostration for forgetfulness, then since the obstacle to analysis is not found, the word salutation will act, meaning it will remove this worshipper from prayer. From this proof it is established that the salutation of the person on whom the prostration for forgetfulness is obligatory removes him from prayer on a conditional basis (ala sabil al-tawaqquf). The author of Al-Hidayah says that the difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn will appear in this issue and in two other issues. One: A person who owes the prostration for forgetfulness laughs after the salutation. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar, his wudu will be broken because laughter occurred within the prayer. And according to the Shaykhayn, if he performed the prostration for forgetfulness, then his wudu will be broken, because due to performing the prostration, the laughter occurred within the prayer. The second issue: After the salutation and before the prostration for forgetfulness, a traveler intended iqamah (settling). According to Imam Muhammad, his prayer will become four rak'ahs instead of two, whether he performs the prostration for forgetfulness or not. And according to the Shaykhayn, if he performed the prostration for forgetfulness, then his intention of iqamah makes it four rak'ahs, and if he did not perform the prostration for forgetfulness, then it will not become four rak'ahs. (From Sharh al-Niqayah)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad (and Imam Zufar) versus the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the effect of the salutation (taslim) for a person who owes the obligatory prostration for forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The core question is: does the salutation remove the person from the sacred state of prayer (hurmah/tahrimah) or not? The scenario involves a person who gives salutation while sajdah al-sahw is due, and then another person joins his prayer after the salutation. According to the Shaykhayn, the salutation exits the person from prayer only conditionally: if he subsequently performs the sajdah, it retroactively confirms that he was still in prayer (tahrimah remained), so the follower's joining is valid; but if he does not perform the sajdah, the salutation is effective in ending the prayer, so the follower's joining is invalid. According to Imam Muhammad, the salutation never exits from prayer—whether sajdah is performed or not—because the sajdah is obligatory to compensate a deficiency in the prayer, and compensation requires the prayer's existence. Therefore, the tahrimah remains after salutation, making the follower's joining valid regardless. The text then extends the dispute to two other cases: (1) laughter (qahqahah) after salutation—whether it breaks wudu (it does if the person is still considered in prayer per Imam Muhammad, or only if sajdah is performed per Shaykhayn); and (2) a traveler intending iqamah after salutation—whether it changes the prayer from two to four rak'ahs (it does according to Imam Muhammad always; according to Shaykhayn only if sajdah is performed). The passage provides proofs for each position: Imam Muhammad argues rationally that compensation requires the continued existence of the compensated act; the Shaykhayn base their view on the hadith 'tahliluha al-taslim' (its analysis is the salutation), meaning the salutation inherently terminates prayer, but if an obstacle (the need for sajdah) prevents this termination, the salutation's effect is suspended until the obstacle is removed.

Key Terms
سہو (sahw): Forgetfulness or inadvertence in prayer that necessitates a compensatory prostration (sajdah al-sahw).
موقوفا (mawqufan): Conditionally; a ruling that is suspended pending the performance of an action (here, the sajdah).
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The state of being in prayer, initiated by takbir and characterized by prohibition of certain actions.
محلل (muhallil): That which makes permissible to exit from prayer; here, the salutation (taslim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person who owes sajdah al-sahw gives the salutation and then another person joins his prayer, when is the joining valid?
A) Always valid regardless of sajdah.
B) Valid only if the imam performs the sajdah after the salutation.
C) Valid only if the imam does not perform the sajdah.
D) Never valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school records a legitimate intra-madhhab dispute on whether the taslim of one who owes sajdah al-sahw exits the prayer conditionally (Shaykhayn) or not at all (Imam Muhammad), with three practical consequences.

Ruling on Giving Salam with Intention to End Prayer While Owing Sajdah
Ruling with proof: salam with intent to cut prayer when sajdah is owed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person who owes sajdah al-sahw gives salutation with the intention to end prayer, and explain the intra-school disagreement on the nature of the salutation.

Core Idea
If you owe sajdah al-sahw, your salam does not cut the prayer — even if you intend it to.

In this passage, Marghinani addresses a subtle case: a person who must perform sajdah al-sahw decides to end his prayer by giving the final salutation. The key ruling is that the salutation is ineffective because the prayer is not yet validly concluded. You'll learn why the Hanafi school unanimously agrees that such a salutation does not cut the prayer, and explore the internal difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the crucial condition
The act is giving salam with intention to cut prayer; the condition is that sajdah al-sahw is owed.
2
State the consensus ruling
By agreement of the Hanafi school, this salam is not qati' (not a cutter).
The text says 'bil-ittifaq'
3
Analyze the two positions on why it is not qati'
Imam Muhammad: salam not legislated as muhallil at all. Shaykhayn: salam is muhallil but conditional (mawquf).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
4
Determine the effect of the intention
The intention to cut is laghw (void) because it contradicts the mashru' (legislation).
Intention alone cannot change the legal nature of the act.
5
Conclude the practical ruling
The person must still perform sajdah al-sahw before any mufsid (invalidator).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يريد به قطع الصلوة وعليه سهو فعليه ان يسجد لسهوه لان هذا السلام غير قاطع ونيته تغيير للغة
جس شخص نے نماز قطع کرنے کے ارادے سے سلام پھیرا حالانکہ اس پر سہو بھی ہے۔ تو اس پر اپنے سہو کی وجہ سے سجدہ کرنا نکہ یہ سلام قاطع نماز نہیں ہے اور اس کی نیت مشروع کو متغیر کرنا ہے لہذ الغو ہوگی۔
صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص جس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہے اس نے نماز قطع کرنے کے عزم سے سلام پھیرا تو اس پر مفسد نے سے پہلے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ علیہ السہو کا سلام بالاتفاق قاطع نماز نہیں ہے امام محمد کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کے نزدیک محلل ( نماز سے خارج کرنیوالا) ہو کر مشروع نہیں ہوا اور شیخین کے نزدیک اگر چه محلل ہے لیکن موقوفا محلل ہے ھا۔ حاصل یہ کہ سلام قاطع نماز ہو کر مشروع نہیں ہوا ہے اور جو چیز قاطع نماز ہو کر مشروع نہ ہو وہ نماز قطع نہیں کر سکتی پس اس طع نہیں ہوگی رہی نماز قطع کرنے کی نیت سووہ خلاف مشروع ہونے کی وجہ سے لغو ہو جائے گی اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا۔
He intended to cut the prayer while he had forgetfulness (sahw). So it is obligatory upon him to prostrate for his forgetfulness because this salutation is not cutting (qati'), and his intention changes the language (mashru'). The explanation: A person who gave the salutation with the intention of cutting the prayer while he also had forgetfulness (sahw) — so upon him, due to his forgetfulness, it is obligatory to perform prostration, because this salutation is not a cutter of prayer, and his intention changes what is legislated, therefore it becomes void. The scenario: A person on whom sajdah al-sahw is wajib gave the salutation with the determination to cut the prayer. Then it is wajib upon him to perform sajdah al-sahw before any nullifier (mufsid), because the salutation of one with forgetfulness is, by agreement (bil-ittifaq), not a cutter of prayer. According to Imam Muhammad, it was not legislated as a muhallil (analyzer that takes out of prayer), and according to the Shaykhayn, although it is a muhallil, it is a conditional muhallil. The upshot is that the salutation was not legislated as a cutter of prayer, and something that is not legislated as a cutter of prayer cannot cut the prayer; so the prayer is not cut. As for the intention to cut the prayer, it becomes void due to being contrary to what is legislated; it is not given consideration.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about a person who, while owing sajdah al-sahw, intentionally gives the salutation (taslim) with the explicit intention to terminate the prayer. The ruling states that this salutation is not effective in cutting the prayer (i.e., it does not validly end the prayer), and therefore he must still perform the required sajdah al-sahw. The reason given is that the salutation of someone on whom sajdah is due is by consensus (bil-ittifaq) not a cutter of the prayer. The text then explains the differences between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn on this point: Imam Muhammad holds that the salutation was never legislated as an exit (muhallil) for such a person, while the Shaykhayn hold that it is a conditional exit (muhallil mawqufan), meaning it can only be effective if the sajdah is not performed. In either case, since the salutation is not legislated as a cutter, it does not cut the prayer. The intention to cut the prayer is itself contrary to the legislation (mashru'), so it is considered void (laghw) and has no effect. The practical consequence is that the person remains in prayer until he performs the sajdah, and any deliberate nullifier (mufsid) before that would invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
قطع الصلوة (qat' al-salah): Terminating the prayer intentionally, either by a valid exit (taslim) or by an invalidating act.
بالاتفاق (bil-ittifaq): By agreement (consensus) within the Hanafi school on this point.
لغو (laghw): Void, of no legal effect; here, the intention to cut the prayer is laghw because it contradicts the legislation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person who owes sajdah al-sahw gives salutation with the intention to end his prayer, what is the ruling?
A) His prayer is cut and he does not need to perform sajdah.
B) His prayer is cut but he must still perform sajdah.
C) His prayer is not cut, and he must perform sajdah.
D) His prayer is nullified by the intention, and he must repeat it.

Key Takeaway
When sajdah al-sahw is wajib, the salutation does not cut the prayer – even if one intends to end it.

First-Time Doubt in Rak'ahs: Restarting the Prayer
Ruling with hadith proof for first-time doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a first-time doubt in the number of rak'ahs, identify the hadith proof, and distinguish between first-time doubt and habitual doubt.

Core Idea
First-time doubt in rak'ahs triggers a wajib to restart the entire prayer.

A worshipper suddenly loses count mid-prayer: three or four rak'ahs? If this is the first time such doubt has occurred, the Hanafi school rules that the prayer must be started anew. This lesson unpacks the hadith proof and the critical distinction between first-time and habitual doubt that changes the ruling entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Locate the specific case: a person doubts whether he has prayed three or four rak'ahs, and this doubt is occurring for the first time (either in this prayer, habitually, or in his life—the exact meaning is debated).
The Arabic phrase 'awwal ma 'arada lahu' signals the first-time condition.
2
Extract the Ruling
The ruling is 'ista'nafa'—he must restart the prayer entirely. Note that this is a wajib, not a sunnah, because the dalil (hadith) contains an imperative.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
3
Examine the Dalil
Find the hadith: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer how much he prayed, let him restart the prayer.' Identify the operative phrase 'falyastaqbil' which gives the wajib ruling.
The hadith is sunnah ahad, thus zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, but still binding for a ruling of wujub.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note the different interpretations of 'first time': (a) forgetfulness is not habitual, (b) first forgetfulness in this specific prayer, (c) first in a lifetime. The preferred view (al-Sarkhasi) is that it means the person is not a habitual forgetter.
This ikhtilaf affects who is subject to the ruling but does not change the basic ruling for non-habitual doubters.
5
Distinguish from Habitual Doubt
Contrast with the rule for kathir al-shakk (habitual doubter), who should rely on the certainty (the lesser number) and perform sajdah al-sahw, not restart.
The source chunk does not elaborate on habitual doubt, but the distinction is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فى صلوته فلم يدر أثلثا صلى ام اربعا و ذلك اول ماعرض له استأنف لقوله عليه السلام اذاشک صلاته انه کم صلى فليستقبل الصلوة
جس نے اپنی نماز کے اندر شک کیا اس کو معلوم نہیں کہ تین رکعتیں پڑھیں یا چار پڑھیں اور یہ شک پہلا شک ہے جو اس کو ں نئے سرے سے نماز پڑھے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی اپنی نماز کے اندر یہ شک کرتے کہ کتنی پڑھی
پڑھے۔
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی کو اپنی نماز میں یہ شک پیش آیا کہ تین رکھتیں ہوئیں یا چار رکعتیں ہوئیں اور یہ شک پہلی ہی بار پیش آیا رت میں نماز از سر نو پڑھے۔ دلیل صاحب ہدایہ کی پیش کردہ حدیث رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ متن کی عبارت اول سے کیا مراد ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اس جملہ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ سہو اس کی عادت نہیں ہے بلکہ کبھی ہے یہ مطلب ہر گز نہیں ہے کہ مر بھر بھی سہوہی نہیں ہوا ہے۔ شمس الائمہ سرخسی کی یہی رائے ہے۔
ام نے کہا ہے کہ مراد یہ ہے کہ اس نماز میں پہلا سہو یہی ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ زندگی میں پہلی مرتبہ یہی سہو پیش آیا
In his prayer, he did not know whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, and that was the first time it occurred to him. He must start anew (ista'nafa) because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer how much he prayed, let him restart the prayer.' The person who doubted in his prayer, not knowing whether he prayed three rak'ahs or four, and this doubt is the first doubt that occurred to him, then he should perform the prayer anew. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer about how much he prayed, let him pray (restart).' The issue: A worshipper experienced doubt in his prayer whether three rak'ahs were prayed or four, and this doubt occurred for the first time; then he should pray the prayer anew. The proof is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, presented by the author of Al-Hidayah. As for the meaning of 'first' in the matn (text), some mashayikh have said that this phrase means that forgetfulness (sahw) is not his habit but occurs occasionally; it does not mean that no forgetfulness has ever happened to him before. This is the view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi. Others have said that it means that this forgetfulness is the first in this prayer, and some have said that it is the first forgetfulness to occur in his life.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific case of doubt (shakk) in the number of rak'ahs of a prayer—whether one has prayed three or four. The ruling is that if this is the first time such doubt has occurred (either in the prayer, or as a habitual occurrence, or in the worshipper's life—there is a difference of interpretation), then the worshipper must restart the entire prayer (ista'nafa). The proof is a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructs: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer about how much he has prayed, let him restart the prayer.' The text then discusses the meaning of 'first time' (awwal ma 'arada lahu). Some scholars, including Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, interpret it as meaning that forgetfulness is not the person's habit; that is, he is not someone who frequently experiences doubts. Others interpret it as the first occurrence of forgetfulness in that particular prayer, and yet others as the first forgetfulness in the person's entire life. The common implication is that this ruling applies only to one who is not habitually forgetful; the habitual doubter has different rules (relying on the majority of certainty).

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Doubt in the number of rak'ahs where one cannot determine how many have been performed.
استئناف (ista'naf): To start anew; here, to begin the entire prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a person do if he doubts whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs and this is the first time he experiences such doubt?
A) He must choose the lesser number and perform sajdah al-sahw.
B) He must restart the entire prayer from the beginning.
C) He can continue based on what he thinks is more likely.
D) He should perform sajdah al-sahw and then complete the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A first-time doubt in the number of rak'ahs requires the worshipper to restart the entire prayer; this applies only to non-habitual forgetters.

Salam with Intention to Cut Prayer When Sajdah Sahw is Due
Ruling on salam intended to end prayer while sajdah sahw is obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effect of an intentional salam given when sajdah sahw is due and distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn on whether the salam is a valid exit.

Core Idea
Intention to end prayer does not make the salam valid; the salam of one who owes sajdah sahw does not cut the prayer.

This passage addresses a tricky scenario: a person who is obligated to perform sajdah sahw gives salam with the explicit intention of ending the prayer. Does the prayer end? The Hanafi school unanimously says no, but there is an internal subtlety about the legal nature of that salam. Let's explore the reasoning and the difference between Imam Muhammad's view and that of the Shaykhayn.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the ruling
Identify the situation: a person is obligated to perform sajdah sahw (due to forgetfulness) and deliberately gives salam with the intention of cutting the prayer. The ruling is that the prayer is not cut; sajdah sahw must still be performed.
2
Identify the consensus
Note that the salam of a person who has forgetfulness (upon whom sajdah sahw is wajib) is unanimously not considered a cutter (qati') of the prayer.
3
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that the salam is not a valid exit (muhallil) at all because it was not placed in its proper context (not mashru'). The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider it a valid exit but suspended (mawquf), meaning it becomes effective only after sajdah sahw is performed.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference lies in whether the person is considered to have exited the prayer before sajdah or not. However, both agree that the prayer is not immediately cut and sajdah sahw is wajib. The intention to cut is futile.
5
Understand the principle
Intentions cannot override the shariah's designation of valid acts. The salam is only the legitimate exit (muhallil) when placed correctly; otherwise, it is ineffective (laghw).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز کو ختم کرنے کے لئے سلام پھیرا، اس پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہے تو سجدہ سہو کر لے يريد به قطع الصلوة وعليه سهو فعليه ان يسجد لسهوه لان هذا السلام غير قاطع ونيته تغيير للغت جس شخص نے نماز قطع کرنے کے ارادے سے سلام پھیرا حالانکہ اس پر سہو بھی ہے۔ تو اس پر اپنے سہو کی وجہ سے سجدہ کرنا نکہ یہ سلام قاطع نماز نہیں ہے اور اس کی نیت مشروع کو متغیر کرنا ہے لہذ الغو ہوگی۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص جس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہے اس نے نماز قطع کرنے کے عزم سے سلام پھیرا تو اس پر مفسد نے سے پہلے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ علیہ السہو کا سلام بالاتفاق قاطع نماز نہیں ہے امام محمد کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کے نزدیک محلل ( نماز سے خارج کرنیوالا) ہو کر مشروع نہیں ہوا اور شیخین کے نزدیک اگر چه محلل ہے لیکن موقوفا محلل ہے ھا۔ حاصل یہ کہ سلام قاطع نماز ہو کر مشروع نہیں ہوا ہے اور جو چیز قاطع نماز ہو کر مشروع نہ ہو وہ نماز قطع نہیں کر سکتی پس اس طع نہیں ہوگی رہی نماز قطع کرنے کی نیت سووہ خلاف مشروع ہونے کی وجہ سے لغو ہو جائے گی اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا۔
He said the salam intending to cut the prayer, and upon him is forgetfulness, so he should perform sajdah for his forgetfulness, because this salam is not a cutter (of prayer) and his intention is to change the legitimate. The person who gave salam with the intention of cutting the prayer while he has forgetfulness, then upon him is to perform sajdah for his forgetfulness, because this salam is not a cutter of prayer, and his intention to change the legitimate is void. The scenario: a person upon whom sajdah sahw is obligatory gave salam with the determination to cut the prayer, then upon him it is wajib to perform sajdah sahw before the invalidator, because the salam of one who has forgetfulness is, by consensus, not a cutter of prayer. According to Imam Muhammad, because it did not become a legitimate exit (from prayer), and according to the Shaykhayn, although it is an exit, it is a suspended exit. The conclusion: the salam has not been legitimated as a cutter of prayer, and whatever is not legitimated as a cutter of prayer cannot cut the prayer. Thus the prayer is not cut. As for the intention to cut the prayer, it becomes void due to being against the legitimate and is not considered.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who is obligated to perform sajdah sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) but instead gives salam (salutation) with the explicit intention of ending the prayer. The author clarifies that the salam does not actually terminate the prayer because it is not the proper concluding salam; rather, the prayer remains valid and the sajdah sahw must be performed. The key point is that the salam is not recognized as a valid exit (muhallil) at that moment. Imam Muhammad holds that the salam is not a valid exit at all because it is not legitimated as such, whereas the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider it a valid exit but suspended (mawquf), meaning it becomes effective only after the sajdah sahw is performed. The practical consequence is that the prayer is not nullified, and the intention to cut it is disregarded as futile. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle that actions are judged by intentions, but intentions cannot override the shariah's designation of valid acts. The hadith 'The analysis of prayer is the salam' is implicitly referenced to show that salam is the legitimate exitor only when placed in its proper context.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
محلل (muhallil): That which legally exits one from the state of prayer.
لغو (laghw): Void, futile, of no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is nullified immediately.
B) The salam is valid and the prayer ends.
C) The prayer is not cut and sajdah sahw must still be performed.
D) Both the salam and the sajdah are invalid.

Key Takeaway
A salam given with intention to end prayer while sajdah sahw is due does NOT terminate the prayer; sajdah sahw remains wajib and must be performed.

Frequent Doubt in Prayer: Build on Predominant Opinion or Lesser
Ruling with proof for frequent doubt in prayer: two cases with hadith and rational evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule to determine whether a frequent doubter should build on predominant opinion or the lesser number of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Frequent doubt does not require repeating; act on predominant opinion if present, else build on the lesser.

This lesson addresses a common concern for those who frequently doubt the number of rak'ahs they have prayed. The Hanafi school provides a clear, practical ruling that avoids hardship while maintaining the integrity of the prayer. You will learn the two scenarios—when a predominant opinion exists and when it does not—and the prophetic evidence behind each.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish frequent from occasional doubt
Identify that the ruling applies only to a person who frequently doubts (kathir al-shakk), not to a first-time doubter. The first doubter must restart the prayer; the frequent doubter follows the rule below.
Frequent is often defined as doubting in every prayer or most prayers.
2
Determine if predominant opinion exists
Ask: Does the worshiper have a strong conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) about the number of rak'ahs? If yes, he acts on that opinion and completes the prayer, then performs sajdah sahw.
The proof is the hadith: 'When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct and complete upon it...'
3
If no predominant opinion, build on the lesser
If the worshiper has no strong guess (e.g., uncertain between 3 and 4), he builds on the lesser number (bina 'ala al-aqall) and treats it as the actual count. He sits for tashahhud in every position that could be the last rak'ah.
The proof is the hadith: '...if he does not know three or four, let him build on three.'
4
Understand the rational proof
If the frequent doubter were required to restart every time, it would cause severe hardship (haraj). The law therefore permits acting on predominant opinion or the lesser to remove hardship, in line with the principle of ease.
This is a classic application of istihsan and raf' al-haraj.
5
Apply to a scenario
Practice applying the rule: A person frequently doubts whether he prayed 3 or 4 rak'ahs in Dhuhr. He has no strong feeling. He should complete the prayer as 3 rak'ahs, perform sajdah sahw, and do the obligatory sitting at the end of the 3rd (and also after the 4th if he adds one? No, he sits after the 3rd and then stands for the 4th, but since he built on 3, he actually has only 3? Wait, the process: he built on 3, so he prays 3 rak'ahs, then sits for tashahhud (as if it's the end), then he is unsure if he should continue. Actually, the rule: he builds on the lesser, so he assumes he has only 3 and continues to complete the prayer accordingly. One method: pray the remaining rak'ahs based on the lesser and perform sajdah sahw. The explanation in the text says he should sit in every position that could be the end, so after the 3rd rak'ah he sits, then stands for the 4th, but since he is uncertain, he should treat it as if he has 3 and then add a 4th? This is complex. For simplicity, the student should understand the two-step process.
Consult a detailed fiqh manual for the exact performance of sajdah sahw in this case.

And if he has no predominant opinion, he acts on the lesser, e.g., if he doubts between three and four and has no strong guess, he considers it as three. The proof is the hadith: '...build on the lesser.' Imam Tirmidhi narrated this hadith with these words: from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, he heard the Prophet say: 'When one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build on one; if he does not know two or three, let him build on two; if he does not know three or four, let him build on three.' And as for 'restarting with salam,' the author's purpose is that if one intends to restart the prayer, it is better to cut the current doubtful prayer with salam, i.e., say salam properly and restart, rather than cutting with speech, because speech is invalidating. The prophetic hadith: 'Its analysis (exit) is the salam.' So since sharia and hadith have established salam as the exit from prayer...
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and explanation of the Hanafi position on frequent doubt (kathir al-shakk) during prayer. The text presents two scenarios for a person who frequently doubts the number of rak'ahs: (1) If he has a predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) about how many he has prayed, he should act upon it and complete his prayer accordingly. The proof is the hadith from Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) that the Prophet said: 'When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct (falyataharr al-sawab) and complete upon it, then say salam and perform two prostrations.' A rational argument (dalil 'aqli) is also given: ordering repetition for every doubt would cause hardship (haraj), so predominant opinion is allowed to remove hardship. (2) If he has no predominant opinion, he must build on the lesser number (bina 'ala al-aqall). For example, if he doubts between three and four, he treats it as three. The proof is the hadith from Tirmidhi with the chain from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf: the Prophet instructed building on the lesser number in steps (one, two, three). The text also discusses that when building on the lesser, the worshiper must sit (for tashahhud) in every position where he suspects it might be the end of the prayer, to ensure he does not miss the obligatory sitting (qada). Additionally, the commentator notes that if one decides to restart the prayer (istinaf), it is better to cut the current prayer by saying the proper salam rather than by speaking, because salam is the legitimate exit (muhallil) from prayer, whereas speech invalidates it. This is based on the hadith 'The analysis of prayer is the salam.'

Key Terms
ظن غالب (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or strong conjecture about the number of rak'ahs prayed.
بناء على الاقل (bina 'ala al-aqall): Building on the lesser number of rak'ahs when no predominant opinion exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Build on four and continue.
D) Choose arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
Frequent doubt in prayer is resolved by acting on predominant opinion if present, otherwise building on the lesser number.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Frequent Doubt in Prayer: Dominant Opinion vs. Certainty
Ruling on frequent doubt: build on dominant opinion or minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a frequent doubter in prayer and apply the rule of dominant opinion or building on the minimum.

Core Idea
When in frequent doubt, act on your strongest opinion; if none, assume the lesser number.

Frequent doubt (kathir al-shakk) is a common challenge in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling to avoid hardship: the worshipper may rely on his dominant opinion (zann ghalib) to determine the number of rak'ahs, and if no opinion prevails, he must build on certainty, i.e., the minimum. This lesson examines the textual evidence and the key rules for managing such doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and conditions
What is the ruling for frequently doubted rak'ahs? What defines 'frequent doubt'? Note that the ruling applies only to one who is frequently doubtful, not occasional doubt.
Frequent doubt is defined as doubt occurring in three consecutive prayers or in most of one's prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: the first commands seeking the correct opinion (falyataharra al-sawab) for building on dominant opinion; the second commands building on the lesser number (fal-yabni 'ala al-aqall) when no dominant opinion exists.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form (فَلْيَتَحَرَّ, فَلْيَبْنِ) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. Thus, acting on dominant opinion or building on the minimum is wajib, not merely recommended.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that one must always build on certainty (the minimum) even if a dominant opinion exists, because certainty is not overridden by doubt. Understand the practical difference.
5
Determine the practical application
When building on the minimum, the worshipper must sit for tashahhud after every rak'ah that could possibly be the last. Also, if intending to start anew, exiting with salam is obligatory; speech invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
وان كان يعرض له كثير ابنى على اكبر رايه لقوله عليه السلام من شك في صلوته فليتحر الصواب وان لم يكن له رأى بنى على اليقين لقوله عليه السلام من شك فى صلوته فلم يدر أ ثلثا صلى ام اربعا بنى على الاقل والاستقبال بالسلام اولى لانه عرف محللا دون الكلام ومجرد النتية تلغو وعند البناء على الاقل يقعده فى كل موضع يتوهم آخر صلاته كيلا يصير تاركا فرض القعدة والله اعلم
ترجمہ اور اگر اس کو یہ شک بہت پیش آتا ہو تو اپنی غالب رائے پر بناء کرے کیونکہ اللہ کے حبیب صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جو کوئی نماز میں شک کرے تو وہ ٹھیک بات کے لئے دل سے تحری کرے۔ اور اس کی کچھ رائے یہ ہوتی یہ یقین پر عمل کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا جس نے اپنی نماز میں شک کیا ہے اس کو معلوم نہیں کہ اس نے تین رکعت پڑھیں یا چار تو کمتر پر بناء کرنے اور نئے سرے سے سلام کے ساتھ پڑھنا اولی ہے۔ کیونکہ سلام محلل ہو کر معلوم ہوا ہے نہ کہ کلام اور خالی نیت لغو ہو گی اور اقل پر بناء کرنے کی صورت میں ہر اس مقام پر جس کی آخری نماز تو ہم کرے قعدہ کرے تا کہ وہ فرض قعدہ کا ترک کرنے والا نہ ہو جائے واللہ اعلم ۔
Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. And if he is frequently afflicted with doubt, he builds upon his strongest opinion, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him seek the correct opinion.' And if he has no opinion, he builds upon certainty, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever doubts in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, builds upon the lesser.' And starting anew with salām is preferable because salām is recognized as the legal exit [from prayer], not speech. Mere intention is futile. And when building upon the lesser, he sits in every position where he suspects it might be the end of his prayer, so that he does not abandon the obligatory sitting. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw and deals with the case of someone who frequently experiences doubt (kathir al-shakk) during prayer. The ruling is that if he has a dominant opinion (zann ghalib) about the number of rak'ahs he has performed, he should act upon that opinion. This is based on the hadith narrated by Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded: 'When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct opinion and complete his prayer based on it, then say salām and perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' The rational basis is that requiring a full repetition every time would cause hardship (haraj), and hardship is to be removed. If the person has no dominant opinion, then he must build upon certainty, i.e., the lesser number (al-aqall). For example, if he doubts between three and four rak'ahs, he considers it as three. This is based on another hadith from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf (may Allah be pleased with him) specifically for the case of no inclination. The text further advises that if he intends to start the prayer anew, it is better to exit the current prayer with salām rather than with speech, because salām is the legislated exit (muhallil) while speech nullifies the prayer. Mere intention (niyyah) without an accompanying invalidating action is ineffective. When building upon the lesser, the worshipper must sit for tashahhud after every rak'ah where it is possible that it could be the last rak'ah, so that he does not miss an obligatory sitting. For instance, if he considers the current rak'ah as the first but it might actually be the second, he sits after finishing it because the second rak'ah requires sitting. This careful approach ensures the obligatory and necessary sittings are observed.

Key Terms
الظن الغالب (al-zann al-ghalib): The strong inclination of the heart towards one possibility, which is relied upon in legal rulings when certainty is unavailable.
البناء على الأقل (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall): To assume the smaller number of rak'ahs when in doubt and have no dominant opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a frequent doubter has a dominant opinion that he prayed 3 rak'ahs in Maghrib (which is 3 rak'ahs), what should he do?
A) Build on 2 because it is the minimum.
B) Build on 3 and perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) Repeat the prayer because doubt invalidates it.
D) Ignore the doubt and continue without any action.

Key Takeaway
In frequent doubt, the worshipper acts on dominant opinion; if none, he builds on the minimum, and in both cases performs sajdah al-sahw.

Prayer of the Sick: Ruling on Sitting When Unable to Stand
Ruling on the sick who cannot stand in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot stand in prayer and identify the primary evidence (dalil) and its legal implication (wajh al-dalalah).

Core Idea
Standing is a pillar, but the sick are excused; they pray sitting with full ruku and sujud.

This lesson addresses the prayer of a sick person who cannot stand. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the hadith of Imran bin Husain. You will learn when sitting is permitted and the evidence that establishes this concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that a sick person who is unable to stand (qiyam) may pray sitting (qa'idan) while performing full ruku and sujud. This is a concession that replaces the normal obligation of standing.
The ruling is specific to genuine inability due to fear of harm, severe weakness, or dizziness.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Imran bin Husain (may Allah be pleased with him), where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side making gestures.' This is a sound (sahih) hadith, though ahad in transmission.
The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari and others. It is classified as zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalalah in its explicit permission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'صَلِّ قَائِمًا' establishes the obligation of standing for the able. The conditional clauses 'فَإِنْ لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ فَقَاعِدًا' demonstrate that when standing is impossible, sitting becomes the valid substitute. The phrase 'لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ' is understood as inability due to genuine harm or extreme difficulty.
Hanafi usul: the imperative indicates obligation, and the conditional exception allows the next form. The sequence shows a gradual relaxation.
4
Note the consensus
This ruling is agreed upon by all major schools (muttafaq alayh). There is no significant ikhtilaf on the basic principle that the sick are excused from standing when unable.
The rational basis (dalil aqli) is also cited: 'obedience is according to capacity' (al-ta'a bi-hasab al-taqah).
5
Evaluate the practical application
The mufta bihi position is clear: sit if unable to stand; if sitting is also impossible, then lie on the side with gestures (ima'). The sick person should not delay prayer but perform it to the best of ability.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah from the six core books.

ترجمہ (یہ) باب بیمار آدمی کی نماز ( کے بیان ) میں ہے
قیام پر قادر نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے
جمہ مریض جب کھڑا ہونے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عمران بن حصین (کاو بواسیر کا مرض تھا) کو فرمایا تھا کہ کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے پھر اگر تجھ کو اس کی استطاعت نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر پڑھ پھر استطاعت نہ ہو تو کروٹ پر اس حال میں کہ تو اشارہ کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اطاعت بقدر طاقت ہوتی ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بیمار آدمی اگر کھڑا ہونے پر قادر نہ ہو بایں طور کہ کھڑا ہونے میں صحت یابی کی تاخیر کا ڈر ہے یا کھڑا ہو پڑھنے میں ضعف شدید لاحق ہوتا ہے یا در دو غیرہ ہوتا ہے تو اس کے واسطے قیام کا ترک کرنا جائز ہے اور یہ شخص بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدے ن نماز ادا کرے۔ دلیل عمران بن حصین رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے قال کنت بی بواسیر فسألت النبی صلی الله وسلم عن الصلاة فقال صل قائما فان لم تيستطع فقاعد افان لم تستطع فعلی جنب
Chapter of the Prayer of the Sick. The sick person, if he is unable to stand, prays sitting, making ruku and sujud, due to his (peace be upon him) saying to Imran bin Husain: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side, making gestures.' And because obedience is according to capacity.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on the prayer of the sick (Salat al-Mareed) and states the fundamental ruling: if a sick person is unable to stand (qiyam) for prayer, he may pray sitting (qa'idan) while performing the full ruku and sujud. The inability is determined by fear of delayed recovery, severe weakness, or dizziness. The primary evidence is the hadith of Imran bin Husain (may Allah be pleased with him) who suffered from hemorrhoids. He asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer, and the Prophet replied ordering standing first, then sitting if unable, then lying on the side with gestures (ima') if even sitting is impossible. This hadith establishes a sequential concession: the most complete form is taken if possible; otherwise, the next level. The rational basis (dalil aqli) is that obedience is required according to one's capacity (al-ta'a bi-hasab al-taqah), as implied in the Quranic verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' This principle allows for relaxation of the obligation of standing when it is genuinely harmful or impossible.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing upright in prayer, which is a pillar (rukn) for those able to do so.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body for ruku and sujud when unable to perform actual movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is ill and cannot stand without severe dizziness. According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Pray lying down with gestures.
B) Delay the prayer until he recovers.
C) Pray sitting with ruku and sujud.
D) Not pray at all because of the difficulty.

Key Takeaway
A sick person who cannot stand may pray sitting with full ruku and sujud, based on the hadith of Imran bin Husain.

Ruling: Sick Person Unable to Stand Prays Sitting
Opening of the chapter on sick person's prayer with first ruling and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a sick person who cannot stand in prayer and identify the conditions that make it permissible to omit standing.

Core Idea
A sick person who genuinely cannot stand without harm omits standing and prays sitting with bowing and prostration.

This lesson opens the chapter on the prayer of the sick. The central ruling is that when standing becomes genuinely impossible due to illness, the obligation of standing is lifted and the prayer is performed sitting, while keeping bowing and prostration intact. We will examine the precise conditions that trigger this concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the obligatory prayer of a sick person. The ruling: if unable to stand, he prays sitting, performing ruku' and sujud as normal.
2
Define inability ('ajz)
Inability is not mere difficulty; it must be genuine: fear of delayed recovery, severe weakness, or pain that prevents standing. Understand the threshold.
Hanafi view: inability is determined by a reasonable fear or severe hardship.
3
Identify the consequence
When the condition of inability is met, standing is waived (not makruh or haram to sit), and the prayer in sitting posture is valid.
The ruling applies to fard prayers, sunnah, etc.
4
Note the preservation of ruku' and sujud
Unlike the case of extreme inability (where gestures suffice), here the sick person must still bow and prostrate normally while sitting.
This distinguishes this level from higher levels of inability mentioned in the hadith.

Chapter of the prayer of the sick. (This) chapter is about the prayer of a sick person. If the sick person is unable to stand, he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, due to his (peace be upon him) statement to Imran bin Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side, gesturing.' And because obedience is according to ability. The summary: When a sick person becomes unable to stand – such that standing would delay recovery, cause severe weakness, or pain – then it is permissible for him to omit standing and he should pray sitting with bowing and prostration. The proof is the hadith of Imran bin Husayn (may Allah be pleased with him): 'I had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Imam Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' The author of Hidayah mentioned the rational proof: obedience is according to ability, so do it as much as possible and in the manner possible. Benefits: If the sick person can stand slightly, e.g., to recite one verse or say the takbir, but cannot stand fully, then he is commanded to stand that much, then when unable, sit. Similarly, if he can stand by leaning on a wall or staff, it is not permissible for him to omit standing. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the prayer of the sick. It first presents a ruling: if a sick person cannot stand due to fear of delayed recovery, severe weakness, or pain, then standing is omitted and he prays sitting, performing bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) normally. The ruling is supported by two proofs: first, a hadith from Imran bin Husayn, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed prayer standing, then sitting, then on the side, then lying on the back – each step for decreasing ability. Second, a rational principle: obedience is proportionate to ability (taklif bi hasab al-taqah). The commentary then discusses two applications: (a) if the person can stand for a short duration (e.g., reciting one verse or takbir), he must perform that much standing and then sit; (b) if he can stand with support (wall or staff), he must do so and cannot omit standing entirely. Both follow from the same principle – the obligation of standing is not waived when minimal ability exists.

Key Terms
عجز المريض عن القيام ('ajz al-marīḍ 'an al-qiyām): Inability of the sick person to stand without harm or severe difficulty.
الطاعة بحسب الطاقة (al-ṭā'ah bi-ḥasab al-ṭāqah): Obedience is according to ability; a principle that obligations are scaled to capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Feeling tired after a long day.
B) Fear that standing will delay recovery from illness.
C) Preference to sit because it is more comfortable.
D) Inability to focus due to noise.

Key Takeaway
A sick person may omit standing in prayer only when genuine inability is established by fear of harm, severe weakness, or pain.
