Proofs and Applications: Hadith and Principle of Obedience According to Ability
Opening of the chapter on sick person's prayer with proofs and furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hadith of Imran bin Husayn and the rational principle 'obedience is according to ability' as proofs for the sick person's prayer, and apply them to cases of partial standing.

Core Idea
The hadith directly commands prayer according to ability, and the rational principle ensures that the concession covers even cases of partial ability.

In this lesson we examine the evidence supporting the sick person's concession. The hadith from Imran bin Husayn provides a clear sequence of postures based on ability. Additionally, the principle of 'obedience according to ability' rationalizes the ruling. We will also see how these proofs extend to specific scenarios where the sick person has partial ability to stand.

Guided Path
1
Examine the hadith text
Read the hadith: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Note the imperative and the conditional.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.
2
Extract the legal principle
The hadith establishes that the obligation of standing is graded according to ability. The command to pray standing is not absolute when inability exists.
The principle 'obedience is according to ability' is the rational basis.
3
Apply to partial standing
If a sick person can stand for only one verse, he must stand for that much and then sit for the rest. This follows from the hadith and the rational principle.
The principle that the obligation is proportional to ability mandates performing what is possible.
4
Apply to standing with support
If a sick person can stand by leaning on a wall or staff, he must do so. The ability to stand with support is still ability, so the concession does not apply.
This shows that the threshold of 'inability' is strict; mere difficulty is not enough.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المريض
ترجمہ (یہ) باب بیمار آدمی کی نماز ( کے بیان ) میں ہے

قیام پر قادر نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے
عجز المريض عن القيام صلى قاعدا يركع ويسجد لقوله عليه السلام لعمران بن حصين صل قائما فان تستطع فقاعدا فان لم تستطع فعلى الجنب تؤمى ايماء ولان الطاعة بحسب الطاقة

جمہ مریض جب کھڑا ہونے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عمران بن حصین کاو بواسیر کا مرض تھا) کو فرمایا تھا کہ کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے پھر اگر تجھ کو اس کی استطاعت نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر پڑھ پھر استطاعت نہ ہو تو کروٹ دارانحالیکہ تو اشارہ کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اطاعت بقدر طاقت ہوتی ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بیمار آدمی اگر کھڑا ہونے پر قادر نہ ہو بایں طور کہ کھڑا ہونے میں صحت یابی کی تاخیر کا ڈر ہے یا کھڑا ہو پڑھنے میں ضعف شدید لاحق ہوتا ہے یا در دو غیرہ ہوتا ہے تو اس کے واسطے قیام کا ترک کرنا جائز ہے اور یہ شخص بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدے ن نماز ادا کرے۔ دلیل عمران بن حصین رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے قال کنت بی بواسیر فسألت النبی صلی الله وسلم عن الصلاة فقال صل قائما فان لم تيستطع فقاعد افان لم تستطع فعلی جنب ، امام نسائی نے یہ لفظ زیادہ کیا لما لم تستطع فمستلقيا لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا عمران بن حصین نے کہا ہے کہ مجھ کو بواسیر کا مرض تھا میں نے سید الانبیاء صلى الله عليه وسلم سے اس حالت میں نماز کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ کھڑے ہو کر نماز ادا کر لو اور اگر اس کی مانت ذکر کی ہے ہو بیٹھ کر ادا کر لو اور اگر اس کی بھی طاقت نہ ہو تو کروٹ پر اور اگر اس کی بھی طاقت نہ ہو تو چت لیٹ کر ادا کرو اللہ تعالی کسی کواس کی مان فاخذه سے زیادہ مکلف نہیں کرتے ۔

سجود
نے اس کے
صاحب ہدایہ نے عقلی دلیل بیان کرتے ہوئے اس جملہ کا حاصل ذکر کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا ہے کہ طاعت بقدر طاقت ہوتی ہے تین لائے تو و قدر ممکن ہو اور جس طرح ممکن ہو اسی طرح اور اسی قدر طاعت کر لے۔ فوائد اگر مریض تھوڑے سے قیام پر قادر ہے مثلا ایک آیت پڑھنے کی مقدار یا تکبیر کہنے کی مقدار پورے قیام پر قادر نہیں ہے بات پر محمد ہی مقدار قیام کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ جب عاجز ہو جائے تو بیٹھ جائے کیونکہ طاقت کے مطابق ہی طاعت ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر مرین ہی کے لئے لگا کر یا لاٹھی پر ٹیک لگا کر کھڑا ہو سکتا ہو تو اس کے لئے قیام کو ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم رکوع اور سجدہ کی طاقت نہ ہو تو اشارہ سے رکوع سجدہ کرے
Chapter of the prayer of the sick. (This) chapter is about the prayer of a sick person. If the sick person is unable to stand, he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, due to his (peace be upon him) statement to Imran bin Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side, gesturing.' And because obedience is according to ability. The summary: When a sick person becomes unable to stand – such that standing would delay recovery, cause severe weakness, or pain – then it is permissible for him to omit standing and he should pray sitting with bowing and prostration. The proof is the hadith of Imran bin Husayn (may Allah be pleased with him): 'I had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Imam Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' The author of Hidayah mentioned the rational proof: obedience is according to ability, so do it as much as possible and in the manner possible. Benefits: If the sick person can stand slightly, e.g., to recite one verse or say the takbir, but cannot stand fully, then he is commanded to stand that much, then when unable, sit. Similarly, if he can stand by leaning on a wall or staff, it is not permissible for him to omit standing. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the prayer of the sick. It first presents a ruling: if a sick person cannot stand due to fear of delayed recovery, severe weakness, or pain, then standing is omitted and he prays sitting, performing bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) normally. The ruling is supported by two proofs: first, a hadith from Imran bin Husayn, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed prayer standing, then sitting, then on the side, then lying on the back – each step for decreasing ability. Second, a rational principle: obedience is proportionate to ability (taklif bi hasab al-taqah). The commentary then discusses two applications: (a) if the person can stand for a short duration (e.g., reciting one verse or takbir), he must perform that much standing and then sit; (b) if he can stand with support (wall or staff), he must do so and cannot omit standing entirely. Both follow from the same principle – the obligation of standing is not waived when minimal ability exists.

Key Terms
عجز المريض عن القيام ('ajz al-marīḍ 'an al-qiyām): Inability of the sick person to stand without harm or severe difficulty.
الطاعة بحسب الطاقة (al-ṭā'ah bi-ḥasab al-ṭāqah): Obedience is according to ability; a principle that obligations are scaled to capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Imran bin Husayn, what is the sequence of postures for prayer when standing is not possible?
A) Sitting, then lying on side, then lying on back.
B) Sitting, then lying on side, then sitting with gestures.
C) Sitting with gestures, then lying on side, then lying on back.
D) Lying on side, then sitting, then lying on back.

Key Takeaway
The hadith and principle together establish that prayer obligations are reduced according to genuine ability, not beyond it.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling for the Sick Unable to Bow and Prostrate: Gesture with Head
Ruling for the sick: gesture (īmā') as substitute for bowing and prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate, specifically gesturing with the head and distinguishing it from raising an object to the forehead.

Core Idea
When unable to bow and prostrate, gesture with head; raising an object invalidates.

In earlier lessons, we covered the rulings for the sick who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate. Now we address the case where even bowing and prostration are impossible. The Hanafi school prescribes a clear substitute: gesturing with the head. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the crucial prohibition against raising an object to the forehead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while sitting and gesturing (īmā') when one cannot physically bow or prostrate. The ruling is that this gesture is wajib—it replaces the actual movements.
The prayer itself is still valid, but the gesture is obligatory for those who cannot perform the movements.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith: 'If you can prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' This is transmitted by al-Bazzar and others.
Although the chain is not mutawatir, the meaning is clear and accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith commands gesturing with the head ('فاوم براسك') when prostration is impossible. The preposition 'راس' indicates the head as the instrument, implying that the substitute is solely a head movement. Raising an object to the forehead is not a head gesture.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow raising an object to the forehead as a valid substitute. The Hanafi school strictly limits the substitute to head gesture because the hadith explicitly says 'with your head' and does not mention objects.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
A sick person who can only move their head must gesture: deeper nod for prostration, shallower for bowing. Raising a chair arm, book, or anything else to the forehead does not fulfill the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان لم يستطع الركوع والسجود او مى ايماء یعنی قاعدا لانه وسع مثله و جعل سجوده اخفض در ركوعه لانه قائم مقامها فاخذ حكمها ولا يرفع الى وجهه شيء يسجد عليه لقوله عليه السلام ان قدرت . تسجد على الارض فاسجد والاقاوم برأسك وان فعل ذلك وهو يخفض رأسه اجزاه لوجود الانماء ول وان لــ وضع ذلك على جبهته لا يجزيه لانعدامه ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر رکوع اور سجدہ کی قدرت نہ ہو تو اشارہ کرے یعنی بیٹھ کر کیونکہ یہی اس کی وسعت میں ہے۔ اور اہے کہ تعالیٰ کو بہ نسبت رکوع کے پست کر دے کیونکہ اشارہ ان دونوں کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور اپنے چہرے کی طرف ایسی چیز نہ اٹھائے جس پر ہی ترجمہ کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے کہ اگر تو زمین پر سجدہ کی قدرت رکھتا ہے تو زمین پر سجدہ کر ور نہ تو اپنے سر سے اشارہ کر اور اگر اس نے کیا اور حال یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنا سر جھکاتا ہے تو اس کو کافی ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اشارہ پایا گیا ہے اور اگر اس نے اس چیز کواپنی پیشانی پر رکھا جائز نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اشارہ معدوم ہے۔ تشریح صاحبقدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے کی قدرت نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر رکوع اور سجدہ اشارہ کے ساتھ ادا کرے کیوی اس وقت اس کی طاقت اسی قدر ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ طاعت بقدر طاقت ہوتی ہے البتہ سجدہ کا اشارہ بہ نسبت رکوع کے اشارے۔ پست کرے یعنی سجدہ کا اشارہ کرتے وقت سر زیادہ جھکا ہوار ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشارہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے قائم مقام ہے بند رکوع اوری بیست کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ حقیقی سجدہ بہ نسبت حقیقی رکوع کے پست ہوتا ہے اس لئے سجدہ کا اشارہ بھی یہ نسبت رکوع کے اشارہ کے کے پر آخر ہوگا۔
 قدرت
تشرة
قضا
شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ سجدہ کرنے کے لئے کوئی چیز اپنے چہرے کی طرف نہ اٹھائے دلیل حدیث رسول ہے کہ کے قدرت ان تسجد على الارض فاسجد والا قادم بر اسک امام بزار نے اپنے مسند میں یہ حدیث ان الفاظ کے مانی
He (al-Quduri) said: If he cannot bow and prostrate, he gestures – i.e., sitting – because this is within his capacity. And he makes his prostration lower than his bowing because the gesture stands in their place, so it takes their ruling. And he should not raise anything to his face to prostrate upon, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'If you can prostrate on the ground, do so; otherwise, gesture with your head.' And if he does that while lowering his head, it suffices because the gesture exists. But if he places something on his forehead, it does not suffice because the gesture is absent. Translation: al-Quduri said: If one does not have the ability for bowing and prostration, he gestures – i.e., sitting – because that is his capacity. And he should make his prostration lower than his bowing because the gesture stands in their place, so it takes their ruling. And he should not raise anything to his face to prostrate upon, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you have the ability to prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' And if he does that while lowering his head, it suffices because the gesture is present. But if he places something on his forehead, it is not valid because the gesture is absent. Explanation: al-Quduri said: If one cannot bow and prostrate, he performs bowing and prostration with gestures while sitting, because his capacity is only that, and it has already passed that obedience is according to ability. However, the gesture for prostration should be lower than the gesture for bowing – i.e., he should lower his head more when gesturing for prostration. The proof is that the gesture stands in place of the actual acts, so it takes their ruling. And since actual prostration is lower than actual bowing, so too the gesture for prostration should be lower than the gesture for bowing. Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: He should not raise anything to his face to prostrate upon. The proof is the hadith of the Messenger: 'If you can prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' Imam Bazzar narrated this hadith in his Musnad with these words.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling for the sick: if even bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) are impossible, the person prays sitting and makes gestures (īmā') with his head. The gesture for prostration must be lower (i.e., a deeper nod) than the gesture for bowing because the gesture substitutes for the actual movements and inherits their relative difference: actual prostration is lower than actual bowing. The passage further states that the sick person should NOT raise an object to his face to prostrate upon it. Instead, he must gesture directly with his head. The proof is a hadith: if you can prostrate on the ground, do so; otherwise, gesture with your head. If he lowers his head, it suffices because the gesture is present. But if he raises an object to his forehead (e.g., a piece of wood or cloth to touch his forehead), the prayer is not valid because the intended gesture is absent – the act of placing something on the forehead does not constitute the gesture that substitutes for the prostration. The commentary notes that this ruling follows from the principle that obedience is according to ability.

Key Terms
ايماء (īmā'): Gesturing with the head to indicate bowing and prostration when unable to perform actual movements.
جعل سجوده اخفض من ركوعه (ja'ala sujūdahu akhfada min rukū'ihi): The gesture for prostration must be lower (a deeper nod) than the gesture for bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a sick person, unable to prostrate, raises a piece of wood to his forehead while praying?
A) The prayer is valid because he is making an effort.
B) The prayer is invalid because the gesture is absent.
C) The prayer is valid only if he also moves his head.
D) The prayer is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
Gesture with the head is the only valid substitute for bowing and prostration in the Hanafi school; raising objects invalidates the prayer.

Gesture (Imā') for Ruku' and Sujud in Sick Person's Prayer
Ruling on head gestures when unable to bow and prostrate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on head gestures (imā') in prayer for those unable to bow and prostrate, explain the evidential basis of the hadith, and distinguish between valid and invalid applications of the gesture (e.g., lifting an object vs. lowering the head).

Core Idea
When unable to bow and prostrate, you must gesture with your head — and make the prostration gesture lower.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling for a sick person who cannot perform the physical acts of ruku' and sujud. The Hanafi school, based on clear prophetic guidance, permits substitution with head gestures (imā') while sitting. The key is that the gesture must be performed correctly: the head is lowered for both ruku' and sujud, but the sujud gesture must be more pronounced. We also look at a related issue — whether it is permissible to lift an object to the forehead to simulate sujud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation: fard of ruku' and sujud and their substitute when unable
The text states that if a person cannot bow and prostrate, they must gesture (imā') while sitting. Gesture is a valid substitute that takes the ruling of the original movements.
The ruling is fard ‘ayn for all prayers.
2
Examine the proof: the hadith of Jabir and its legal implication
The hadith commands the sick person to prostrate on the ground if possible, otherwise gesture with the head. The phrase 'make your prostration lower than your bowing' prescribes the relative lowering.
This hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear and accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the sub‑ruling on lifting an object to the forehead
The text distinguishes two scenarios: (a) if the person lowers their head while lifting an object, the gesture is present, so it suffices but is makruh; (b) if they lift the object without lowering the head, the gesture is absent and the prayer is invalid.
The head movement is the essential element of imā'.
4
Apply the ruling to common cases
For a patient who can only manage a slight head movement, the imā' is valid as long as the sujud gesture is clearly lower. Those who can stand but not bow must perform standing gestures? (Not directly covered here, but the principle extends.)
Refer to the full fiqh of al-marīḍ (the sick person) for details.

Source Text

کیونکہ یہی اس کی وسعت میں ہے۔ اور سجدہ کو بہ نسبت رکوع کے پست کر دے کیونکہ اشارہ ان دونوں کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور اپنے چہرے کی طرف ایسی چیز نہ اٹھائے جس پر سجدہ کرے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا کہ سجدہ کرنے کے لئے کوئی چیز اپنے چہرے کی طرف نہ اٹھائے، دلیل حدیث رسول ہے. عن جابر رضي الله عنه ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عاد مريضا فراه يصلي على وسادة فاخذها فرمى بها ثم اخذ عودا ليصلي عليه فاخذه فرمى به وقال صل على الارض ان استطعت والا فاوم ايماء واجعل سجودك اخفض من ركوعك. یعنی حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ نے کہا کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ایک بیمار کی عیادت کو تشریف لائے تو دیکھا کہ وہ تکیہ پر نماز پڑھتا ہے پس آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے تکیہ لے کر پھینک دیا پھر اس نے ایک لکڑی لی تاکہ اس پر نماز پڑھے آپ نے اس کو بھی پھینک دیا اور فرمایا کہ زمین پر نماز پڑھ اگر قدرت ہو ورنہ اشارہ کر اور اپنے سجود کو اپنے رکوع سے پست کر۔ یہ حدیث اس پر محمول ہے کہ وہ بیمار تکیہ اٹھا کر پیشانی سے لگاتا تھا، آنحضور نے اس سے منع فرمایا۔ پس اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ کے لئے کسی چیز کو اٹھا کر پیشانی سے لگانا درست نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مریض نے اگر تکیہ اٹھا کر پیشانی سے لگایا تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں: اگر سر جھکاتا ہے تو کافی ہوگیا کیونکہ سر جھکانے سے اشارہ پایا گیا، اور یہی اس پر فرض ہے، البتہ مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر تکیہ اٹھا کر پیشانی پر رکھا اور سر قطعی پست نہیں ہوا تو اس سے رکوع اور سجدہ ادا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اشارہ معدوم ہو گیا حالانکہ یہ فرض تھا۔
He (Al-Quduri) said: If he is unable to bow and prostrate, he gestures while sitting, because that is within his capacity. He makes his prostration gesture lower than his bowing gesture, because the gesture is a substitute for them and takes their ruling. He should not lift anything to his face to prostrate on, due to the Prophet's saying: 'If you are able to prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' And if he does that while lowering his head, it suffices because the gesture is present; but if he does not lower his head and places that thing on his forehead, it does not suffice because the gesture is absent. Commentary: Al-Quduri said that if unable to bow and prostrate, he performs them while sitting by gesture, because his ability is only that much, and it has passed that obedience is according to ability. He should make the prostration gesture lower than the bowing gesture, meaning lower the head more for prostration. The evidence is that the gesture stands in the place of bowing and prostration, and since the actual prostration is lower than the actual bowing, the gesture for prostration is lower. Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that one should not lift anything to the face for prostration, based on the hadith of Jabir: The Prophet visited a sick person who was praying on a cushion; he took it and threw it away, then he took a stick to pray on, and he threw that and said: 'Pray on the ground if you can, otherwise gesture, and make your prostration lower than your bowing.' This hadith is interpreted that the patient was lifting the cushion to his forehead. The Prophet forbade that. So it is learned that lifting something to the forehead for prostration is not correct. The author of Hidayah says: If the patient lifts a cushion to his forehead, two cases: if he lowers his head, it suffices because the gesture is present, and this is his duty, though it is makruh; if he lifts the cushion to his forehead but does not lower his head, then his bowing and prostration are not valid because the gesture is absent, while it was obligatory.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the prayer of the sick. The author, Al-Quduri, states the rule: when a sick person cannot physically perform ruku' and sujud, he must do so by head gestures (imā') while sitting. The gesture must be such that the head is lowered more for sujud than for ruku', because the gesture substitutes for the actual movements. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet commanding a sick person to prostrate on the ground if possible, otherwise gesture with the head. The passage then clarifies a common error: one should not lift an object (like a cushion) to the forehead to simulate sujud. If one does lift it but also lowers the head, it is valid but makruh (disliked) because the gesture is achieved by the head movement. If one lifts the object without lowering the head, the gesture is absent and the prayer is invalid. The hadith of Jabir supports this: the Prophet rejected a sick person's use of a cushion for sujud.

Key Terms
إيماء (imā'): Gesture with the head, as a substitute for bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) in prayer when one is unable to perform the actual movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person lifts a cushion to his forehead for sujud but does not lower his head, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid because the cushion touched the forehead.
B) The prayer is invalid because the gesture (imā') is absent.
C) The prayer is valid but makruh.
D) The prayer is valid only if performed while sitting.

Key Takeaway
A sick person unable to bow and prostrate must gesture with the head while sitting, making the sujud gesture lower; lifting an object to the forehead without lowering the head invalidates the prayer.

Prayer When Unable to Sit: Lying on Back and Gesturing
Ruling for prayer when unable to sit: lie on back and gesture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a sick person who cannot sit: the required position and gesture, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
When sitting is impossible, lie on your back, face the qibla, and gesture with head for ruku' and sujud.

This lesson extends the rulings for sick prayer. When even sitting is not possible, the Prophet ﷺ taught a specific posture: lying on the back, feet toward the qibla, and using head gestures to indicate bowing and prostration. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the hadith proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
When a sick person cannot sit, they must lie on their back (استلقاء) and perform prayer using gestures. This is a substitution for the normal standing/sitting prayer.
The act is still the obligatory prayer (fard).
2
Understand the required actions
Lie flat on the back, place feet towards the qibla, place a pillow under the head to elevate it (facilitating gesture), and gesture with the head for ruku' and sujud.
The head gesture is called imā'.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'يصلي المريض قائما...' which outlines a sequence of concessions: standing → sitting → on back with gesture → if unable to gesture, then Allah accepts the excuse.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'استلقى على ظهره وأومى' is derived from the hadith's explicit instruction to gesture on the back. The sequence shows that this is the penultimate level of concession.
5
Note the scope
This ruling applies only when the person can gesture. If even gesture is impossible, a further concession applies (see next lesson).
The source text only covers the case where gesture is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لم يستطع القعود استلقى على ظهره وجعل رجليه الى القبلة وأومى بالركوع والسجود لقوله عليه السلام: يصلي المريض قائما فان لم يستطع فقاعدا فان لم يستطع فعلى قفاه يومئ إيماء فان لم يستطع فالله تعالى أحق بقبول العذر منه. ترجمہ: اگر مریض کو بیٹھنے کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو اپنی پشت پر لیٹ جائے اور اپنے پاؤں قبلہ کی طرف رکھے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بیمار کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے، اگر اس کی قدرت نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر پڑھے، اور اگر اس کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو گدی کے بل لیٹ کر اشارہ کرے، پھر اگر یہ بھی نہ ہو سکے تو اللہ تعالی زیادہ لائق ہیں اس سے عذر قبول کریں۔ تشریح: اگر مریض کو بیٹھنے کی قدرت نہ ہو تو اپنی پشت کے بل چت لیٹ جائے اور اپنے سر کے نیچے اونچا سا تکیہ رکھے تاکہ بیٹھنے کے مشابہ ہو جائے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرنا ممکن ہو، اور پاؤں قبلہ کی طرف کرلے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے۔ دلیل آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول ہے۔ حدیث کے 'فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه' کی تفسیر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے: بعض علماء نے کہا ہے کہ اشارہ پر قادر نہ ہونے کی صورت میں نماز نہیں ہوتی البتہ نماز مؤخر کی جا سکتی ہے جب تندرست ہو جائے قضاء کرے۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک اس جملے کی تفسیر یہ ہوگی کہ اللہ تعالی عذر تأخیر کو قبول کرنے کے لیے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ ایسی حالت میں قضاء ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، ان حضرات کے نزدیک تفسیر یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی عذر اسقاط کو قبول کرنے کے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اسی قول کو اصح کہا ہے۔
And if he is unable to sit, he lies on his back, places his feet towards the qibla, and gestures for bowing and prostration, due to his saying (peace be upon him): The sick person prays standing; if unable, then sitting; if unable, then on his back gesturing; if unable, then Allah is most deserving of accepting the excuse. Commentary: If the patient cannot sit, he lies flat on his back, places a high pillow under his head to resemble sitting and make gesture possible, and points his feet towards the qibla, and gestures for bowing and prostration. The proof is the Prophet's saying. There is a difference among scholars in interpreting 'Allah is most deserving of accepting the excuse': Some say that if unable to gesture, the prayer is not performed but can be postponed, and when healthy, he makes it up. They interpret that Allah accepts the excuse of postponement. Others say that in that state, the obligation falls (qada' is dropped). They interpret that Allah accepts the excuse of dropping. The author of al-Inayah considered the latter view as more correct (asahh).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage continues the ruling on the sick person's prayer, now addressing the case when even sitting is impossible. The rule is clear: lie on the back, feet toward qibla, and gesture with the head for ruku' and sujud, placing a pillow under the head to facilitate gesture. The proof is a well-known hadith that outlines the sequence: standing, sitting, on the back, and finally if even gesture is impossible, Allah is most deserving of accepting the excuse. The passage then notes a scholarly difference in interpreting this final phrase. Some Hanafi scholars (as mentioned in the commentary) hold that the prayer should be postponed until recovery and then made up (qada'). Others hold that the obligation is completely dropped (isqat), and no makeup is required. The commentator, Sahib al-Inayah (author of al-'Inayah), declares the latter view as 'asahh' (more correct), making it the relied-upon position in this text.

Key Terms
إيماء (imā'): Gesture with the head; in this context, the movement of the head for ruku' and sujud while lying on the back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what should a sick person do if he cannot sit?
A) Lie on his back and gesture with his head.
B) Lie on his side and gesture with his head.
C) Stand with support.
D) Postpone prayer.

Key Takeaway
When sitting is impossible, the sick must lie on their back, face the qibla, and gesture with the head for ruku' and sujud, as shown in the hadith.

When Unable to Gesture: Is the Obligation Dropped or Postponed?
Scholarly difference on inability to gesture and the tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of the hadith's final phrase and state the mufta bihi position: the obligation is dropped.

Core Idea
If even head gesture is impossible, the prayer obligation drops entirely — no makeup required, per the preferred Hanafi view.

The Prophetic hadith ends with a crucial phrase: 'If unable (to gesture), then Allah is most deserving of accepting the excuse.' Scholars differed: does this mean postpone and make up later, or does it drop the obligation? This lesson explores the two interpretations, their proofs, and the tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of difference
The difference centres on the interpretation of 'قبول العذر' (acceptance of the excuse) in the hadith. Does Allah accept the excuse of delay (requiring qada' later) or the excuse of complete inability (dropping the obligation)?
This arises when the sick person cannot even gesture.
2
State the first view: postponement and qada'
Some Hanafi scholars say the prayer is not performed in that state but is postponed, and when the person recovers, he must make it up (qada'). They interpret 'قبول العذر' as Allah accepting the excuse of delaying the prayer.
3
State the second view: obligation dropped (isqat)
Other scholars say the obligation of that prayer is completely dropped; no qada' is required. They interpret 'قبول العذر' as Allah accepting the excuse of dropping the obligation due to inability.
This view is preferred by the author of al-Inayah.
4
Identify the tarjih
Sahib al-Inayah (author of al-'Inayah) declared the drop view as 'asahh' (more correct). In Hanafi fatwa, this is the mufta bihi position.
Thus, if a person cannot gesture, no prayer is required, and no makeup upon recovery.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under the postponement view, qada' is required when health returns. Under the drop view, no qada' is required.
This significantly impacts the sick person's obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لم يستطع القعود استلقى على ظهره وجعل رجليه الى القبلة وأومى بالركوع والسجود لقوله عليه السلام: يصلي المريض قائما فان لم يستطع فقاعدا فان لم يستطع فعلى قفاه يومئ إيماء فان لم يستطع فالله تعالى أحق بقبول العذر منه. ترجمہ: اگر مریض کو بیٹھنے کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو اپنی پشت پر لیٹ جائے اور اپنے پاؤں قبلہ کی طرف رکھے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بیمار کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے، اگر اس کی قدرت نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر پڑھے، اور اگر اس کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو گدی کے بل لیٹ کر اشارہ کرے، پھر اگر یہ بھی نہ ہو سکے تو اللہ تعالی زیادہ لائق ہیں اس سے عذر قبول کریں۔ تشریح: اگر مریض کو بیٹھنے کی قدرت نہ ہو تو اپنی پشت کے بل چت لیٹ جائے اور اپنے سر کے نیچے اونچا سا تکیہ رکھے تاکہ بیٹھنے کے مشابہ ہو جائے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرنا ممکن ہو، اور پاؤں قبلہ کی طرف کرلے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے۔ دلیل آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول ہے۔ حدیث کے 'فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه' کی تفسیر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے: بعض علماء نے کہا ہے کہ اشارہ پر قادر نہ ہونے کی صورت میں نماز نہیں ہوتی البتہ نماز مؤخر کی جا سکتی ہے جب تندرست ہو جائے قضاء کرے۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک اس جملے کی تفسیر یہ ہوگی کہ اللہ تعالی عذر تأخیر کو قبول کرنے کے لیے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ ایسی حالت میں قضاء ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، ان حضرات کے نزدیک تفسیر یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی عذر اسقاط کو قبول کرنے کے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اسی قول کو اصح کہا ہے۔

Key Terms
قضاء (qadā'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after the time. In this lesson, it refers to whether makeup is required after recovery.
اسقاط (isqāt): Dropping of the obligation; no requirement to make up the prayer.
عذر (ʿudhr): Excuse; in this hadith, the excuse of either delay or complete inability.

Using a Pillow for Prostration: Head Movement is Essential
Hadith and Hanafi ruling on using a pillow for prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a pillow for prostration and explain why head movement is the decisive condition for valid gesture.

Core Idea
For a sick person, the obligatory gesture is head movement, not touching an object.

This lesson examines a hadith where the Prophet (SAW) forbade a sick person from using a pillow or stick for prostration. The Hanafi commentary from al-Hidayah derives two distinct rulings depending on whether the sick person actually lowers his head. Understanding the precise condition for valid gesture (ima') is crucial for applying the rules of the prayer of the sick.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sick person using a pillow for prostration. The ruling has two forms: if head is lowered, the prayer is valid but makruh; if head is not lowered, the prayer is invalid.
The ruling depends solely on whether the head moves.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Jabir: the Prophet visits a sick person, sees him praying on a pillow, takes it and throws it, then picks a stick and throws it, saying 'Pray on the ground if you can, otherwise gesture, and make your prostration lower than your bowing.'
The Prophet's action shows rejection of using objects.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's rejection indicates that gesture must be by head movement, not by using an object. The command to make prostration lower than bowing implies actual head tilting.
The meaning extracted: ima' is head motion.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is may permit using a pillow in necessity based on ease and removing hardship.
This is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit hadith action and is the mufta bihi (operative) ruling in the school.
The majority of Hanafi scholars adhere to this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المريض عن جابر ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عاد مريضا فراه يصلى على وسادة فاخذ ها فرمي بها ثم اخذ عودا ليصلى عليه فاخذه فرمى بها وقال صل على الأرض ان استطعت والا فايماء وجعل سجودك اخفض من ركوعك. صاحب هداية كہتے ہیں کہ مریض نے اگر تکیہ اٹھا کر پیشانی سے لگایا تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں: رکوع اور سجدہ کے لئے اپنا سر جھکاتا ہے تو کافی ہوگیا کیونکہ سر جھکانے سے اشارہ پایا گیا اور یہی اس پر فرض ہے البتہ مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر تکیہ اٹھا کر پیشانی پر لگایا اور سر قطع پست نہیں ہوا تو اس سے رکوع اور سجدہ ادا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اشارہ معدوم ہو گیا حالانکہ یہ فرض تھا۔
Chapter of the prayer of the sick. From Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) visited a sick person and saw him praying on a pillow, so he took it and threw it. Then he took a stick to pray on, so he took it and threw it and said: 'Pray on the ground if you are able, otherwise gesture, and make your prostration lower than your bowing.' The author of al-Hidayah says: If the sick person lifts a pillow and places it on his forehead, there are two cases: if he lowers his head for bowing and prostration, it suffices because the gesture is achieved by lowering the head, and that is what is obligatory upon him, but it is makruh. And if he lifts the pillow to his forehead and does not lower his head at all, then bowing and prostration are not performed, because in this case the gesture is absent, whereas it was obligatory.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a sick person using a pillow for prostration. It begins by citing the hadith of Jabir in which the Prophet (SAW) forbade a sick person from using a pillow or stick for prostration and instructed him to pray on the ground if possible, otherwise gesture with the head, making the inclination for prostration lower than that for bowing. The commentary from al-Hidayah then explains the legal ruling: if the sick person lifts a pillow and touches it to his forehead while also lowering his head in gesture, the prayer is valid but makruh because the obligatory gesture is achieved through the lowering of the head. However, if he merely touches the pillow to his forehead without lowering his head at all, then the gesture is absent, and the bowing and prostration are not performed; the prayer is invalid because the required action is missing. The key point is that the gesture (ima') by head movement is what fulfills the obligation, not merely touching an object. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الوسادة (al-wisadah): A pillow or cushion used to elevate the forehead during prostration.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostration when unable to perform the full actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person lifts a pillow and touches it to his forehead but does not lower his head, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid and there is no problem.
B) The prayer is invalid because the gesture was not performed.
C) The prayer is valid but makruh.
D) The prayer is invalid only if the pillow is more than 10 cm high.

Key Takeaway
In the prayer of the sick, the essential act for prostration is the gesture of the head; merely using an object without head movement invalidates the prayer.

Praying Lying on Back with Gesturing
Method for sick person unable to sit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of prayer for a sick person who cannot sit, and apply the hadith to determine the obligation to gesture.

Core Idea
If you cannot sit, prayer is still wajib—lie on your back, point feet to qibla, and gesture.

When illness prevents standing or sitting, the obligation of prayer does not drop. The Hanafi school provides a clear method: lying on the back with gestures. This lesson explains the ruling and the prophetic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the act
The ruling applies when the sick person cannot sit. The act is to lie on the back, place feet toward qibla, and gesture for ruku and sujud.
Note: 'istilqa' means lying supine, face up.
2
State the ruling level
Prayer is wajib even in this state; this method fulfills the obligation.
Wajib here means obligatory; leaving it is sinful if possible.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith orders a sequence: standing → sitting → lying on back with gestures. If even gesturing is impossible, Allah accepts the excuse.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted by Hanafis.
4
Understand the sequence of options
The hadith establishes a hierarchy: pray standing if possible; if not, sitting; if not, lying with gestures; if gestures impossible, no prayer required.
This hierarchy prevents dropping prayer prematurely.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario where a person cannot sit, the mufta bihi is to lie on the back, point feet to qibla, and gesture with head.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لم يستطع القعود استلقى على ظهره وجعل رجليه الى القبلة واومى بالركوع والسجود لقوله عليه السلام: يصلى المريض قائما فان لم يستطع فقاعدا فان لم يستطع فعلى قفاه يؤمى ايماء فان لم يستطع فالله تعالى احق بقبول العذر منه.
And if he cannot sit, he should lie on his back and place his feet towards the qibla, and gesture for bowing and prostration due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The sick person prays standing; if he cannot, then sitting; if he cannot, then on his back gesturing; if he cannot, then Allah is more worthy to accept his excuse.'
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a sick person who cannot even sit. The method is to lie on the back, feet pointing towards the qibla, and perform gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration by moving the head. The proof is the hadith reported from the Prophet (SAW) which outlines the sequence: standing, then sitting, then lying on the back with gestures, and finally, if even that is impossible, Allah will accept the excuse. This is a clear ruling from the Sunnah establishing the obligation to pray in any possible manner.

Key Terms
الاستلقاء (al-istilqa'): Lying on the back with face upwards.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head to indicate bowing and prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He should lie on his back, feet towards qibla, and gesture.
C) He should pray with his eyes only.
D) He is exempt from prayer.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to pray remains even in extreme illness; the method adapts to ability, with lying on the back and gesturing as the final physical option before exemption.

When Gesture Fails: Is Qada Dropped or Postponed?
Interpretation of a hadith regarding prayer obligation for the incapacitated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi interpretations of the hadith 'Allah is more worthy to accept excuse' regarding prayer qada, and identify the preferred view according to al-'Inaya.

Core Idea
If unable even to gesture, qada may be dropped—Allah accepts the excuse of inability.

A person too ill to gesture with the head during prayer still owes the obligation of salah. But must that prayer be made up after recovery? The hadith saying 'Allah is more worthy to accept his excuse' is ambiguous. Hanafi scholars have differed: some require postponement and qada, others drop the qada entirely. The author of al-'Inaya chooses the latter as the more correct view.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the scenario: a sick person who cannot even gesture with the head. The question is whether the missed prayer must be made up (qada) or the obligation falls away entirely.
2
Identify the two positions
Some scholars say the prayer is postponed until recovery, and qada is required. Others say the obligation of qada is dropped. Note that both are within the Hanafi school.
The difference hinges on how 'acceptance of excuse' is interpreted.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith states: 'فان لم يستطع فالله تعالى احق بقبول العذر منه' (if he cannot, Allah is more worthy to accept his excuse). The wording is ambiguous: does it excuse the delay (postponement) or the entire obligation (isqat)?
The dalil is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
4
Note the tarjih
The author of al-'Inaya (صاحب العناية) declares the view that qada is dropped as 'أصح' (more correct). This is a later Hanafi preference.
This is a fatawa mutakhkhirin position; it may not be the outright majority.
5
Apply the preferred view
According to al-'Inaya, if a person is completely unable to gesture, no qada is required. The obligation is removed as a concession for extreme hardship.
This does not apply to those who can gesture but omit it carelessly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقوله: فالله تعالى احق بقبول العذر منه. في تفسير هذا الحديث اختلاف العلماء. بعض العلماء قالوا: اذا كان لا يقدر على الإيماء، لا تسقط الصلاة عنه ولكن يؤخرها حتى يبرأ فيقضيها. وتفسير هذه العبارة عندهم: 'فالله تعالى احق بقبول عذر التأخير منه'. وبعض قالوا: تسقط القضاء في هذه الحالة. وتفسيرهم: 'فالله تعالى احق بقبول عذر الإسقاط منه'. صاحب العناية قال: هذا القول اصح.
So His saying: 'Allah is more worthy to accept his excuse.' In the interpretation of this hadith, the scholars differ. Some scholars said: If he is unable to gesture, the prayer is not dropped from him, but he postpones it until he recovers and then makes it up. Their interpretation of this phrase: 'Allah is more worthy to accept the excuse of postponement.' And some said: The qada is dropped in this situation. Their interpretation: 'Allah is more worthy to accept the excuse of dropping (the obligation).' The author of al-'Inaya said: This latter statement is more correct.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute (though it mentions 'some scholars', it reflects views within the Hanafi school). The hadith concludes with 'فالله تعالى احق بقبول العذر منه' (Allah is more worthy to accept his excuse). Scholars disagreed on what this means. Some hold that even if one cannot gesture with the head, the prayer is not dropped; it is postponed until recovery, and qada must be performed. They interpret the 'acceptance of excuse' as referring to the delay. Others hold that if one cannot even gesture, the obligation of qada is dropped entirely; Allah accepts the excuse and no makeup is needed. The commentator of al-'Inaya prefers the view that qada is dropped. This reflects a relaxation for extreme incapacity.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body as a substitute for bowing and prostration when one cannot perform the actual movements.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after recovery.
الإسقاط (al-isqat): The dropping of the obligation entirely, so no qada needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which interpretation did صاحب العناية (author of al-'Inaya) consider more correct?
A) The prayer is postponed and qada required.
B) The qada is dropped.
C) The person must use eye gestures only.
D) The person must pay fidya.

Key Takeaway
For a person utterly unable to gesture, the preferred Hanafi view is that qada is not required because Allah accepts the excuse of dropping the obligation.

Preference: Lying on Back vs Side for Sick Prayer
Comparing lying on back vs side for sick prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the preferable lying position for a sick person's prayer and explain the rationale based on the direction of gestures, while distinguishing the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Hanafis prefer lying on the back because head gestures point toward the air of the Ka'bah, unlike the side.

When a sick person cannot sit, they may pray lying down. But which position is better: on the back or on the side? This lesson explores the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on this matter, focusing on the direction of gestures as the key criterion. By the end, you'll understand why Hanafis recommend the supine position and why the difference matters in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school considers lying on the back (istilqa') as the preferable (awla) position for a sick person who cannot sit.
Both positions are valid, but one is preferred.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik) prefer lying on the side (idtija').
The Shafi'i rely on a hadith from 'Imran ibn Husayn.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the Hanafi rationale: when lying on the back, the head's gesture (ishara) is directed towards the air of the Ka'bah, which is the qibla direction. On the side, the gesture goes towards the feet, not directly towards the qibla.
The proof is based on the principle that prayer gestures should point towards the qibla.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i cite the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet instructed a sick man to pray lying on his side. The Hanafi response notes that the hadith of Ibn 'Umar supports lying on the back, and both are authentic; preference is based on direction of gesture.
Both positions are valid; the dispute is about which is better.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis recommend supine, Shafi'is recommend side. A person following either school may choose the other view if not aware, but both fulfill the obligation.
The fatwa in the Hanafi school is that supine is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان استلقى على جنبه ووجهه الى القبلة جاز لما روينا من قبل الا ان الاولى هو الاستلقاء عندنا خلافا للشافعي لان اشارة المستلقى تقع الى هواء الكعبة واشارة المضطجع على جنبه الى جانب قدميه وبه تنادى الصلاة.
And if he lies on his side with his face towards the qibla, it is permissible based on what we narrated earlier, but the preferred (position) is lying on the back in our view, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the gesture of one lying on his back falls towards the air of the Ka'bah, while the gesture of one lying on his side falls towards his feet, and with that the prayer is called (fulfilled).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning which position is preferable for a sick person who can only pray lying down: on the back (supine) or on the side (lateral). Both positions are valid, as both are supported by hadith. However, the Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa and his followers) considers lying on the back as more virtuous (awla). The rationale is that when one lies on the back, the gestural movements (for bowing and prostration) are directed towards the space of the Ka'bah, which is the direction of prayer. In contrast, when lying on the side, the gestures are directed towards the feet, which is not directly towards the qibla. The Shafi'i school (and also Maliki) prefer lying on the side. The Hanafi reasoning is based on the principle that the ritual prayer (salat) is fulfilled by directing gestures towards the qibla, and the supine position better achieves this.

Key Terms
المستلقى (al-mustalqi): One who lies on his back facing upward.
المضطجع (al-mudtaji'): One who lies on his side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis prefer lying on the back over lying on the side for a sick person's prayer?
A) Because it is easier for the sick person.
B) Because the gesture is directed towards the air of the Ka'bah.
C) Because it is mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because the Prophet always prayed that way.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis recommend the supine position for a sick person's prayer because it directs gestures toward the qibla, but the side position is also valid.

Ruling on Gesturing with Eyes and Heart When Head Unable
Sick person unable to gesture with head

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling for a conscious sick person who cannot gesture with his head, identify the dispute with Zufar, and explain the evidence and the condition of consciousness.

Core Idea
If the head cannot move, prayer is postponed—never performed by eye, heart, or eyebrow; qada is wajib when able.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in the prayer of a sick person: when even head movement is impossible. The Hanafi school maintains that the prayer is not dropped but postponed, and alternative gestures (eyes, heart, eyebrows) are invalid. We will examine the majority position, the dissenting view of Zufar, and the key distinction between conscious and unconscious patients.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the prayer is postponed (not performed by eye, heart, or eyebrow gestures) and must be made up when the person recovers.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify Zufar's opposing view
Zufar allowed gesturing with the eyes or eyebrows as a substitute. Understand his rationale: analogy to the head gesture.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar whose view is not the relied-upon position.
3
Examine the evidence for the majority view
The text cites a hadith (narrated earlier) that specifies gesturing with the head, and a rational argument: setting substitutes by opinion is prohibited (la yunṣabu al-abdāl bi al-ra'y), and there is no analogy (qiyas) between the head and the eye because the head is the body part that performs the pillar (rukn).
The head gesture is itself a rukn; eyes and heart are not analogous.
4
Distinguish between conscious and unconscious patients
The text notes that the ruling applies only if the patient is conscious (mufiq). The unconscious person (mughmā ʿalayhi) is exempt from qada because he does not understand the address (khiṭāb).
Consciousness is a condition for the obligation of qada.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text concludes 'this is the correct view' (al-ṣaḥīḥ). The majority position (postpone, no eye/heart gestures) is the operative ruling for fatwa. Zufar's view may be considered in extreme cases but is not the standard fatwa.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يستطع الايماء براسه اخرت عنه ولا يؤمى بعينه ولا بقلبه ولا بحاجبيه خلافا لزفر لما روينا من قبل ولان نصب الابدال بالرأى ممتنع ولا قياس على الرأس لانه ينادى به ركن الصلوة دون العين واختيها. وفي قوله 'اخرت عنه' اشارة الى انه لا تسقط الصلوة عنه وان كان العجز اكثر من يوم وليلة اذا كان مفيقا وهو الصحيح لانه يفهم مضمون الخطاب بخلاف المغمى عليه.
Then if he cannot gesture with his head, it is postponed from him, and he does not gesture with his eye, nor with his heart, nor with his eyebrows, contrary to Zufar, due to what we narrated before, and because setting up substitutes by opinion is prohibited, and there is no analogy to the head because the head is the one by which a pillar of prayer is performed, not the eye and its likes. And in his saying 'it is postponed from him' there is an indication that the prayer is not dropped from him, even if the incapacity exceeds a day and night, provided he is conscious. This is the correct view because he understands the content of the address, unlike the unconscious person.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who sometimes differed from Abu Hanifa). It rules on the case where a sick person cannot even move his head to gesture. According to the majority of Hanafis (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), the prayer is not performed by eye, heart, or eyebrow gestures. Instead, the prayer is postponed until the person recovers or can gesture. Zufar held that one can gesture with the eyes or eyebrows, but the text rejects this because gesturing with the head is a distinct pillar (rukn) that cannot be substituted by mere opinion (ra'y) or analogy. The head itself is the body part by which the pillar of prayer (the gesture) is performed; eyes and others are not analogous. The phrase 'it is postponed from him' indicates that the obligation is not dropped; qada must be done later as long as the person is conscious. If unconscious, the prayer is dropped entirely. This is an important distinction: consciousness is a condition for understanding the address (mukhatab), and only the conscious are obligated to make up missed prayers.

Key Terms
الإيماء بالرأس (al-ima' bi al-ra's): Gesturing with the head to indicate bowing and prostration.
المغمى عليه (al-mughma 'alayhi): A person who is unconscious (e.g., due to illness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what should a conscious sick person do if he cannot gesture with his head?
A) He should gesture with his eyes or eyebrows.
B) He should postpone the prayer and make it up later.
C) He does not need to pray at all; it is dropped.
D) He should pray with his heart (intention).

Key Takeaway
A conscious sick person who cannot move his head must postpone prayer, not perform it with eye or heart gestures, and make it up later (qada); the unconscious person is exempt.

Preferred Posture for Sick Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on preferred posture for sick prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers lying on the back (istilqa') over lying on the side (idtija') for a sick person's prayer, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Both postures valid, but Hanafi prefers back because indication is more direct to the Kaaba.

When a person is too ill to stand or sit for prayer, they may pray lying down—but which posture is better? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on this, each citing a different hadith. This lesson examines the proofs and reasoning behind the Hanafi preference for lying on the back, and how it answers the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that the Hanafi school holds both postures permissible but considers lying on the back (istilqa') better (awla).
The source calls this 'the better is better' (الاولى هو الاولى).
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
Find the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar: 'If he cannot [pray standing], then on his back indicating.' This is the primary proof.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in the school.
3
Identify the opposing view and its dalil
The Shafi'i school prefers lying on the side (idtija') based on the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn: 'If you cannot, then on your side indicating.'
Both hadiths are authentic; the ikhtilaf is in preference.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that both hadiths are valid, but the back posture gives a more direct indication (isharah) to the airspace of the Kaaba (hawa' al-ka'bah), while the side indication points toward the feet, which is less direct.
The qibla direction is fulfilled by indicating toward the Kaaba's airspace.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi will pray on his back, a Shafi'i on his side. Both prayers are valid, but each follows the sunnah as understood by his school.
No issue of invalidity; only optional preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المريض

وان استلقى على جنبه ووجهه الى القبلة جاز لماروينا من قبل الا ان الاولى هو الاولى عندنا خلافا للشافعي لان اشارة المستلقى تقع الى هواء الكعبة واشارة المضطجع على جنبه الى جانب قدميه و به تنادى الصرة
ترجمہ اور اگر بیمار کروٹ پر لیٹا اور اس کا منہ بجانب قبلہ ہے تو جائز ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے پہلے روایت کی ہے گورکی جیت ہمارے نزدیک اولی ہے امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ چت لیٹنے والے کا اشارہ ہوا کعبہ کی طرف پڑتا ہے اور کروٹ پر لیٹے کا اشارہ اس کے دونوں قدموں کی جانب پڑتا ہے اور اسی کے ساتھ نماز ادا ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ بیا را گر کروٹ پر لیٹ کر اشارے سے نماز پڑھے درانحالیکہ اس کا منہ قبلہ کی جانب سے بھی جائز ہے دلیل حدیث عمران بن حصین ہے جو اول باب میں مذکور ہو چکی ہے اور باری تعالیٰ کا قول يَذْكُرُونَ اللَّهَ قِيَامًا قُعُونَ عَلَى جُنُوبِهِمُ بھی اس پر دال ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ عمران بن حصین کی حدیث فان لم تستطع فعلى الجنب يومى ايمان عبد اللہ بن عمر کی حدیث فان لم يستطع فعلى قفاا یو می ایماء متعارض ہیں کیونکہ حدیث عمران ابن حصین میں کروٹ پر لیٹ کرنا پڑھنا مذکور ہے اور عبد اللہ بن عمر کی حدیث میں چت لیٹ کر نماز پڑھنا مذکور ہے۔ اور بیمار کی حالت عذر کی حالت ہے اس لئے ان واو حالتوں میں سے ہر ایک ہیئت پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے البتہ اولویت میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ ہمارے نزدیک ہیئت اولی ( چت لیٹ کری) نماز پڑھنا اولیٰ ہے اور امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک ہیئت ثانیہ ( کروٹ ) پر نماز پڑھنا اولیٰ ہے ہمارے نزدیک وجہ اداوین ہے کہ چت لیٹ کر نماز ادا کرنے کا اشارہ کعبہ کی قضاء کی طرف پڑتا ہے اور کروٹ پر لیٹ کر نماز ادا کرنے والے کا اشارہ اس کے قدموں کی طرف پڑتا ہے اور نماز اس سے ادا ہوتی ہے کہ اشارہ فضاء کعبہ کی طرف پڑے اس لئے چت لیٹ کر نماز ادا کرنا اولی ہو گا۔
Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick

And if he lies on his side with his face toward the qibla, it is permissible due to what we narrated before, but the better is the better in our view, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the indication of one lying on his back is toward the airspace of the Kaaba, and the indication of one lying on his side is toward the direction of his feet, and with that the prayer is performed.
Translation: And if a sick person lies on his side and his face is toward the qibla, it is permissible due to the hadith we narrated before. However, in our view the better is better; Imam al-Shafi'i differs because the indication of one lying on his back is toward the airspace of the Kaaba, and the indication of one lying on his side is toward his feet, and with that prayer is performed.
Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said that if a sick person prays lying on his side with indication while his face is toward the qibla, it is also permissible. The proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn mentioned earlier in the chapter, and the saying of Allah Almighty: 'They remember Allah standing, sitting, and on their sides.' The summary is that the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn 'If you cannot [prostrate], then on your side indicating' and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar 'If he cannot, then on his back indicating' conflict, because in Imran's hadith praying on the side is mentioned, and in Abdullah ibn Umar's hadith praying on the back is mentioned. Since the sick person is in a state of excuse, praying in either posture is permissible, but there is a difference in preference. Thus in our view, the first posture (lying on the back) is better, while Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that the second posture (on the side) is better. Our reason is that the indication of one lying on his back is toward the direction of the Kaaba, while the indication of one lying on his side is toward his feet, and prayer is performed by indicating toward the airspace of the Kaaba, so praying on the back is better.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the preferred posture for a sick person who cannot pray standing. The Hanafi position, based on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar and the principle that the indication toward the Kaaba is more direct, holds that lying on the back (istilqa') is better. The Shafi'i position, based on the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn, prefers lying on the side (idtija'). Both are valid, but the Hanafi school prioritizes the back because the indication points directly to the airspace of the Kaaba, while the side indication points to the feet. The commentator explains that both postures are permissible due to the excuse, and the difference is only in preference (awlawiyyah). The reasoning is that the prayer is performed by indicating toward the Kaaba, and the back posture achieves this more precisely.

Key Terms
استلقى (istalqa): Lying on one's back with face upward.
مضطجع (mudtaji'): Lying on one's side.
هواء الكعبة (hawa' al-ka'bah): The airspace above and around the Kaaba; direction for qibla for those who cannot face the Kaaba directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is lying on the back (istilqa') preferred over lying on the side (idtija') for a sick person's prayer?
A) Because the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar explicitly commands it.
B) Because the indication points directly to the airspace of the Kaaba, fulfilling the qibla requirement more precisely.
C) Because lying on the side is only for those who cannot lie on their back.
D) Because Imam al-Shafi'i said so.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a sick person's prayer is valid whether lying on the back or side, but the back is preferred because its indication is directly toward the Kaaba.

Indication in Prayer for the Severely Ill: Delay vs. Substitution
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether eye/heart indication can replace head indication for the sick.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person unable to indicate with the head and explain why Zufar's counter-argument based on qiyas is rejected.

Core Idea
Head indication is irreplaceable; without it, prayer delays—substitution by qiyas is invalid.

When a sick person cannot even gesture with the head during prayer, what should they do? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, insists on delaying the prayer until head indication is possible. Imam Zufar, a prominent Hanafi, disagrees and allows indication with eyes or heart based on analogy (qiyas). In this lesson, we will examine the reasoning behind the majority Hanafi position and the rebuttal to Zufar's argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Exceptions
First, note that the base ruling is: if a sick person can indicate with the head, they do so. But if they cannot, the prayer is delayed (yu'akhkhar). No other body part can substitute.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the Disagreement
Imam Zufar holds that when head indication is impossible, the person may indicate with eyes, eyebrows, or even the heart. This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Al-Shafi'i also holds a similar view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
The Hanafi proof is based on a hadith that only mentions head indication (omission implies exclusion) and the principle that substitutes cannot be appointed by personal opinion (ra'y). The head is a pillar (rukn) of prostration; eyes are not analogous.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Examine Zufar's Qiyas Argument
Zufar reasons by qiyas: just as head indication substitutes for actual ruku' and sujud, so can other body parts when the head is incapacitated. The Hanafi response: qiyas on the head fails because the head is specifically designated and is the site of the rukn.
Shafi'is accept this qiyas, making it a cross-madhhab difference.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis delay the prayer (qada later); Shafi'is (and Zufar) pray immediately with eye indication, no qada. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
If the patient recovers, they must make up delayed prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يستطع الايماء براسه اخرت عنه ولا يؤمى بعينه ولا بقلبه ولا بحاجبيه خلافا لزفر لما روينا من قبل ولان نصب الابدال بالرأى ممتنع ولا قياس على الرأس لانه يؤدى به ركن الصلوة دون العين واختيها وفي اخرت عنه اشارة الى انه لا تسقط الصلوة عنه وان كان العجز اكثر من يوم ليلة اذا كان مفيقا وهو الصحيح لانه يفهم مضمون الخطاب بخلاف المغمى عليه
ترجمہ پھر اگر مریض اپنے سر سے بھی اشارہ کی قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو تو اس سے نماز کو مؤخر کر دیا جائے گا اور اشارہ نہیں کرے گا اپنی آنکھی سے اور نہ اپنے دل سے اور نہ اپنی بھنوں سے امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم پہلے دوایت کر چکے ہیں اور اس وجہ کہ بدل کا رائے سے مقرر کرنا منع ہے اور سر پر قیاس نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ سر کے ساتھ نماز کا ایک رکن ادا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ آنکھ اور اس اختین (بھنووں اور قلب ) سے اور امام قدوری کا قول اخرت عنہ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اس سے نماز ساقط نہ ہوگی اور اگر چہ والی دن رات سے زائد ہو بشرطیکہ وہ شخص افاقہ میں ہو۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ مریض مضمون خطاب کو سمجھتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف وہ شخص جو ایک دن رات سے زائد بے ہوش رہا تو چونکہ وہ فہم خطاب سے عاجز ہے اس لئے نماز اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
If he cannot indicate with his head, (the prayer) is delayed for him, and he does not indicate with his eye, nor with his heart, nor with his eyebrows, contrary to Zufar, due to what we narrated before, and because appointing substitutes by opinion is prohibited, and qiyas on the head is not valid, because a pillar of prayer is performed with the head, not with the eye and its sisters. And the saying of al-Quduri 'it is delayed for him' is an indication that prayer is not dropped from him, even if the inability is more than a day and night, as long as he is conscious—this is correct, because he understands the content of the address, contrary to the unconscious one.
Translation: Then if the patient does not have the ability to indicate even with his head, then the prayer is delayed for him, and he does not indicate with his eyes, nor with his heart, nor with his eyebrows. Imam Zufar differs, due to the hadith we narrated before, and because appointing a substitute by opinion is prohibited, and qiyas on the head is not valid, because a pillar of prayer is performed with the head, not with the eye and its sisters (eyebrows and heart). And al-Quduri's statement 'it is delayed for him' indicates that prayer is not dropped from him, even if the inability exceeds a day and night, provided he is conscious. This is correct because this patient understands the content of the address. Contrary to the one who remains unconscious for more than a day and night, since he is unable to understand the address, prayer is dropped from him.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a sick person who cannot even indicate with his head. The Hanafi position, following Abu Hanifa, is that such a person must delay the prayer until he regains the ability to indicate with his head. He cannot substitute with eye movements, heart intention, or eyebrow movements, contrary to Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i. The proof is that the head is the bodily part with which the pillar (rukn) of prostration is performed, and substituting it with other parts by personal reasoning (ra'y) is not allowed. Additionally, the hadith only mentions head indication, not others. The prayer is not dropped even if the inability lasts more than a day and night, as long as the person is conscious and understands the obligation. However, if the person becomes unconscious for more than a day and night, the prayer is dropped due to inability to understand the address. The commentator clarifies that this is the correct view (sahih). The practical consequence is that such a sick person must make up the missed prayers upon recovery, unless unconscious for an extended period.

Key Terms
ايماء (ima'): Indication (gesture) with the head to replace bowing and prostration.
بدل (badal): Substitute; in this context, the indication is a substitute for the actual physical actions of ruku' and sujud.
ركن الصلوة (rukn al-salah): Pillar of prayer; here specifically referring to sujud (prostration) which involves the head touching the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (majority view), what must a sick person do if he cannot even indicate with his head during prayer?
A) He should indicate with his eyes and heart.
B) He should delay the prayer until he is able to indicate with his head.
C) He should pray with his heart alone.
D) The prayer is dropped from him entirely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely holds that head indication is irreplaceable; if unavailable, the prayer is delayed, not substituted by other body parts.
