Ruling for Patient Unable to Signal with Head: Hanafi Position and Dispute with Zufar/Shafi'i
Dispute on signaling with eyes in extreme illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a patient who cannot signal with the head and evaluate the opposing view of Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Only head signaling suffices; eyes and eyebrows are not substitutes for prayer.

This passage from al-Quduri's commentary presents the Hanafi position on an extreme case: a patient so ill that even nodding the head is impossible. The prayer is not dropped but deferred, and must be made up if the patient recovers consciousness. Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, allowing signaling with the eyes and requiring repetition. We will examine the textual and rational proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what al-Quduri rules: the prayer is deferred, not performed with eyes/eyebrows, and must be made up later if the patient recovers and was conscious.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the patient should signal with eyes/eyebrows and repeat the prayer upon recovery.
This is an inter-madhhab dispute with a minority Hanafi view.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
Understand the opponent's qiyas: just as head signaling substitutes for bowing/prostration, so should eye signaling by analogy.
Analogy is the core of the opposing argument.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Two arguments: (a) Textual: the hadith only mentions head, omitting other body parts shows non-permissibility. (b) Rational: a substitute (badal) cannot be determined by personal opinion; the head is directly involved in prostration, eyes are not, so analogy fails.
The difference in involvement in the actual pillar (rukn) breaks the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi says patient must wait and make up later; Shafi'i says pray immediately with eyes and repeat later.
Both require repetition, but Hanafi defers prayer, Shafi'i performs it immediately with eye signals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ مرض اگر اس قدر بڑھ گیا کہ سر کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنے کی قدرت بھی باقی نہ رہی ہو تو نماز موخر کر دی جائے گی لیکن آنکھوں، قلب اور بھنوؤں کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ امام زفر کہتے ہیں کہ ایسا مریض اپنی آنکھوں اور نب کے ساتھ اشارہ کر کے نماز ادا کرے اور تندرست ہونے پر اس کا اعادہ کر لے۔ اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی ان قدرت ان تسجد على الارض فاسجد والا قادم بر آسک اس حدیث کے اندر مقام بیان کے موقع پر سر پر اکتفاء کیا ہے۔ اگر سر کے علاوہ کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنا جزء ہوتا تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم اس کونہ در بیان فرماتے۔ آپ کا بیان نہ فرمان عدم جواز کی دلیل ہے۔
عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشارہ در حقیقت رکوع اور سجدہ کا بدل ہے اور بدل کا رائے سے مقرر کرنا ممنوع ہے اور حدیث کے اندر فقط سر کے ساتھ اشارہ کا ذکر ہے نہ کہ آنکھ وغیرہ کے ساتھ اشارہ کا۔ پس اگر ان چیزوں کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنے کی اجازت دے دی جائے تو بدل کا رائے سے مقرر کرنالازم آئے گا حالانکہ یہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے آنکھ وغیرہ کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر آپ یہ کہیں کہ رائے سے بدل کا مقرر کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو سر کے حکم پر قیاس کرنا ہے یعنی جس طرح سر کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنا رکوع اور سجدہ کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اسی طرح آنکھ وغیرہ کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنا بھی کافی ہونا چاہئے ۔ تو جواب یہ ہوگا کہ آنکھ وغیرہ کو سر پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ سر کے ساتھ نماز کا ایک رکن یعنی سجدہ ادا ہوتا ہے اور آنکھ قلب بھنووں کے ساتھ سجدہ ادا نہیں ہوتا یعنی ان تینوں اعضاء کو سجدہ کی لا گی میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ پس اس فرق کے ساتھ ایک کا دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا کیسے درست ہوسکتا ہے قدوری کی عبارت اخرت عنہ سے اس بات کی نشاندہی ہوتی ہے کہ ایسے مریض کے ذمہ سے نماز ساقط نہ ہو گی بلکہ نماز اس کے ذمہ باقی رہے گی صحت یاب ہونے پر فنا واجب ہوگی اگر چہ یہ حالت ایک دن رات سے زائد ہی ہو بشر طیکہ اس عرصہ میں مریض با ہوش رہا ہو۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ مریض جب افاقہ و ہوش میں ہے تو نماز کے حکم ادا کو سمجھتا ہے۔ اور جب حکم کو سمجھتا ہے تو اس پر حکم متوجہ ہے جس سے اس کے ذمہ ادا واجب ہو گئی مگر عذر کی وجہ سے بالفعل ادا سے مہلت دیدی گئی ہے یہاں تک کہ قدرت حاصل ہو اس کے برخلاف وہ شخص جو ایک دن رات سے زائد بے ہوش رہا تو چونکہ وہ فہم خطاب سے عاجز ہے اس لئے نماز اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ بیماری کی یہ حالت کہ جس میں سر کے ساتھ اشارہ پر بھی قدرت نہ ہوا گر ایک دن رات سے زائد ہے تو اس پر قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی اور ایک دن رات سے کم ہے تو قضاء لا زم ہو جائے گی۔
Explanation: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: If the illness increases to the extent that one cannot even signal with the head, then prayer will be deferred. But signaling with the eyes, heart, and eyebrows is not sufficient. Imam Zufar says: Such a patient should perform prayer by signaling with his eyes and eyebrows, and repeat it when healthy. Imam al-Shafi'i holds this view. Our proof is the hadith that passed earlier: 'If you cannot prostrate on the ground, then...' [i.e., signal with head]. In that hadith, at the place of explanation, the head is deemed sufficient. If signaling with something other than the head were a substitute, the Prophet ﷺ would have mentioned it. His not mentioning it is evidence of non-permissibility. Rational proof: Signaling is in reality a substitute for bowing and prostration, and determining a substitute by opinion is prohibited. The hadith only mentions signaling with the head, not with the eyes etc. If permission were given for these, it would necessitate determining a substitute by opinion, which is not permissible. Therefore signaling with eyes etc. is not sufficient. If you say: This is not determining a substitute by opinion, but analogizing it to the ruling of the head—just as signaling with the head is sufficient for bowing and prostration, similarly signaling with eyes etc. should be sufficient—the answer is: Analogizing eyes etc. to the head is not correct because with the head a pillar of prayer, i.e., prostration, is performed, but with the eyes, heart, and eyebrows, prostration is not performed; these three limbs have no involvement in prostration. So with this difference, how can one analogize one to the other? Quduri's phrase 'deferred from him' indicates that prayer is not dropped from his responsibility; rather prayer remains due, and upon recovery, it becomes obligatory to make it up, even if this state exceeds one day and night, provided that the patient remained conscious during this period. This is the correct view because this patient, when conscious, understands the command to perform prayer. And when he understands the command, the command is directed at him, making it obligatory upon his responsibility, but due to the excuse, he is given respite until ability is regained. Contrary to the person who remains unconscious for more than a day and night: since he is incapable of understanding the address, prayer is dropped from his responsibility. Some scholars have said: If this state of illness, where one cannot even signal with the head, exceeds one day and night, then making it up is not obligatory; if it is less than one day and night, then making it up becomes incumbent.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a patient who cannot even signal with the head. It begins by stating the Hanafi position (from al-Quduri) that such a patient's prayer is deferred, and that signaling with the eyes, heart, or eyebrows is insufficient. Then it presents the opposing view of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who allow signaling with the eyes and eyebrows and require repetition upon recovery. The Hanafi evidence is both textual (the hadith limiting permission to head signaling) and rational (that a substitute cannot be determined by personal opinion, and analogizing eyes to head fails due to the lack of involvement of eyes in the actual pillar of prostration). The passage further clarifies that the prayer is not dropped; it remains a debt that must be made up if the patient regains health, as long as the patient was conscious. This is contrasted with a person unconscious for more than a day and night, for whom the prayer is dropped because of the inability to understand the address. The passage concludes by noting a minority view linking the obligation to make up to the duration of the condition.

Key Terms
اشارہ (isharah): Signaling with a body part to indicate bowing and prostration in prayer when physically unable.
بدل (badal): A substitute for an original act (e.g., signaling substitutes for actual bowing/prostration).
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a patient who cannot even signal with the head?
A) He should signal with his eyes and eyebrows, and repeat the prayer when healthy.
B) He must pray with head signaling only; if unable, prayer is deferred and must be made up if he recovers.
C) The prayer is entirely dropped and no make-up is required.
D) He may pray lying down without any signaling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that only head signaling is valid for prayer; if even that is impossible, prayer is deferred and must be made up, provided the patient remained conscious.

Ruling for a Patient Who Can Stand but Cannot Bow or Prostrate
Ruling: patient who can stand but cannot bow/prostrate should pray sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a patient who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, and explain the rational proof based on the instrumental nature of standing.

Core Idea
Standing is not a pillar if it cannot lead to prostration — the patient may sit and signal.

This lesson examines a specific situation: a patient who is physically able to stand but cannot perform the bowing and prostration postures. How does the Hanafi school rule? The answer hinges on understanding why standing is a pillar in the first place. Let's work through the proof.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
What does the Hanafi school say about a patient who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate?
The ruling: standing is not obligatory; the patient may pray sitting with signals.
2
Identify key concepts
Understand the terms ‘ruknīyah’ (pillarhood) and ‘tawassul’ (means). Standing is a pillar only as a means to perform prostration.
3
Analyze the proof
Why does standing lose its pillar status? Because if it cannot lead to prostration, the purpose is defeated, so it is no longer a pillar.
The proof is based on the effective cause (‘illa) of standing’s pillarhood.
4
Note the dispute
Imam Zufar (and al-Shafi‘i) argues that standing remains obligatory since it is a pillar and the patient is able. Understand the opposing evidence.
The Hanafi response refutes by emphasizing the conditional nature of standing's pillarhood.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the majority Hanafi view relied upon? The better practice is to sit, as it more closely resembles actual prostration.
This is the mufta bihi position.

قيام پر قادر ہو رکوع سجدہ پر قادر نہ ہو اس کے لئے کیا حکم ہے
ران قدر على القيام ولم يقدر على الركوع والسجود لم يلزمه القيام و يصلى قاعدا يومى الايماء لان ركنية القيام للتوسل به الى السجدة لما فيها من نهاية التعظيم فاذا كان لا يتعقبه السجود لا يكون ركنا فيتخير والافضل هو الايماء قاعدا الانه اشبه بالسجود
رجمہ اور اگر مریض کو قیام پر قدرت ہے اور رکوع اور سجود پر قدرت نہیں ہے تو اس پر قیام کرتا لازم نہ رہا۔ اور بیٹھ کر پڑھے درانحالیکہ اشارہ کرتا ہو اس لئے کہ قیام کا رکن ہونا اس غرض سے ہے کہ قیام کے وسیلہ سے سجدہ ادا ہو کیونکہ ایسے سجدہ میں انتہائی تعظیم ہے پس جب قیام ایسا ہو کہ اس کے بعد سجدہ نہ ہو تو قیام رکن نہیں رہے گا۔ اس لئے مریض کو اختیار ہے افضل تو بیٹھ کر اشارہ کرنا ہے کیونکہ بیٹھ کر اشارہ کرنا حقیقی سجدہ کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔

Ruling: He who can stand but cannot bow and prostrate: standing is not obligatory upon him, and he prays sitting, signaling with head, because the pillar-like nature of standing is for the purpose of reaching prostration due to the ultimate reverence in it. So when prostration does not follow it, it is not a pillar. So he has a choice, and the best is signaling while sitting because it is more similar to prostration.
Translation: If a patient has ability to stand but not to bow and prostrate, then standing is not obligatory upon him. He should pray sitting while signaling, because the pillar of standing is for the purpose that through standing prostration is performed, since in that prostration is ultimate reverence. So when standing is such that prostration does not follow it, standing will not be a pillar. Therefore the patient has a choice; the best is signaling while sitting because signaling while sitting is more similar to actual prostration.
Explanation: The issue is that if a person is so ill that he can stand but cannot bow and prostrate, then standing is not obligatory upon him. Rather he should pray sitting with signals. Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i said that if he can stand but cannot bow and prostrate, standing is not dropped from his responsibility. Their evidence: standing is a pillar and the patient is not incapable of it; he is incapable of another pillar, so why would standing be dropped? Our evidence: standing is only a pillar for the purpose of performing prostration, and it is a means to prostration because of the ultimate reverence in prostrating after standing. So when prostration does not follow it, standing is not a pillar. When it is not a pillar, the praying person has a choice; but the best is to signal for bowing and prostration while sitting because it is more similar to actual prostration, since when sitting, the head is closer to the ground than when standing.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof (and an implicit intra-Hanafi dispute). The ruling: a patient who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate is not required to stand; instead he prays sitting and signals with his head. The author gives the rational proof: the status of standing as a pillar (rukn) is only to enable prostration, which is the ultimate act of reverence. If standing cannot lead to prostration, it loses its ru'lence. Hence the patient has the option to stand or sit, but it is better to sit because sitting makes the head closer to the ground, more resembling actual prostration. The passage also mentions the opposing view of Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who argue that since standing is a pillar and the patient is able to perform it, it should not be dropped. The Hanafi response refutes this by explaining that the pillar nature of standing is conditional on its leading to prostration. The reliable Hanafi position is thus that standing is not obligatory in this case.

Key Terms
رکنیت (ruknīyah): The quality of being a pillar (rukn) of prayer, essential for validity.
توسل (tawassul): Means or intermediary; here standing is a means to reach prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the best posture for a patient who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate?
A) Standing and signaling with head
B) Sitting and signaling with head
C) Lying down and signaling with eyes
D) Standing without any bowing or prostration

Key Takeaway
Standing is not an absolute pillar; it is instrumental to prostration, and when prostration is impossible, the obligation to stand is lifted, with sitting being the better practice.

Completing Prayer When Illness Strikes Mid-Prayer
Ruling about completing prayer when a healthy person falls ill mid-prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a healthy person who becomes unable to stand during prayer may complete it in a lower posture (sitting or lying) and explain the proof based on the principle of building the lesser upon the greater.

Core Idea
If you fall ill during prayer, complete it in the best posture possible; starting standing doesn't lock you in.

Imagine you begin your prayer standing, healthy, and midway a sudden illness prevents you from standing. Does your prayer break? According to the Hanafi school, you may continue in the best posture you can manage. This lesson explores the ruling and its proof, based on the principle of 'building the lesser upon the greater' (binā' al-adnā 'alā al-a'lā) and analogy to following an imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage describes three levels of incapacity: unable to stand but able to bow and prostrate (sit and perform ruku/sujud), unable to bow/prostrate (sit and signal), and unable to sit (lie on back and signal). Recognize the progression.
The person does not restart the prayer; they continue from where they left off.
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For each case, state the required posture and actions. The key is that the prayer remains valid (sahih) as long as the person performs the actions to the best of their ability.
This is leniency from Allah, not a compromise of the prayer's validity.
3
Understand the proof: analogy to following an imam
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the permissibility of a sitting person following a standing imam. If that is allowed, then it is even more appropriate to build one's own prayer upon the earlier standing part.
The effective cause (illah) is the principle of building the lesser upon the greater.
4
Reflect on the principle of binā' al-adnā 'alā al-a'lā
This principle is a legal maxim that allows a lower-status action to be built upon a higher-status preceding action when there is a valid excuse. It is not limited to this case but applies across fiqh.
It shows the Hanafi school's flexibility in accommodating genuine hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تندرست نے نماز کھڑے ہو کر شروع کی پھر مرض لاحق ہو گیا بیٹھ کر مکمل کرے
وان صلى الصحيح بعض صلوته قائما ثم حدث به مرض اتمها قاعدا يركع ويسجدا يؤمى ان لم يقدرار مستلقيا ان لم يقدر لانه بنى الادنى على الاعلى فصار کا لاقتداء
ترجمہ اور اگر تندرست آدمی نے نماز کا کچھ حصہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھا پس اس کو مرض حادث ہو گیا تو بیٹھ کر نماز کو پورا کرے درانحالیکہ رکوع اور سجدہ کرے یا اشارہ کرے اگر ( رکوع سجدہ پر ) قادر نہ ہو یا لیٹ کر ( نماز پوری کرے) اگر ( بیٹھنے پر قادر نہ ہو کیونکہ اس نے اورنی کو اعلی پر مبنی کیا ہے لہذا اقتداء کے مانند ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تندرست آدمی نے نماز کا ایک حصہ کھڑے ہو کر ادا کیا پھر درمیان نماز ایسا مرض لاحق ہو گیا کہ قیام پرتقان نہ رہا تو اگر رکوع سجدہ پر قدرت ہو تو بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پوری کرے اور اگر رکوع سجدہ پر قدرت نہ ہو تو رکوع سجدہ کا اشار کرے اور نماز پوری کرے اور اگر اس قدر مریض ہو گیا کہ بیٹھنے پر بھی قدرت نہ رہی تو چت لیٹ کر نماز پوری کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں ادنی کی بناء اعلی پر کی گئی ہے اور ادنی کی بناء اعلیٰ پر کرنا جائز ہے جیسے کہ ادنیٰ حال والے کا اعلیٰ حال والے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے یعنی جس طرح بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے والے کا کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء جائز ہے اسی طرح خود اپنے حق میں یہ بات جائے ہے کہ نماز کا اول حصہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھے پھر عذر کی وجہ سے بعد کا حصہ بیٹھ کر پڑھے۔
If a healthy person prays part of his prayer standing, then illness occurs, he completes it sitting, bowing and prostrating, or signaling if unable, or lying on back if unable, because he built the lower upon the higher, so it became like following (an imam).
Translation: And if a healthy person performed some part of his prayer standing, then illness befell him, he completes it sitting, bowing and prostrating, or signaling if unable to bow and prostrate, or lying on back if unable to sit, because he built the lesser upon the greater, so it became like following (an imam). Explanation: The issue is that if a healthy person performed a part of his prayer standing, then in the middle of the prayer such illness occurred that he could no longer stand, then if he has ability to bow and prostrate, he completes the prayer sitting with bowing and prostration. If he cannot bow and prostrate, he signals for them and completes the prayer. If he becomes so ill that he cannot even sit, he lies on his back and completes the prayer. The proof: In all these three cases, the lesser is built upon the greater, and building the lesser upon the greater is permissible, just as it is permissible for a person in a lesser state to follow (i'tida') a person in a greater state. For example, it is permissible for one praying sitting to follow one praying standing. Similarly, in one's own prayer, it is permissible to pray the first part standing and then, due to an excuse, the later part sitting.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof about a healthy person who falls ill during prayer. The ruling: the person completes the prayer in the best posture possible: sitting with bowing/prostration if able, sitting with signals if unable to bow/prostrate, or lying on back if unable to sit. The proof is based on the principle of 'building the lesser upon the greater' (بنی الادنى على الاعلى). This is analogized to the permissibility of a person in a lower state (sitting) following an imam in a higher state (standing). Similarly, within one's own prayer, beginning in a higher state (standing) and continuing in a lower state (sitting) due to a valid excuse is allowed. The passage does not present any dispute, indicating this is the settled Hanafi position.

Key Terms
بناء الادنى على الاعلى (binā' al-adnā 'alā al-a'lā): Building the lesser upon the greater: performing a lower-status action based on a higher-status preceding action, permissible when needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts prayer standing and then becomes unable to stand, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Restart the prayer from the beginning in a sitting position
B) Continue from where he left off, sitting and bowing/prostrating if able
C) Abandon the prayer and make it up later
D) Stand as long as possible then stop

Key Takeaway
A prayer begun standing is not invalidated by mid-prayer illness; one continues in the best achievable posture, based on building the lesser upon the greater.

intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Sick Person Who Can Stand but Cannot Bow or Prostrate
Ruling with dispute: standing obligation drops when unable to prostrate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether standing (qiyam) is obligatory for a sick person who can stand but cannot bow/prostrate, and explain the Hanafi proof based on the purpose of qiyam.

Core Idea
Qiyam is a pillar only as a means to sajdah; if sajdah is impossible, qiyam's obligation drops.

This lesson examines a dispute about the obligation of standing (qiyam) for a sick person who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate. The Hanafi school holds that qiyam is not obligatory in such a case because its purpose is to facilitate prostration. Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, arguing that qiyam is an independent pillar. Understanding the basis of this dispute reveals how Hanafi usul uses purpose (maqsad) to determine the ruling of a pillar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The case is a sick person who can stand but cannot bow/prostrate. The Hanafi ruling: qiyam is not obligatory; he may pray sitting with gestures.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof (talil)
Qiyam is a rukn only for the sake of performing sajdah. If sajdah is impossible, qiyam loses its status as rukn.
The 'illah is the purpose of qiyam as a means to sajdah.
3
Examine the opposing view
Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i argue that qiyam is an independent rukn; inability for another rukn does not drop it.
Their proof: qiyam is a separate pillar, and the patient is capable of it.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response is that qiyam only has pillar status because it leads to prostration; without prostration, the means has no purpose.
This is based on istihsan and the maqsad of qiyam.
5
Apply the ruling: what should the sick person do?
He has a choice to stand or sit, but the better (afdal) is to sit and gesture because it resembles actual prostration more closely.
Sitting and gesturing brings the head closer to the ground.

باب صلوة المريض اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم اشارہ کرتا ہو اس لئے کہ قیام کا رکن ہونا اس غرض سے ہے کہ قیام کے وسیلہ سے سجدہ ادا ہو کیونکہ ایسے سجدہ میں انتہائی تعظیم ہے پس جب قیام ایسا ہو کہ اس کے بعد سجدہ نہ ہو تو قیام رکن نہیں رہے گا۔ اس لئے مریض کو اختیار ہے افضل تو بیٹھ کر اشارہ کرنا ہے کیونکہ بیٹھ کر اشارہ کرنا حقیقی سجدہ کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص ایسا بیمار ہے کہ وہ قیام پر تو قادر ہے لیکن رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے پر قدرت نہیں ہے تو اس پر قیام لازم نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ وہ بیٹھ کر اشارہ کے ساتھ نماز ادا کرے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اگر قیام پر قدرت ہو اور رکوع اور سجود پر قدرت ہو تو قیام اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط نہ ہو گا ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیام رکن ہے اور مریض اس سے عاجز نہیں ہے بلکہ دوسرے رکن یعنی رکوع اور سجدہ سے عاجز ہے پس رکوع اور سجدہ سے عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے قیام کیونکر ساقط ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیام فقط اس غرض سے رکن ہے کہ وہ ادائے سجدہ کا وسیلہ ہوتا ہے اور قیام ادائے سجدہ کا وسیلہ اس لئے ہے کہ قیام کے بعد سجدہ کرنے میں انتہائی تعظیم ہے پس جب قیام کے بعد سجدہ نہ ہو وہ قیام رکن نہیں ہوگا اور جب اس حالت میں قیام رکن نہ رہا تو بیمار مصلی کو قیام کرنے اور نہ کرنے میں اختیار ہے البتہ افضل یہ ہے کہ بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے کیونکہ بیٹھ کر سجدہ کا اشارہ کرنا حقیقی سجدہ کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے اس لئے کہ بیٹھ کر اشارہ کرتے وقت سرزمین سے زیادہ قریب ہو جائے گا بہ نسبت کھڑے ہو کر اشارہ کرنے کے۔
Chapter of the prayer of the sick. The commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah (Urdu) indicates that standing is a pillar for the purpose that prostration is performed through it, because in such prostration there is extreme reverence. So when standing is such that prostration does not follow it, then standing will not remain a pillar. Therefore, the sick person has a choice; the better is to sit and gesture, because sitting and gesturing is more similar to actual prostration. Explanation: The ruling is that if a person is so ill that he is able to stand but unable to bow and prostrate, then standing is not obligatory upon him. Rather, he should pray sitting with gestures. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i said: If he is able to stand and able to bow and prostrate, then standing is not dropped from his responsibility. Their proof is that standing is a pillar and the sick person is not incapable of it; rather, he is incapable of another pillar, namely bowing and prostrating. So how can standing be dropped due to incapacity for bowing and prostration? Our proof is that standing is a pillar only for the purpose that it is a means to perform prostration, and standing is a means for prostration because there is extreme reverence in prostrating after standing. So when there is no prostration after standing, that standing will not be a pillar. And when in this state standing is no longer a pillar, the sick worshipper has a choice to stand or not. Nevertheless, the better is to sit and gesture for bowing and prostration, because sitting and gesturing for prostration is more similar to actual prostration, because when sitting and gesturing, one comes closer to the ground compared to gesturing while standing.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the case of a sick person who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate. The author first establishes the general principle: standing is a pillar (rukn) in prayer only for the sake of prostration, because prostration after standing achieves a greater degree of reverence. Therefore, if prostration is impossible, the purpose of standing is nullified, and it ceases to be a pillar. Consequently, such a patient is not required to stand; he may sit and perform his prayer by gestures (ima'). A dispute is then presented: Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that since the patient is capable of standing, it remains obligatory because it is an independent pillar. Their dalil is that inability for one pillar does not remove another. The Hanafi response (the author's position) is based on the 'illah (effective cause) of qiyam's pillar status: it is a means, not an end. Since the end (sajdah) is absent, the means loses its ruling. The text also clarifies that although standing is not obligatory, the patient may choose to stand if he wishes; however, the preferred (afdal) method is to sit and gesture, because this more closely resembles actual prostration, bringing the head closer to the ground. This ruling is a concession (rukhsah) based on istihsan.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing in prayer; a pillar (rukn) normally required for salah.
رکن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer; omission invalidates the prayer unless compensated by sajdah sahw or repetition.
اشارہ (isharah): Gesture; to indicate bowing and prostration by lowering the head while sitting, used when one cannot physically perform the actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is standing (qiyam) not obligatory for a sick person who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate?
A) Because standing is a pillar only as a means to perform prostration; if prostration is impossible, standing loses its pillar status.
B) Because all pillars are waived for the sick regardless of ability.
C) Because bowing and prostrating are more important than standing.
D) Because the sick person may choose any position that is comfortable.

Key Takeaway
Qiyam's obligation drops when sajdah is impossible because its purpose is to facilitate prostration, not as an end in itself.

Building the Lower upon the Higher: Completing Prayer After Illness
Ruling with proof on completing prayer when illness occurs mid-prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la to cases where a worshipper's ability changes during prayer and state the Hanafi ruling on completing prayer in a lower posture.

Core Idea
A healthy person who becomes ill during prayer may complete it sitting or lying down because the lower is built upon the higher, like following an imam.

In this lesson, we examine a common scenario: a person begins prayer standing (the higher state) but falls ill mid-prayer and can no longer stand. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle of bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la. You will learn not only what to do but also the legal reasoning behind it, which extends to other acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three possible postures
The passage describes a person who starts prayer standing (healthy) and then becomes ill mid-prayer. There are three outcomes: sitting with ruku/sujud, sitting with gesture, or lying on back. Identify which case applies based on ability.
The key is the progression: standing → sitting → lying, depending on the degree of inability.
2
State the ruling for each posture
For each case, the ruling is that the prayer is completed in the lesser posture without breaking and restarting. The prayer remains valid (sahih).
No compensation is required because the lower state is built upon the higher by analogy.
3
Identify the proof: the principle of bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la
The text states the ruling is based on 'building the lower upon the higher'. This principle is not from a direct text but from qiyas (analogy). Understand that the higher state (standing) is considered the foundation, and the lower state (sitting/lying) is added later due to excuse.
This is a rational proof accepted in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the qiyas: analogy to following an imam
The proof is analogized to a person in a lower state (sitting) following a standing imam in congregational prayer. Just as that is permissible, it is permissible for one's own prayer to have a higher part followed by a lower part.
The illa (effective cause) is the excuse that necessitates the lower state.
5
Understand the illa and the scope of the ruling
The illa is the occurrence of a genuine excuse (illness) that prevents continuation in the higher state. The ruling applies to obligatory and voluntary prayers. If the excuse is self-inflicted or deliberate, the ruling may differ.
This principle also applies to other acts like fasting or hajj if partial ability changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان صلى الصحيح بعض صلوته قائما ثم حدث به مرض اتمها قاعدا يركع ويسجد او يومئ ان لم يقدر او مستلقيا ان لم يقدر لانه بنى الادنى على الاعلى فصار كالاقتداء ترجمہ اور اگر تندرست آدمی نے نماز کا کچھ حصہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھا پس اس کو مرض حادث ہو گیا تو بیٹھ کر نماز کو پورا کرے درانحالیکہ رکوع اور سجدہ کرے یا اشارہ کرے اگر رکوع سجدہ پر قادر نہ ہو یا لیٹ کر نماز پوری کرے اگر بیٹھنے پر قادر نہ ہو کیونکہ اس نے ادنی کو اعلی پر مبنی کیا ہے لہذا اقتداء کے مانند ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تندرست آدمی نے نماز کا ایک حصہ کھڑے ہو کر ادا کیا پھر درمیان نماز ایسا مرض لاحق ہو گیا کہ قیام پر قادر نہ رہا تو اگر رکوع سجدہ پر قدرت ہو تو بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پوری کرے اور اگر رکوع سجدہ پر قدرت نہ ہو تو رکوع سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے اور نماز پوری کرے اور اگر اس قدر مریض ہو گیا کہ بیٹھنے پر بھی قدرت نہ رہی تو چت لیٹ کر نماز پوری کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں ادنی کی بناء اعلی پر کی گئی ہے اور ادنی کی بناء اعلیٰ پر کرنا جائز ہے جیسے کہ ادنیٰ حال والے کا اعلیٰ حال والے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے یعنی جس طرح بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے والے کا کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء جائز ہے اسی طرح خود اپنے حق میں یہ بات جائز ہے کہ نماز کا اول حصہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھے پھر عذر کی وجہ سے بعد کا حصہ بیٹھ کر پڑھے۔
And if a healthy person prayed part of his prayer standing, then an illness occurred to him, he completes it sitting, bowing and prostrating, or gestures if he is unable, or lying on his back if he is unable, because he built the lower upon the higher, so it becomes like following (iqtida). Translation: And if a healthy person prayed some portion of prayer standing, then an illness occurred to him, he completes the prayer sitting while bowing and prostrating, or gestures if unable, or lying down if unable, because he has based the lower upon the higher, so it becomes like following. Explanation: The ruling is that if a healthy person performed part of the prayer standing, then in the middle of the prayer an illness occurred such that he cannot continue standing, then if he is able to bow and prostrate, he should complete the prayer sitting with bowing and prostration. If he is unable to bow and prostrate, he should gesture. If he becomes so ill that he cannot sit either, he should complete the prayer lying on his back. The proof is that in all three cases, the lower state is built upon the higher, and building the lower upon the higher is permissible, just as it is permissible for a person in a lower state to follow a person in a higher state in congregation. Just as a person praying sitting can follow a person praying standing, similarly in one's own prayer, it is permissible to pray the first part standing and later part sitting due to excuse.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling when a person who is healthy at the beginning of prayer becomes ill during it. The ruling is that such a person should complete the prayer in the best possible posture given his new condition. If he can sit and perform ruku and sujud, he should do so. If he cannot bow/prostrate, he gestures. If he cannot sit, he lies on his back. The proof is based on the principle of 'building the lower upon the higher' (bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la). This principle is justified by analogy (qiyas) to the permissibility of a person in a lower state (e.g., sitting) following a leader in a higher state (standing) in congregational prayer. Similarly, in an individual prayer, the earlier standing portion is 'higher' and the later sitting portion is 'lower', but it is valid to complete the prayer in the lower state because the excuse arose after the higher portion was performed. The proof is not from a specific text but from this rational analogy which is accepted in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
بناء الأدنى على الأعلى (bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la): The legal principle that permits a person to complete an act of worship in a lower state after having performed part of it in a higher state, by analogy to the permissibility of a follower in a lower state following an imam in a higher state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the ruling that a person who becomes ill during prayer may complete it sitting?
A) A direct command from the Quran.
B) The principle of building the lower upon the higher, analogized to following an imam.
C) Consensus of all companions.
D) The ruling only applies to voluntary prayers.

Key Takeaway
A prayer begun in a higher state (standing) is validly completed in a lower state (sitting/lying) when a genuine excuse arises, based on the Hanafi principle of bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la.

Building Prayer After Recovery: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building prayer after recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding building prayer upon recovery from illness and apply the underlying principle of iqtida to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
Building a standing prayer upon a sitting portion is allowed only if standing can follow sitting — an analogy to iqtida.

Imagine you are praying while sitting due to illness, and during the prayer you suddenly feel better and can stand. Should you continue from where you left off, or start over? This scenario produced a well-known dispute between the two senior Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The resolution depends not on the prayer itself, but on a prior disagreement about whether a standing person can follow a sitting imam in congregation (iqtida). This lesson unpacks that disagreement and its logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A person begins praying sitting (with actual ruku' and sujud) due to illness. During the prayer, he recovers and becomes able to stand. The question: can he continue his prayer standing, building upon the sitting portion?
The prayer was valid so far; the only issue is the change of posture.
2
State the Two Rulings
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) say he can build (bina') and complete standing. Imam Muhammad says he must start the prayer anew (istiqbal).
Both positions are from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Trace the Root Disagreement
The dispute is not about building directly, but about a prior issue: can a standing person (qaim) follow a sitting imam (qa'id) in congregational prayer?
The two shaykhs say yes; Muhammad says no.
4
Apply the Analogy
Building one's own prayer upon a sitting portion is analogous to following a sitting imam. If standing can follow sitting (as per the two shaykhs), then building is allowed. If not (as per Muhammad), building is disallowed.
The analogy is qiyas: asl = iqtida, far' = bina', illa = the combination of standing and sitting postures in one prayer.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The position of the two shaykhs (building is allowed) is the relied-upon view for fatwa, as it is the majority position and avoids unnecessary repetition.
This is the view adopted by later Hanafi manuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من صلى قاعدا يركع ويسجد لمرض ثم صح بنى على صلاته قائما عند ابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف و قال محمد استقبل بناء على اختلافهم في الاقتداء وقد تقدم بيانه اور جوشخص کسی مرض کی وجہ سے بیٹھ کر رکوع سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھتا ہے پھر تندرست ہو گیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اپنی نماز کڑے ہو کر بنا ء کرے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا از سرنو پڑھے ( یہ اختلاف ان کے اقتداء کے اندر اختلاف پر مبنی ہے اور اس کا بیان پہلے گذر ہے۔ تفریح صورت مسئلہ ایک شخص نے مرض کی وجہ سے رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ بیٹھ کر نماز کا ایک حصہ ادا کیا پھر نماز کے درمیان ہی درست ہو کر قیام پر قادر ہوگیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک کھڑے ہو کر اپنی نماز پر بنا کرے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک از سرنو نماز پڑھے۔ لام محمد اور شیخین کا اصل اختلاف اس بات میں ہے کہ قائم قاعد کے پیچھے اقتداء کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ قائم کا قاعد کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور شیخین نے فرمایا کہ جائز ہے پس چونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک قائم کا قاعد کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے تو بات قیام نماز کی بناء کرنا بحالت قعود نماز پر بھی نا جائز ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک قائم کا قاعد کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا چونکہ جائز ہے لہذا اپنے نفس میں بھی حالت قیام کی نماز کو حالت قعود کی نماز پر مبنی کرنا جائز ہوگا۔
Whoever prayed sitting, bowing and prostrating due to illness, then recovered, he builds upon his prayer standing according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: he starts anew, based on their disagreement regarding following (iqtida), and its explanation has preceded. And a person who prays sitting with bowing and prostrating due to illness, then recovers: according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), he should build upon his prayer standing; Imam Muhammad said: he should start anew. This difference is based on their difference regarding following: can a standing person follow a sitting person? Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible for a standing person to follow a sitting person, and the two shaykhs said it is permissible. Since according to Imam Muhammad it is not permissible, therefore building the standing prayer upon the sitting prayer is also not permissible. And according to the two shaykhs, since it is permissible for a standing person to follow a sitting person, therefore in one's own case, building the standing state upon the sitting state is also permissible.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sick person who begins praying sitting (with actual ruku and sujud) and then recovers during the prayer, becoming able to stand. The two positions are: (1) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that the person should build (bina') upon his earlier sitting prayer and complete it standing, i.e., continue from where he left off. (2) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that he must start the prayer anew (istiqbal). The key to this difference lies in their respective rulings on the permissibility of a standing person (qaim) following a sitting person (qa'id) in congregational prayer. The two shaykhs consider it permissible, while Imam Muhammad does not. Since building one's own prayer upon a previous portion is analogous to following (iqtida), the difference in the ruling on following leads directly to the difference in the ruling on building. The passage references that this very issue was discussed earlier in the text.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): The legal concept of continuing a prayer by building upon a valid preceding portion when the excuse preventing a higher posture is removed.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer. Here the key is whether a standing person can follow a sitting imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the intra-Hanafi dispute on building prayer after recovery from illness?
A) A difference in interpreting the Quranic verses on prayer.
B) A disagreement on whether a standing person can follow a sitting imam in congregation (iqtida).
C) A dispute over the validity of prayer performed while sitting.
D) A difference in calculating the number of rak'ats.

Key Takeaway
Building upon a sitting portion of prayer is allowed when the underlying act of following (iqtida) would be allowed, and this is the view of the two shaykhs, which is the mufta bihi.

Building Upon Gesture Prayer When Ability Returns
Ruling: no building when regaining ability from gestures, with Imam Zufar's exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building upon a prayer performed with gestures, explain the qiyas reasoning behind the majority view and Imam Zufar's exception, and apply the mufta bihi to determine the required action.

Core Idea
If you regain ability during gesture prayer, you cannot build—restart is mandatory by analogy to following a lower-state imam.

A person who starts praying with gestures (ima') due to inability may recover the ability to bow and prostrate mid-prayer. The Hanafi school's majority holds that the prayer must be started over, while Imam Zufar allows building. This lesson unpacks the qiyas reasoning and the intra-madhhab dispute, clarifying the operative ruling for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage describes a person who performs part of the prayer with gestures (because of inability) and then becomes able to bow and prostrate. The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that he must start the prayer anew. Note that the gestured portion itself is valid, but building upon it is not allowed.
2
Understand the qiyas to iqtida'
The ruling's basis is analogy (qiyas) to congregational prayer: it is not permissible for a person who can bow to follow (iqtida') an imam who gestures. The same prohibition applies to building (bina') in one's own prayer—since building is like following a previous state of oneself.
The illa (effective cause) is the difference in ability level: the earlier state (gestures) is considered lower, and the later state (full ability) is higher; building from a lower to a higher state is invalid.
3
Contrast Imam Zufar's view and his reasoning
Imam Zufar holds that building is permissible. He allows following a gesturing imam, so for him the analogy to iqtida' does not produce a prohibition. Therefore, in his view, one can continue the prayer by building upon the gestured portion.
Imam Zufar's position is a legitimate minority view within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the three imams: the prayer must be restarted. In practice, if someone recovers ability mid-prayer, they should stop, make intention, and begin anew.
This ruling applies to any case where one prays in a lower state (e.g., sitting due to illness) and later becomes able to perform the full movements.

ن صلى بعض صلوته بايماء ثم قدر على الركوع والسجود استأنف عندهم جميعا لانه لا يجوز اقتداء رائع بالمومى فكذا البناء جمہ اور اگر نماز کا ایک حصہ اشارے کے ساتھ ادا کیا پھر رکوع اور سجدہ پر قادر ہو گیا تو ائمہ ثلثہ کے نزدیک نماز از سر نو پڑھے۔ اس لئے کہ رکوع کرنے والے کا اشارہ کرنے والے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہی حال بناء کا ہے۔ یح مسئلہ ایک شخص نے عجز کی وجہ سے نماز کا ایک حصہ اشارے کے ساتھ ادا کیا پھر درمیان نماز رکوع اور سجدے پر قادر ہو گیا تو اسناد ( ابوحنیفہ صاحبین ) کے نزدیک از سر نو نماز پڑھے امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں بھی بنا ء کرنا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسناد کے نزدیک رکوع کرنے والے کا اشارہ کرنے والے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز ہے پس یہی حال بناء کا ہے۔
And if [a person] prayed part of his prayer with gestures, then was able to bow and prostrate, he starts anew according to all of them (the three imams), because it is not permissible for one who bows to follow one who gestures, and similarly for building. Explanation: If a person performed part of prayer with gestures due to inability, then in the middle of prayer became able to bow and prostrate, then according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) he must start the prayer anew. Because it is not permissible for a person who bows to follow a person who gestures. The same applies to building. Imam Zufar said: In this case too, building is permissible. The reason is that according to the three imams, it is not permissible for a person who bows to follow a person who gestures, and according to Imam Zufar it is permissible. So the same applies to building.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person performed some part of prayer with gestures (ima') due to inability to bow and prostrate, and then during the prayer regains the ability to perform actual ruku and sujud. The ruling, according to the three main imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), is that he must start the prayer over from the beginning; he cannot build upon the gestured portion. The reason is that building (bina') is analogous to following (iqtida'), and it is not permissible for a person who can perform actual ruku/sujud to follow a person who only gestures, because the person with full ability is in a higher state and the gesturer in a lower state. Following a lower state imam is not allowed. Therefore, building upon a lower state portion in one's own prayer is also not allowed. Imam Zufar, however, disagrees. He holds that building is permissible even in this case because he allows a person with full ability to follow a person who gestures in congregational prayer. This is a minority view within the Hanafi school, and the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that of the three imams: one must start anew.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gestures made with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration when a person is unable to perform the actual physical movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the analogy used by the three imams to prohibit building upon a prayed gestured portion?
A) Qiyas to forgetting a prostration.
B) Qiyas to the prohibition of following a gesturing imam.
C) Qiyas to the permissibility of cutting the prayer short.
D) Qiyas to the validity of gestures as full substitutes.

Key Takeaway
According to the three imams, building upon a prayer performed with gestures is not allowed; one must restart, by analogy to the prohibition of following a gesturing imam.

Permissibility of Leaning in Nafl Prayer
Ruling statement on permissible posture change in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on changing posture in nafl prayer due to an excuse and identify the conditions for its permissibility.

Core Idea
In nafl prayer, leaning or sitting due to fatigue is permissible — the excuse excuses the change.

This brief passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: if a person begins a nafl prayer standing but becomes tired mid-prayer, can they lean on something or sit? The answer illustrates the Hanafi principle that nafl prayers have greater flexibility than fard prayers, especially when an excuse ('udhr) arises. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish the different standards of obligation between obligatory and voluntary acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act in question is nafl prayer (tatawwu'), which is supererogatory. Recognise that the ruling applies specifically to voluntary worship, not obligatory (fard) prayer.
In Hanafi fiqh, nafl prayers have more flexibility; one may even break them without sin.
2
Locate the ruling from the text
The text explicitly states 'la ba'sa' (there is no harm) for leaning on a stick or wall, or sitting down. This indicates permissibility (ibahah).
The ruling is unconditional in the text but is linked to the presence of an excuse.
3
Identify the rationale (illah)
The reason given is 'li-anna hadha 'udhr' (because this is an excuse). The excuse of fatigue or hardship triggers the relaxation of the normal requirement to stand.
Without an excuse, the ruling may differ; the text does not cover that scenario.
4
Distinguish from fard prayer
The Hanafi school holds that in fard prayer, unnecessary changes in posture may invalidate the prayer or require sajdah al-sahw. The flexibility in nafl is a concession due to its voluntary nature.
This distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفل کھڑے ہو کر شروع کئے پھر ٹیک لگالی تو کیا حکم ہے افتتح التطوع قائما ثم اعنى لابأس ان يتوكاً على عصا او حائط او يقعد لان هذا عذر، وان كان الاقعاء
If he started a supererogatory prayer standing, then leaned (on something), what is the ruling? He began the nafl prayer standing, then became tired, there is no harm in his leaning on a stick or a wall, or sitting down, because this is an excuse, even if sitting down [..]
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses a short ruling regarding nafl (supererogatory) prayer. It asks: if a person starts a nafl prayer standing, then during the prayer becomes tired and leans on a stick or a wall, or even sits down, what is the ruling? The answer: there is no harm (la ba'sa) in doing so, because this is due to an excuse (udhr). The text implies that in nafl prayer, flexibility is allowed due to hardship. The phrase 'عذر' indicates that the reason for changing posture is acceptable. The mention of 'الاقعاء' (sitting on the heels or squatting) is likely part of the allowable sitting positions. The ruling distinguishes nafl from fard prayers, where such changes might require repetition or compensation. This is in line with the Hanafi view that nafl prayers can be performed with more ease, including breaking it without sin.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer, as opposed to fard (obligatory).
عذر ('udhr): A valid excuse that allows relaxation of the normal rules of prayer, such as fatigue or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person who started a nafl prayer standing becomes tired and leans on a wall?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is permissible because of the excuse.
C) It is makruh but valid.
D) He must break the prayer immediately.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, the presence of a valid excuse permits changing posture without harming the prayer's validity.

Leaning in Nafl Prayer Without Excuse
Ruling on leaning in nafl prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaning in nafl prayer without excuse and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Leaning in nafl prayer without excuse is disliked (makruh) due to bad manners, but Abu Hanifa differs, allowing it by analogy to sitting.

When performing nafl prayer, one may need to lean due to fatigue. But what if there is no excuse? The Hanafi school has a difference of opinion. This lesson examines the ruling and the reasoning behind the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
Identify the default ruling stated at the beginning: leaning without excuse is makruh because it is bad manners (su' al-adab).
2
Identify the ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees and considers it permissible, while the Sahibayn agree with the default ruling that it is makruh.
3
Follow the analogy
Understand the reasoning: The dispute hinges on the ruling for sitting without excuse. Abu Hanifa allows sitting without excuse, so leaning (a lesser deviation) is also allowed. The Sahibayn do not allow sitting, so they consider leaning makruh.
This is a qiyas argument: leaning is like sitting.
4
Examine the commentary's distinction
Read the commentary's explanation that the difference lies in the worshipper's choice at the start: one can choose to sit at the beginning, but not lean; hence leaning is more problematic.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position among later scholars is that leaning without excuse is makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بغير عذر يكره لانه اساءة فى الادب وقيل لايكره عند ابي حنيفة لانه لو قعده عنده يجوز من غير عذر فكذا لا يكره الاتكاء وعندهما يكره لانه لا يجوز القعود عندهما فيكره الاتكاء
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے نفل کو کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا پھر وہ تھک گیا تو اس بات میں کوئی حرج نہیں کہ وہ لاٹھی یا دیوار پر ٹک لگا۔ بیٹھ جائے کیونکہ یہ عذر ہے اور اگر ٹیک لگا نا بغیر عذر ہو تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ بے ادبی ہے اور کہا گیا کہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مکروہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک اگر بغیر عذر بیٹھ گیا تو جائز ہے اسی طرح ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک بیٹھنا نا جائز ہے پس ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح اگر کسی نے نفل نماز کھڑے ہو کر شروع کی پھر کسی چیز پر ٹیک لگائی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ ٹیک لگانا عذر کی وجہ سے ہو گا پانی عذر کے ہوگا اگر اول ہے تو مثلا تکان ہو گیا تو اس میں کوئی مضائنہ نہیں ہے اور اگر ثانی صورت ہے تو بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ باتقان احناف مکروہ ہے۔ وجہ کراہت یہ ہے کہ بلا عذر ٹیک لگانے میں سوئے ادب اور بے ادبی ہے۔ لیکن اس قول کی بنیاد پر امام ابو نیف طرف سے بلا عذر بیٹھنے اور بلا عذر ٹیک لگانے میں فرق بیان کرنا ضروری ہو گیا کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بلا عذر بیٹھنا غیر مکر ہے اور بلا عذر ٹیک لگانا مکروہ ہے سوجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ ابتداء کھڑے ہو کر نفل شروع کرنے میں اور بیٹھ کر شروع کرنے میں نفل پڑھنے والے اختیار ہے پس یہ اختیار انتہاء بھی بلا کراہت باقی رہے گا۔ البتہ اس کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ ابتداء نفل نماز ٹیک لگا کر پڑھے یا بغیر ٹیک لگائے پڑھے پس جب ابتدا ء یہ اختیار نہیں ہے تو انتہا نگی اختیار نہ ہوگا بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز کے درمیان اگر بغیر عذر کے ٹیک لگائی تو بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ دلیل ہے ہے کہ امام صاحبکے نزدیک بغیر عذر نفل نماز کے درمیان بیٹھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے لہذا ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بیٹھنا جو منافی قیام جب وہ مکروہ نہیں تو ٹیک لگانا جو قیام کے منافی بھی نہیں ہے وہ بدرجہ اولی مکروہ نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک بلا عذر ٹیک لگانا مکروہ ہے؟ اس کی یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک بلا عذر بیٹھنا مکروہ ہے لہذا ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ ہوگا۔
Without excuse, it is disliked (makruh) because it is bad manners. And it was said: it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa because if he sits without excuse it is permissible, so likewise leaning is not disliked. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is disliked because sitting is not permissible for them, so leaning is disliked. Translation: And the person who started a nafl prayer standing then became tired, there is no harm in him leaning on a stick or wall and sitting because this is an excuse. And if he leans without excuse, it is disliked because it is bad manners. And it was said that according to Abu Hanifa it is not disliked because according to him if he sits without excuse it is permissible, likewise leaning is not disliked. And according to the Sahibayn it is disliked because according to them sitting is not permissible, so leaning is also disliked. Commentary: If someone started a nafl prayer standing then leaned on something, there are two cases: leaning with an excuse or without. If the former (e.g., fatigue) there is no problem. If the latter, some mashayikh said it is makruh by consensus of Hanafis. The reason for karahah is that leaning without excuse involves bad manners (su' al-adab). But on the basis of this statement, it became necessary to distinguish between sitting without excuse and leaning without excuse according to Imam Abu Hanifa because according to him sitting without excuse is non-disliked (ghair makruh) while leaning without excuse is disliked. The reason for the difference is that the one praying has a choice in starting nafl standing or sitting, so this choice remains until the end without dislike. However, he does not have the choice to start nafl prayer leaning or not leaning. So since he has no choice at the beginning, he also has no choice at the end. Some mashayikh said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one leans without excuse during prayer, it is permissible without dislike. Their proof is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, sitting without excuse in the middle of nafl prayer is not disliked, so leaning is even more not disliked because sitting contradicts standing, but leaning does not contradict standing. According to the Sahibayn, leaning without excuse is disliked because sitting without excuse is disliked, so leaning is also disliked.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding leaning (itika') during a nafl prayer after having started standing, without a valid excuse. The basic ruling stated first is that it is makruh because it is a form of bad manners (su' al-adab). However, there is a difference of opinion: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not makruh, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), it is makruh. The reasoning is based on the ruling for sitting without excuse: Abu Hanifa considers sitting without excuse in nafl prayer permissible (though the text later notes there are two narrations from him), and since leaning is less oppositional to standing than sitting, it follows that leaning is also permissible. For the Sahibayn, since sitting is not permissible without excuse, leaning is also not permissible and is therefore makruh. The commentary further explains that according to some later scholars, the relied-upon position is that leaning without excuse is makruh even according to Abu Hanifa, but others maintain that it is permissible. The key distinction is that at the start, the worshipper has a choice between standing and sitting, so he may also change to sitting later without dislike; but he does not have a choice to start leaning, so at the end it remains non-optional. Thus, leaning without excuse is considered disliked because it is an innovation (bid'ah) in the prayer posture.

Key Terms
اتكاء (itika'): Leaning on something (e.g., a stick or wall) during prayer, which is a change in posture.
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse such as fatigue or illness that allows one to deviate from the standing posture in nafl prayer.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, which is optional but recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), what is the ruling on leaning (itika') during a nafl prayer without a valid excuse?
A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahab)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, leaning during nafl prayer without excuse is disliked (makruh) according to the majority view, but Imam Abu Hanifa allowed it by analogy to sitting.

Praying Sitting in a Moving Boat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on sitting prayer in a boat with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sitting in a moving boat, explain the Hanafi proof using the principle al-ghalib ka al-muhaqqaq, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A prevalent dizziness in a moving boat is treated as actual incapacity, making sitting permissible (Abu Hanifa) — but standing avoids doubt.

When you board a moving boat, you may feel dizzy if you stand. But what if you are perfectly fine? The Hanafi masters disagreed on whether you can pray sitting without an actual excuse. Imam Abu Hanifa ruled it permissible due to the dominant occurrence of dizziness, while his two disciples required standing. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each view and the preferred practice.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules for praying sitting in a moving boat without illness. Note that standing is still considered better (afdal).
Abu Hanifa: sitting is ja'iz (sufficient/valid).
2
2. Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: sitting is not sufficient except with an actual excuse. Recognize that this is also the view of the other three schools.
Sahibayn: ghaira ja'iz (invalid) without excuse.
3
3. Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn argue from the principle that one who is able to stand must do so; the possibility of dizziness does not override this obligation.
Dalil: complete ability to stand is present, so standing cannot be abandoned.
4
4. Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa uses the usul principle al-ghalib ka al-muhaqqaq (the dominant is like the certain) and draws an analogy (istihsan) to sleeping on one's side breaking wudu due to the dominant likelihood of wind.
The prevalent dizziness in a moving boat is treated as if it actually occurs, making the person virtually incapable of standing.
5
5. Determine thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the sitting prayer is valid; under the Sahibayn, it is not. The mufta bihi for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view, but standing is recommended to avoid disagreement, and exiting the boat is even better.
Tarjih based on the text's endorsement: 'هو الصحيح' regarding the moored/unmoored distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بن صلى فى السفينة قاعدا من غير علة اجزاه عند ابي حنيفة والقيام افضل و قالا لا يجزيه الا من عذر لان التام مقدور عليه فلا يترك وله ان الغالب فيها دوران الرأس وهو كالمتحقق الا ان القيام افضل لانه أبعد من شبهة الخلاف والخروج افضل ما امكنه لانه اسكن لقلبه والخلاف في غير المربوطة والمربوطة للشط هو الصحيح
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے بغیر کسی بیماری کے چلتی ہوئی کشتی میں بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھی تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور کھڑا ہونا افضل ہے اصالحین کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہوگی مگر عذر سے کیونکہ قیام پر اس کو قدرت حاصل ہے تو وہ ترک نہ کیا جائے گا اور امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ یک کشتی کے اندر بالعموم سر گھومتا ہے اور وہ تحقیق کے مانند ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ قیام افضل ہے اس لئے کہ وہ شبہ خلاف سے دور تر ہے اور جس قدر کن ہوکشتی سے باہر نکل آنا افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں اطمینان قلب ہے اور اختلاف بغیر بندھی ہوئی کشتی میں ہے اور بندھی ہوئی کشتی دریا کے کنارے کے مانند ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔
ریح صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ کشتی میں نماز پڑھنے والا قیام سے عاجز ہوگا یا عا جز نہیں ہوگا۔ اگر عاجز ہے تو بالا تفاق بیٹھ کر نماز سنا جائز ہے اور اگر قیام سے عاجز نہیں تو اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ کشتی ٹھہری ہوئی ہوگی یا چلتی ہوئی ہوگی اگر اول ہے تو بالا تفاق بیٹھ نماز پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر ثانی ہے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بغیر کسی بیماری کے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے لیکن کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنا کمل ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے یہی مذہب امام مالک، امام شافعی ، امام احمد کا ہے صاحبین کی نا یہ ہے کہ قیام پر اس کو قدرت حاصل ہے اور قدرت علی القیام کی صورت میں قیام کو ترک نہیں کیا جاتا۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی قیام کو ال نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چلتی ہوئی کشتی میں کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھنے سے بالعموم دوران رأس ( سر کا چکر ) ہو ہا ہے اور غالب بمنزلہ تحقیق کے ہوتا ہے مثلا کروٹ پر سونے کو حدث کہا گیا ہے کیونکہ اس حالت میں بالعموم اعضاء کے ڈھیلے پڑ جانے ہ سے ریح خارج ہو جاتی ہے پس غالب کو تحقیق کرے مرتبہ میں اتار کر نقض وضو کا حکم لگا دیا جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں دوران راس ناب احتمال کو تحقیق کے مرتبہ میں اتار کر یہ کہا گیا ہے کہ گویا یہ شخص قیام سے عاجز ہے اور جب قیام سے عاجز ہے تو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے ہوئی قباحت نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنا افضل ہے کیونکہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنا اختلاف کے شبہ سے ہے یعنی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے لیکن کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے کی صورت میں اختلاف کی زحمت سے نجات مل جائے سالہدایہ فرماتے ہے کہ اگر ممکن ہو تو نماز کے لئے کشتی سے باہر نکل آنا افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں ہر ایک کے قلب کو سب سے
Whoever prays sitting in a ship without cause, it is sufficient according to Abu Hanifa, and standing is better. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not sufficient except with an excuse, because complete ability to stand is within his power, so it should not be abandoned. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is the argument that generally dizziness of the head occurs in it, and it is like realization. Except that standing is better because it is farther from the doubt of disagreement, and going out (of the boat) is better if possible because it gives peace of heart. And the dispute is regarding an unmoored boat; a moored boat at the shore is like land - this is correct. Translation: And the person who prayed sitting in a moving boat without any illness, according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible, and standing is better. According to the Sahibayn it will not be permissible except with an excuse because he has the ability to stand, so it should not be abandoned. The proof of Imam Sahib is that generally in a boat the head spins, and that is like certainty. However, standing is better because it is farther from the doubt of disagreement, and as much as possible, coming out of the boat is better because it brings peace of heart. And the difference is in an unmoored boat; a moored boat is like the shore, that is correct. The author of al-`Inayah said: The one praying in a boat will either be incapable of standing or not. If incapable, by consensus sitting is permissible. If not incapable, there are two cases: stationary or moving. If stationary, by consensus sitting is not permissible. If moving, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible without illness, but standing is better. And the Sahibayn said that sitting without excuse is not permissible; this is also the school of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. The proof of the Sahibayn is that he has ability to stand, and with ability to stand, standing should not be abandoned. So in this case, standing should also not be left. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that in a moving boat, standing generally causes dizziness, and the predominant possibility is like certainty. For example, sleeping on the side is considered hadath because in that state the limbs generally loosen and wind escapes, so the predominant possibility is given the rank of certainty and the ruling of breaking wudu is applied. Similarly, here dizziness (dawaran al-ra's) downgrades the possibility to the rank of certainty, so it is said that this person is incapable of standing. And when he is incapable of standing, there is no harm in praying sitting. However, according to Imam Sahib as well, standing is better because standing avoids the doubt of disagreement (shubhat al-khilaf). The author of al-Hidayah says that if possible, coming out of the boat for prayer is better because it brings the most peace to the heart.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on praying sitting in a boat without a valid excuse, such as illness. The key factor is the motion of the boat. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the boat is moving, it is permissible to sit due to the prevalent dizziness (dawaran al-ra's), which is treated as a virtual excuse (ka al-muhaqqaq). The Sahibayn require standing because the person is physically able to stand; they consider the mere possibility of dizziness insufficient to abandon the obligatory posture of standing (in fard) or the required posture (in nafl with ability). The text further clarifies that if the boat is stationary (moored at the shore), it is like land, and sitting is not permissible without excuse by consensus. If the boat is moving, Abu Hanifa allows sitting even without an actual illness, but standing remains superior (afdal). The Sahibayn restrict sitting to cases of genuine excuse like sickness. The commentary from al-`Inayah and Hidayah emphasizes that the predominant occurrence of dizziness is equated to actual inability by way of istihsan (juristic preference), drawing an analogy to sleeping on one's side being considered a cause for wudu breakage due to the dominant likelihood of wind escaping. The preferred position is to stand if possible to avoid scholarly dispute, and exiting the boat to pray on land is even better.

Key Terms
دوران رأس (dawaran al-ra's): Dizziness of the head caused by the motion of a boat, prevalent in moving boats.
مربوطة (marbutah): A boat moored to the shore, considered like land (sahih al-tasarruf).
غالب (ghalib): Dominant occurrence, which in Hanafi usul is given the weight of certainty (ka al-muhaqqaq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa for praying sitting in a moving boat without a specific illness?
A) It is permissible, and standing is better
B) It is impermissible
C) It is permissible without any preference
D) It is obligatory to stand

Key Takeaway
In a moving boat, the prevalent dizziness justifies sitting per Abu Hanifa, but standing remains superior to avoid scholarly disagreement.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Sitting Prayer in a Moving Ship: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting prayer in a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on praying while sitting in a moving ship, articulate the Ṣāḥibayn's counterargument, and apply the principle al-ghālib ka al-muḥaqqaq to similar cases.

Core Idea
Predominant dizziness (غالب) is treated as certain (متحقق), making sitting permissible – but standing is still better to avoid disagreement.

You may have wondered: if you are on a moving ship, can you pray sitting down without an excuse? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it based on the predominant dizziness caused by the ship's motion, treating that prevalence as actual inability. However, his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree, insisting on standing unless the person truly cannot. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the principle behind Abu Hanifa's ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What exactly is being debated? The act is praying salah (presumably farḍ) while sitting in a moving ship without any physical excuse. The ruling depends on whether the person is considered able to stand or not.
Note: The debate does not apply to a moored ship, which is treated like land.
2
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that in a moving ship dizziness (دوران رأس) is predominant (غالب), and according to Hanafi uṣūl, the predominant is like the certain. Thus the person is legally unable to stand, making sitting permissible.
He uses qiyās khafī via istiḥsān, comparing to sleep nullifying wuḍū’.
3
Examine the Ṣāḥibayn's proof
They argue that the person has physical ability to stand (التام مقدور عليه), so standing is obligatory and cannot be abandoned. They do not accept the predominant as a sufficient excuse.
Their view is also held by Mālik, Shāfi‘ī, and Aḥmad.
4
Understand the tarjīḥ and practical difference
The author of al-Hidāyah deems Abu Hanifa's view correct (al-ṣaḥīḥ) and muftā bihī. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the prayer performed sitting is valid no repetition needed; under the Ṣāḥibayn, it must be repeated if no excuse existed.
All agree that standing is afḍal to avoid disagreement, and leaving the ship is best.
